# James Howlett  —  *Logan / Wolverine / Patch / Weapon X / Death*

![[_attachments/logan.png]]

# Logan — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# Executive Brief (BLUF)

## Bottom Line, Up Front

The subject is a chronically dissociative complex-trauma survivor whose body cannot die and whose mind has been overwritten — by violence, by handlers, and by his own protective amnesia — so many times that the question *who am I* has, for him, no stable referent. He has been alive and combatant for approximately 130 chronological years, presents physiologically as a man in his mid-forties, and has organized that long second life around a single load-bearing project: **the construction, by hand, of a containing structure for a self that was repeatedly broken open before it ever finished forming, by people who wanted a weapon.** The container is built out of four materials — a borrowed code of Bushidō; the protective mentorship of adolescent girls; ethanol; and geographic exile — and it works, barely. He knows it was not designed to hold and is not guaranteed to. That knowledge is the substrate beneath every behavior in the file.

He is not a berserker with a soft side. He is not a noble warrior with an anger problem. He is not an antisocial killer rehabilitated by love of team. He is a Şar-spectrum dissociative case — amnesia, depersonalization, identity confusion, identity alteration, and acute dissociative reactions ("berserker") collapsed into one syndrome with one etiology (chronic agentic violation across a developmental and adult lifespan) — co-presenting with Complex PTSD and a moderate-to-severe alcohol use disorder that is invisible to ordinary quantity criteria because his hepatic regeneration outpaces the dose. The whole picture is held together by a robust, *under-acknowledged* moral conscience and a small set of durable attachments without which he would have decompensated into something indistinguishable from the man the Weapon X program intended to manufacture.

## The Through-Line

A single recursive shape runs through every era of the record from 1880s Alberta to the Krakoan present:

**Catastrophic violence → identity dissolution → flight into wilderness or animality → tentative re-attachment to a vulnerable person or a code → loss of that person, often by his own hand or proximate cause → renewed dissolution.**

The shape is laid down in childhood at the Howlett estate (the social father killed by the biological father, the first claw-extrusion, the flight to the Yukon, the feral period with wolves) and is then *re-enacted* with industrial regularity for the next century and a quarter: Rose, impaled on the new claws; Itsu, murdered while pregnant; Mariko, poisoned and finally killed by his hand at her request; Jean Grey, lost twice; the X-Men of the *Old Man Logan* timeline, slaughtered by his own hand under Mysterio's illusion; the Krakoan deaths and resurrections that have made the cycle literally institutional. Across forty-plus years of publication and a dozen primary architects (Wein, Claremont, Miller, Hama, Windsor-Smith, Jenkins, Way, Millar, Aaron, Hickman), *the same three behavioral signatures recur*: amnesia and identity confusion, dissociative berserker episodes under threat-overload, and a compulsive protective-paternal attachment to adolescent girls. That cross-author consistency is not narrative drift; it is the etiological signature of the case.

## The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**The core wound is not Weapon X.** Weapon X is the most legible scar and the one the subject himself most often points to, but it is the *amplifier*, not the origin. The origin is the Howlett scene: in a single moment, the category "father" collapses (the man who raised him is not his blood; his blood-father has just killed his social father; the child's own body has just produced bone weapons he did not know it contained and used them to kill). Three foundational certainties — *who my father is*, *what my body is*, *what I am capable of doing to people I love* — are destroyed in the same instant. He flees the name "James Howlett" within hours and has never reliably returned to it. Every subsequent violation lands on already-broken ground.

**Weapon X is the wound's industrial-scale reproduction.** The Windsor-Smith record is unambiguous: he was conscious for portions of the adamantium bonding; the staff explicitly engineered dissociative states; he was used as a remote-piloted murder tool against animals and humans; he escaped naked into snow in a fugue. That procedure took the disorganized-attachment, identity-collapsed feral young man and *welded the trauma to his skeleton*. He now wears the instrument of his torture inside his body. Every claw extrusion lacerates the dorsal surface of his hand. **Pain is the literal prerequisite of his primary defensive act.** No other case file contains that fact. It is decisive.

**The maintenance machinery** — what keeps the wound active across thirteen decades when ordinary forgetting and ordinary mourning would have closed it — has four components:

1. **Iatrogenic memory corruption.** Weapon X, Team X, Romulus, the Hand/Hydra (*Enemy of the State*), Apocalypse's "Death" overwrite, the Persephone kill-triggers of the *Return of Wolverine* arc, and Krakoan resurrection protocols have *each independently* edited his autobiography. He cannot perform the normal trauma-integration work of testing memory against narrative because his memory is known-contaminated evidence. He treats his own past the way a careful investigator treats a hostile witness — and lives, accordingly, without the orienting function that intact autobiography provides.

2. **The healing factor as parasuicidal disinhibitor.** A century-plus of unkillable injury has conditioned him to a recklessness toward his own body that in any non-mutant would qualify as chronic parasuicidal behavior. The somatic feedback loop that teaches most humans to *stop* — pain followed by lasting damage — is, in him, pain followed by repair. He has learned that no injury is final, and behaves as if his body is expendable, which it is not psychologically even when it is physiologically.

3. **The sensorium.** Hyperacute olfaction, audition, and vision constitute an unremitting stimulus load he cannot voluntarily filter. He smells fear, arousal, illness, and lies on everyone around him at all times. The normal social-perceptual buffering that allows humans to occupy a room with strangers is anatomically denied him. **Hypervigilance, in his case, is partly imposed by anatomy.** Calm requires either solitude (wilderness), intoxication (the alcohol load), or controlled-stimulus environments (the dojo, the Danger Room, structured combat).

4. **The unkilled adversary.** Sabretooth's continued existence functions as a chronic destabilizer around which the subject has, over a century, *organized his identity*. The annual ritualized birthday attempt on his life is, perversely, the single most temporally stable relationship in the record. Removing Creed permanently would likely produce *more* destabilization than maintaining him — a paradox the subject himself probably grasps and never articulates.

## Who He Is at the Deepest Level

Beneath the animal-mask the subject has manufactured for himself ("the best there is at what I do, and what I do isn't very nice") sits a man whose behavior, examined across the full record without reference to his self-description, evidences a strong, almost rigid, internalized moral conscience: protection of the vulnerable as non-negotiable, loyalty to specific persons as absolute, a Bushidō-derived ethic of restraint and right action that he genuinely struggles to live by, and a sustained reparative parenting project (Kitty, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, X-23) that constitutes his most regulated and competent mode of functioning. **The animal-mask is a defense against the disappointment of the samurai-ideal.** He pre-rejects intimacy and high self-regard so that failure cannot land as catastrophe. The self-stigma is not symptom — it is *prophylaxis*.

The samurai-ideal itself — laid down at Jasmine Falls under Bando Saburo before the wars, returned to throughout the Mariko arc, invoked in the teaching of X-23 and Kitty — is the only positive identity-template he has ever willingly chosen. It is not native to him; it is borrowed, and he knows it is borrowed, which is part of why it functions: it is a *code* rather than a *self*, and codes survive identity-overwrites in a way that selves do not. When Weapon X, Romulus, Apocalypse, and the Hand have finished editing his autobiography, the Bushidō residue is still there because it was never stored as autobiography. It was stored as practice.

At the deepest level, then: he is a man who has lost the ability to know who he is from the inside, has compensated by adopting from the outside a code of who he *ought* to be, has spent over a century failing and partially succeeding at the code, and has built around the whole apparatus a fierce protective stance toward young people in his orbit — because the one thing he is certain of, having been the child to whom it was done, is that *what was done to him should not be done to anyone else*. That certainty is the bedrock under everything. It survives every overwrite.

## Operational Summary

**Reliable behaviors.** Will protect endangered children at any cost to self and at considerable cost to mission. Will keep his word to a named individual indefinitely. Will absorb extraordinary physical and informational punishment in service of a person or principle he has chosen. Will mentor effectively, patiently, and with unusual emotional precision when the protégé is adolescent, female, and traumatized in a way that resonates with his own history. Will function within team structures (X-Men, Alpha Flight, Quiet Council) provided the structure is person-anchored rather than institution-anchored. Will refuse orders from any handler not personally trusted.

**Predictable failure modes.** Decompensates under unstructured peace faster than under combat — sobriety, stillness, and idleness are aversive states he flees through alcohol, geographic exile, or self-prescribed mission. Cannot reliably moderate the high end of his affective range; once the berserker threshold is crossed (cued by smell of specific enemies, harm to a protected person, or threat-overload), consciousness narrows, behavior automatizes, and post-episode amnesia is partial-to-complete. Will idealize-then-withdraw from adult romantic partners because intimacy activates the Rose/Itsu/Mariko template and the load-bearing belief *she will die because of me*. Will not seek psychiatric care and will not narrate his interior; the file must be inferred behaviorally.

**Exploitable vectors (defensive awareness required).** Children in danger override tactical judgment and have been weaponized against him repeatedly (Hand, Mystique, Mojo). Credible claims that his memories are not his own destabilize him faster than physical injury and the healing factor cannot close that wound. The Rose/Mariko/Itsu pattern — beloved woman placed where he must kill her or watch her die — is the canonical psychological kill-shot and works every time it is attempted. Invocation of the samurai-ideal can recruit him to causes against his interest; confrontation with his failures against it can disable him.

**Containment requirements.** Person-anchored loyalty (a Xavier, a Rogers, a Kitty in the chain). Structured time, ideally pedagogical. Access to controlled-violence outlets (training, sanctioned mission). Tolerance, not policing, of the alcohol load — it is regulatory, and removing it without substitution will produce decompensation, not improvement. Tolerance of periodic geographic disappearance — the wilderness exile cycle is a self-administered de-escalation protocol and has prevented worse outcomes for a century. Access to Japan and to formal practice. Protection of the protégés in his orbit, because they are not only his patients in the reparative-parenting sense — they are also his treatment, and harm to them is the single most destabilizing event the file contemplates.

**Prognosis.** The container holds. It has held, against repeated and escalating assault, for a hundred and thirty years. It will likely continue to hold so long as the four maintenance conditions above are met and so long as at least one young person under his protection remains alive and reachable. Outside those conditions the prognosis darkens rapidly toward the *Old Man Logan* presentation — total behavioral inhibition, depressive shutdown, vow of nonviolence — which is not recovery but the inverse symptom of the same disorder: when the dissociative weapon-self becomes too contaminated to deploy, the conscious self goes catatonic to prevent its use. Both states are the disorder. Neither is the man.

**The single sentence.** He is the child who killed his father with bones he did not know he had, who has spent thirteen decades being made into a weapon by people who saw the bones and not the child, and who has built — from a borrowed code, a series of borrowed daughters, a borrowed liver's worth of whisky, and the borrowed wilderness — a place for the child to keep living inside the weapon.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

*Subject: LOGAN. Section I of a longitudinal dossier. Covers the period from birth (late 1880s) through the catastrophic night at the Howlett estate and the immediate aftermath of flight. Primary canonical substrate: Jenkins/Quesada/Kelly/Isanove, **Origin** #1–6 (Marvel, 2001–2002), with corroborative material from **Wolverine: The Origin** epilogue matter, **Wolverine** vol. 3 #36–40 ("Origins & Endings," Jenkins), and the **Wolverine: Origins** sequence (Way, 2006–2010) where it back-fills the Howlett-estate household. Where the published record is silent, gaps are flagged as such; nothing is invented.*

---

## 1.1 Birth, Lineage, and the Two Fathers

The subject is born **James Howlett**, on the Howlett estate outside Cold Lake, Alberta, in the late 1880s. The chronology is anchored backward from his apparent age at the *Origin* events (approximately twelve years old) and from the dated 1897 sequence that closes *Origin* #6. Place of birth is the main house of the estate — a substantial English-style manor sited in the boreal forest belt of north-central Alberta, lit by oil lamps and serviced by a domestic staff of indeterminate but visibly large size (cooks, grooms, gardeners, the gamekeeper Logan, the housekeeper Mrs. Brindle in some interpretations, and the orphan-girl servant Rose O'Hara, brought in as a companion for James after his elder brother's death).

The household, on the published evidence, contains:

- **John Howlett Sr.**, paterfamilias; aging, infirm in mind, kept upstairs and largely absent from the boy's daily life. His sole significant appearance is to die in the kitchen during the climactic intrusion of *Origin* #2.
- **John Howlett Jr.**, social father; landowner; emotionally remote, decent, ineffectual under pressure. He has already lost one son before James's birth — an event that has flooded the house with grief and rendered Elizabeth chronically unstable. He addresses James in the formal register of his class and station; he does not roughhouse with the boy, does not hunt with him, does not appear in any panel touching him with warmth.
- **Elizabeth Howlett**, mother; presented across *Origin* as bedridden, intermittently catatonic, periodically lucid in a brittle and frightened register. The death of the first son has functionally ended her parenting capacity. She does not nurse, soothe, or instruct James in any sequence depicted. She locks herself in her rooms; her primary recorded gesture toward James is recoil.
- **Thomas Logan**, the estate's groundskeeper; a coarse, drunken, ambulatorily violent man who lives in a cottage on the grounds with his son. He is, on the disclosure that drives *Origin* #2, **James's biological father** — the product of a liaison with Elizabeth that the household has either suppressed or accommodated by silence. He is dismissed from service shortly before the killing.
- **"Dog" Logan**, Thomas's acknowledged son; James's slightly elder playmate-by-proximity; a boy already malformed by his father's beatings and contempt. The household tolerates him on the grounds as a companion for James.
- **Rose O'Hara**, a red-haired Irish orphan, brought to the estate to serve as James's playmate-companion (the explicit framing is that the sickly heir requires *managed* socialization). She is approximately James's age. Her status is hybrid — neither domestic, nor family, nor governess — and that ambiguity will matter.

The *two-father* structure is the file's first and most consequential datum. The man James calls father is not his father. The man who is his father is the violent man who lives at the edge of the estate. The boy lives in the architectural and emotional space of the first while being, biologically, the property-by-blood of the second. The household maintains this fiction with such success that James himself does not know it until the catastrophe forces it into the open. Every later instance in which an authority figure turns out to have been *handling* him under false pretenses — the Professor at Weapon X, his Team X handlers, Romulus, Apocalypse — reactivates a template laid down here in childhood: *the person you take as your origin is not your origin*.

## 1.2 Constitutional Status — the Sickly Child

The boy as drawn and written across *Origin* #1–2 is **somatically fragile, undersized for his age, allergic, asthmatic, photophobic**. He is kept indoors. He wears a nightshirt for much of the early sequencing because he is too unwell to dress for outside. The estate's physician is a recurring presence. The household speaks of him in the register reserved for children who may not live.

This is critical and is often under-read. The man who will become the most physically indestructible figure in his world begins life as *the boy who cannot run with the other children*. The healing factor, which is implicitly active in some attenuated form from birth (it is what saves him at age twelve and is responsible for his apparent age progression thereafter), is not phenomenologically available to him as a child. He experiences himself as weak, as a burden, as the heir who will not last. Two later behavioral signatures track to this:

1. **The mentorship pattern with small, underestimated, fast adolescents** — Kitty Pryde, Jubilee, Armor, Laura — selects, with notable specificity, for children built like the child he was, and teaches them precisely the survival competencies he himself lacked at their age.
2. **The lifelong recklessness toward his own body** is grounded not only in the eventual experience that no injury kills him, but in an earlier and inverted premise that *the body is unreliable and may fail at any moment*. He oscillates between treating the body as a fortress and treating it as expendable, because both are felt-truths from different developmental epochs.

## 1.3 Daily Environment, Sensorium, Routines

The estate as depicted is a closed system. The boy's daily orbit is small: bedroom, kitchen, library (his father's), the parlor, the verandah, the immediate grounds. He reads. He is read to. He is taught by tutors whose names are not given in canon. He plays with Dog and Rose on the grounds — supervised, then increasingly less so as he stabilizes physically. He has no siblings present (the elder brother is dead before his memory begins). He has no peer cohort beyond Dog and Rose. He has no exposure to town life, schooling among other children, or the Indigenous communities of the region (the household is presented as insular and ethnically English-Canadian in the colonial mode).

The **sensorium** in which his hyperacute senses will later install themselves is, at this stage, the sensorium of a large, drafty house: woodsmoke, lamp oil, polished wood, the cold of the floors in the morning, the kitchen at bread-making, horses and manure from the stables, the bog-and-spruce smell of the boreal forest at the property's edge. His later olfactory map of safety — fire, leather, tobacco, snow on conifers, horse — derives from this period and will be reproduced, decades on, in his choice of cabins in the Canadian Rockies, his preference for the Hudson household's hearth, and his affinity for the Xavier mansion's library wing.

His **early speech pattern** is, on the published evidence, the speech of a well-raised Anglo-Canadian boy of the period — formal, soft-voiced, deferential to adults. The clipped, drawling, monosyllabic register that becomes his adult signature is acquired post-trauma, in the mining camps and on the rail crews. The change in his voice is itself a marker of identity discontinuity; the file should note that the voice in which he speaks for the next century is a learned voice, an over-written one.

## 1.4 The Three Primary Childhood Bonds

**Rose O'Hara (primary attachment).** The published record is unambiguous that Rose is the closest figure in James's emotional life. She is age-mate, playmate, confidante, and — in the boy's own register — the figure who organizes his daily affect. She speaks to him without the household's pity. The sequence in *Origin* in which the two of them play at the pond and on the grounds is the only depicted period of regulated, age-appropriate, mutually responsive relating in his entire pre-Weapon X biography. She is the prototype of the **redheaded woman** to whom he will return, compulsively, for the next hundred and twenty years (Jean Grey being the most consequential reactivation, but not the only one).

**Dog Logan (rivalrous bond).** Dog is the boy's second sustained peer relationship and the inverse of Rose in every register. He is loud where Rose is steady, cruel where she is kind, opportunistic where she is loyal. He envies James for the house, the food, the bed, the parents-as-frame-even-if-cold; James, in canonical sequence, intercedes for Dog with the elder Howlett to spare him beatings and is, for that intercession, hated. Two scenes establish the dynamic before the catastrophe: Dog killing James's dog (the act named in the title of his own nickname's etymology, an authorial joke that nevertheless lands behaviorally), and Dog's attempted assault on Rose, which James and Rose both witness and which is reported up the household chain, leading to Thomas Logan's dismissal. Dog is the **prototype of the antagonistic mirror** — the same age, the same locale, knowing him too well, hating him for what he has, returning across years to renew the conflict. Sabretooth in the twentieth century is Dog in adulthood, structurally if not literally. (Some later canon, *Wolverine: Origins*, treats the Romulus-engineered hostilities as the deep frame; the Howlett-estate Dog is nevertheless the experiential ground.)

**John Howlett Jr. (deficient social father) and Thomas Logan (rejected/violent biological father).** Neither father is felt as a father. The social father is distant, polite, ineffective. The biological father is unknown-as-such, present as a frightening adult on the grounds whose anger occasionally spills toward the children. The mother is essentially absent. **The boy's effective parenting is being done by Rose and, residually, by the kitchen staff.** This is the developmental fact from which the disorganized attachment profile derives. The figures contractually responsible for protection are non-responsive; the figure functionally providing companionship is a child; the violent man on the perimeter is the genetic origin nobody has named. No structure in this configuration permits the child to develop a stable internal model of "caregiver."

## 1.5 The Catastrophic Night (*Origin* #2)

The triggering event of the entire subsequent biography occurs in a single evening at the Howlett house. The sequence, recovered in *Origin* #2 and clarified by *Origin* #6, runs:

1. Thomas Logan, recently dismissed from the estate over the assault on Rose, returns to the main house drunk and armed, with Dog in tow. The intent, as the dialogue makes plain, is partly robbery, partly the reclamation of Elizabeth (whom he characterizes as having been his), and partly inchoate class-and-paternity grievance.
2. They force entry through the kitchen. John Howlett Sr. is killed almost immediately.
3. John Howlett Jr. confronts Thomas; Thomas shoots him dead in front of James.
4. The boy, witnessing the killing of the man he believes to be his father, undergoes the **first claw extrusion** of his life. Three bone claws — to that point unknown to him and to the household — erupt through the skin of the dorsal surface of each hand. He charges Thomas Logan and impales him, killing him. He wounds Dog across the face in the same sequence, leaving the scarring that Dog will carry into adulthood.
5. Elizabeth, who has descended into the chaos, **recoils from her son in horror**. The dialogue of her response — language to the effect of *what are you* — is the second wound of the night and arguably the deeper one. She subsequently takes her own life with the shotgun left at the scene; *Origin* depicts this explicitly.

Within a span of minutes the boy has, in order: watched the killing of his social father; killed (without knowing it) his biological father; been recoiled-from and effectively disowned by his mother; lost his mother to suicide; and discovered that his own body contains weapons. *The category of family is annihilated in one continuous sequence, and the instrument of the annihilation is the body the boy has just discovered he inhabits.*

The behavioral consequences are immediate and lifelong:

- **Trauma-coupled mutation onset.** The first claw extrusion is welded, neurologically, to mortal threat and to the death of a parent. Every later extrusion accesses, at some sub-symbolic level, this initial circuit. The fact that extrusion lacerates the dorsal hand each time means that *the act of self-defense reproduces a small bodily wound in the exact site of the first traumatic discovery of the self-as-weapon*. The body keeps the score in literal scar tissue, healed and re-opened thousands of times.
- **Maternal-recoil imprint.** The look on Elizabeth's face is the file's candidate for the founding image of his lifelong **self-as-monster** schema. The conscious adult identity — "the animal," "what I do isn't very nice," the pre-emptive refusal of intimacy — is the metabolized form of *the mother saw me and turned away*.
- **Familicide-by-claw template.** The first use of the claws kills a parent (unbeknownst, his actual parent). The pattern in which **the people he loves die on or because of his claws** — Rose within months, Itsu by proxy, Mariko by his hand at her request, the X-Men under Mysterio's illusion in *Old Man Logan* — is not a coincidence of plot. It is the compulsive re-staging of the founding scene, with the variable of who-knows-what shuffled. The unconscious experiment, repeated for a century, is *can I do this once without the loved one dying.* The answer in canon, with rare and qualified exceptions, is no.

## 1.6 Flight, the Quarry, Rose, and the Death of "James"

James and Rose are placed into flight by the surviving household — the boy is, after all, the killer of the groundskeeper, his health is fragile, and the household cannot publicly accommodate a son with claws. They are sent to a **stone quarry in British Columbia** (the locale across *Origin* #3–5), where Rose, despite being a child herself, takes on the role of his guardian. The boy, in shock, has lost continuous autobiographical access to the events of the catastrophic night. *He believes John Howlett is dead of an illness or accident.* The amnesia is not yet the Weapon X amnesia; it is its developmental precursor — **a child's dissociative response to overwhelming violence and maternal rejection**, in which the unbearable scene is sealed off and the cover story is allowed to ride on top.

At the quarry, several formative patterns consolidate:

- **He abandons the name James.** He takes the surname of his biological father — *Logan* — without consciously knowing why. This is, structurally, the first of the lifelong **alias-as-identity-management** behaviors. Each later name (Patch, Weapon X, Death, the various covers) inherits the underlying gesture: when the self becomes intolerable, *take a different name and proceed*. The choice of *Logan* specifically — the name of the man he killed, the name of the household's violent edge — is the period's most telling unconscious act. He is, in naming himself, identifying with the killed father and with the violence by which the killing occurred.
- **Manual labor as regulator.** He works the quarry alongside grown men, including the older Cree miner Smitty (who becomes a quasi-paternal figure and, by the close of *Origin*, a romantic rival for Rose). The hard physical labor, performed by a body that is rapidly outgrowing its earlier fragility under the healing factor's quiet operation, becomes the **first non-pharmacological affect regulator** of his life. The lifelong pattern of self-imposed physical hardship — long hikes alone, woodcutting, the Bushidō kata, the punishing training regimens he inflicts on himself and on his students — is prefigured here. *Labor steadies him when nothing internal can.*
- **Romantic idealization of Rose, suppressed.** As the two of them age in the quarry sequence (the timeline collapses several years), James/Logan's attachment to Rose deepens into something the published panels render as adolescent romantic love, expressed obliquely because of Smitty and because the boy's own affective vocabulary is, by now, badly damaged. He cannot speak it. He watches. *The pattern of being unable to declare to the beloved woman what is felt for her* will run from this scene to Jean Grey eighty years later, essentially unmodified.
- **Animal proximity.** The *Origin* sequences and the immediately subsequent *Wolverine: The Origin* coda show him beginning the drift toward the forest — taking long unsupervised periods outside the camp, returning later, eventually finding the wolf pack with which he will live after the second catastrophe. The fascination with wolves is encoded before he leaves human society; it does not come from the forest, it precedes the move into the forest.

## 1.7 The Second Catastrophe — Rose's Death

The closing sequence of *Origin* #6 stages the formative event's first **major repetition**. Dog Logan, now grown, arrives at the quarry as a bounty hunter sent to retrieve James Howlett for the killings at the estate. The confrontation escalates to combat. In the chaos — and the panel composition makes it almost a stage-managed accident, not an intentional strike — **Rose is impaled on the bone claws** as Logan turns, dies in his arms, and the second catastrophe of his life is complete.

Within nine years of the first, he has killed his biological father with the claws and killed the woman he loves with the claws. The hypothesis sealed in this moment, and never subsequently dislodged by any therapeutic relationship in canon, is: *the apparatus of my body kills the people I love.*

The behavioral response is immediate and definitive. He **leaves human society**. He walks into the forest. The wolf-living period — alluded to across *Origin*'s epilogue, the *Wolverine: The End* fragments, and various flashbacks — begins here. He runs on four limbs. He eats raw. He does not speak for an undefined long interval (years, in the published implication). The dissociative withdrawal that will characterize every subsequent crisis (the wilderness exiles of the X-Men era, the geographic flight of *Old Man Logan*, the Krakoan retreats) **acquires its full template here**: when the human social field becomes intolerable, *exit it and become something else*. The "animal" identity that the adult will wear as a defensive self-stigma is, in its origin, a literal episode of his life — not a metaphor.

## 1.8 The Earliest Behavioral Patterns — Summary for the File

Compiled from the above and noted here for cross-reference in subsequent sections:

1. **Disorganized attachment** — the result of two non-responsive parents, a violent unacknowledged biological father, and the salvaging of effective companionship by a child (Rose) who is herself unprotected. Manifest later in the approach-withdrawal pattern with every adult intimate.
2. **Dissociative defense, child-onset.** The seal-off of the catastrophic night is a developmentally early instance of the mechanism that Weapon X will later exploit to industrial scale. Per Şar (2014), the dissociation spectrum is most strongly associated with childhood trauma; the file reads Weapon X as having found pre-existing dissociative architecture and instrumentalized it, not as having created it from nothing.
3. **Alias-as-identity-management.** The renaming from James to Logan is the inaugural instance. The mechanism is operational by age ~twelve.
4. **Claw-extrusion as trauma-coupled act.** Pain at the dorsal hand + threat-cue + loss-of-parent are all welded into a single neurological event at first onset. The act of defense is, biographically, the act of orphaning.
5. **The redhead template.** Rose is the prototype. Jean Grey is the most consequential later instance. Mariko is a non-redheaded but structurally identical case (the woman whose death is delivered on the claws).
6. **Wilderness exile as regulatory exit.** The post-Rose wolf-living period is the prototype of every subsequent withdrawal.
7. **Self-as-monster schema, maternal source.** Elizabeth's recoil is the founding image. The adult's "I'm not fit" register is its metabolized form.
8. **Mentorship-of-the-young as reparative compulsion.** The protected child here is *himself, by Rose*; the adult will spend a century inverting the polarity and being-Rose for a succession of adolescent girls whose situations rhyme structurally with his own.
9. **Labor as regulator.** The quarry establishes it. It runs unchanged to the woodlots and dojos of the late biography.
10. **The chronic confusion of who is family.** Two fathers, one mother who recoils, a sister-figure who is not a sister, a half-brother (Dog) who is not acknowledged as such, a biological father not known as such — the **category of kin** is, from the first decade of life, an unreliable construct. The lifelong inability to settle into a family of choice (the X-Men come closest and remain provisional) is grounded here. So is the pathos of his eventual surrogate-fatherhoods (Amiko, Jubilee, Laura): they are constructed families assembled deliberately because the inherited one detonated.

---

*Section close. Section II will pick up with the wolf-living period, the gradual reentry into human society at the Yukon mining camps, the late-Victorian/Edwardian drift through the Canadian and American west, and the consolidation of the adult "Logan" presentation in advance of his arrival in Japan and the First World War.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

*Subject: LOGAN. Period under review: c. 1898 (the night the claws first came) through the end of the First World War, with selective extension into the interwar feral/Japanese reintegration phase that closes the formation arc. Source base: ORIGIN #1–6 (Jenkins/Kubert/Isanove, 2001–02); ORIGIN II #1–5 (Gillen/Kubert, 2013–14); WOLVERINE: THE ORIGIN backmatter; LOGAN (Vaughan/Risso, 2008); WOLVERINE vol. 3 #32–40 (Aaron, "Get Mystique" and adjacent flashback work); WOLVERINE: THE END (Castellini, frame data only); WOLVERINE: ORIGINS #1–10 (Way) for the Itsu/Daken material that closes this stratum; UNCANNY X-MEN #268 (Claremont/Lee) for the 1937 Madripoor reference points; corroborating flashbacks from WOLVERINE vol. 2 #34, #48–50, #125. Where the published record contradicts itself (and it does, repeatedly), I treat the contradiction as itself a datum: it is consistent with — and partial evidence for — the dissociative-amnesia diagnosis carried forward from Section 1.*

---

## I. Pre-Emergence Baseline (Alberta, c. 1882–1897)

Before the formation event, the subject's behavioral baseline reads almost as the *photographic negative* of the man he becomes. The salient pre-trauma data points:

- **Somatic fragility.** Documented as asthmatic, frequently bedridden, light-sensitive, sensitive to cold. He is the *sickly* Howlett child, kept indoors, schooled by tutors rather than peers. The household runs on the assumption he will not live long. Read this against the later record: a man who cannot be killed begins life as a child no one expects to keep. The healing factor, when it surfaces, is not experienced as a gift but as the cancellation of an identity organized around fragility.
- **Sensory hypersensitivity in nascent form.** ORIGIN registers him as flinching at sounds, smells of the kitchen, the dogs in the yard. Reframed retrospectively: the hyperacute senses are not bestowed at puberty by mutation; they are present, sub-clinically, from childhood, and the sickliness is partly *sensory overwhelm* misread by the household as constitutional weakness.
- **Affective constraint of the household.** Elizabeth Howlett: postpartum-and-then-some, intermittently institutionalized after the death of an earlier child (the elder son Saul/John Jr., implied in ORIGIN), emotionally unavailable to James. John Howlett Sr. (social father): decent, ineffectual, unable to discipline the groundskeeper Thomas Logan, unable to reach his wife, unable to be present for the boy in any consistently embodied way. Grandfather John Howlett Sr. Sr.: cold, autocratic, contemptuous of weakness, the family's actual gravitational center. From the disorganized-attachment frame: the boy's caregivers are simultaneously the source of safety and a chronic, low-grade source of dysregulation — a textbook precondition.
- **Two surrogate-sibling bonds.** *Rose O'Hara*, the redheaded Irish kitchen girl brought in nominally as his companion: the first object of trust, the first person who touches him without medical pretext. *Dog Logan*, Thomas Logan's son, his rough playmate, who teaches him to throw a punch, to track in snow, to lie to adults. The two bonds correspond to the two poles he will oscillate between for the next 130 years — the tender protected feminine, and the brutal masculine peer who will turn predatory. Both poles are *already in the household* by his tenth year.
- **The kennel.** A behavioral micro-detail worth flagging: ORIGIN puts him with the dogs more often than with his mother. He sleeps on the floor by the kennel during one illness. The wolves he will later live among in the Yukon are not a discovery; they are a return.

What is *absent* from the baseline is equally diagnostic: there is no recorded incident of him initiating violence before age fifteen. He is the bullied child, not the bully. Dog is the aggressor; James is the one Rose protects. The capacity is latent. The trigger has not yet been pulled.

---

## II. The Formation Event (c. 1897–98)

The night of John Howlett's killing is the *Stunde Null* of the file. ORIGIN #2–3 give the canonical version; ORIGIN II adds inflection. Reconstructed in close detail because every later pattern can be read back to this twenty-minute interval:

1. **Precipitant.** Thomas Logan, dismissed from the estate by John Howlett Sr. (the social father) for unspecified misconduct, returns drunk with Dog. He enters the master bedroom and shoots John Howlett dead in front of the boy. (The retconned subtext, established in ORIGIN: Thomas Logan is James's biological father, the product of an affair with Elizabeth; John Howlett Sr. is the man who raised him but not the man who sired him.)
2. **First extrusion.** The boy's claws — *bone*, not adamantium; this matters historically and somatically — extrude through the dorsal fascia of both hands for the first time. The pain is recorded in his expression and posture in the Kubert art (hunched, screaming, staring at his own hands). Pain is, from the first instant, the *prerequisite* of his primary defensive capability. He will never extrude the claws painlessly across the entire record.
3. **First kill.** He impales Thomas Logan — *his actual biological father* — across the chest. The kill is reflexive, not chosen. He does not yet know the parentage; the reader, retroactively, does. From the formation standpoint this is the load-bearing fact: his inaugural violence is patricide of a father he does not know is his father, in defense of a father who is not his father.
4. **Collateral.** He also strikes Dog across the face, leaving the three-line scar Dog will carry for the rest of his short, ruinous life. The peer-bond is severed in the same instant as the father-bonds. The household, the family, the two bonds: all dissolved in under a minute. *This is the structural template.* Every later love object who dies (Rose, Itsu, Silver Fox, Mariko, Jean repeatedly) repeats some piece of this minute.
5. **Maternal repudiation.** Elizabeth, surfacing from her depressive baseline, looks at the bloody child and calls him an animal — the *exact* word that the Weapon X overseers will use ninety years later. She subsequently kills herself with the same rifle Thomas used. The word "animal" is, from this moment, the maternal verdict, and his entire later self-stigmatizing identity ("I'm the best there is at what I do, and what I do ain't very nice") is *the mother's word internalized*. The Bushidō-samurai counter-ideal he develops in Japan is the lifelong counter-argument to that one word.
6. **Flight.** Within hours, Rose takes him and runs. The grandfather signs them out into the wilderness rather than face the scandal. He never sees the house again. The boy is removed from his name — Rose, by the journey's end, is calling him "James" privately and "Logan" in public to hide him.

The immediate post-event behavioral picture, in the days following: amnesia for the event (or convincing performance of amnesia; the published record cannot resolve this and *neither can he*), regression to non-speech for some days, somatic complaints, refusal to look at his own hands. The bone claws retract and he does not, for some time, deploy them again. This is the first dissociative fugue in the file. He is roughly fifteen. The pattern — extreme violence followed by amnesia followed by withdrawal followed by reattachment to a protective female figure followed by another extreme violence — is now installed and will iterate for a hundred and thirty years.

---

## III. The Stone Pit (c. 1898–1907): Rose, Smitty, the Mining Camp

Rose delivers them to a British Columbia stone quarry / mining settlement run by a man called Hines (the surname recurs in Weapon X; the canon's choice to reuse it is, generously, thematic — the mining-camp foreman is the prototype of the laboratory overseer). The decade in the camp is the *training* period: not a happy interlude, but the apprenticeship in suppression.

- **Identity manufacture.** Rose introduces him as her cousin "Logan." The name is constructed on the spot, from the man he killed (Thomas *Logan*). He is *named after his first victim*, who is also his biological father. He uses that name, on and off, for the next century. Every signature is a covert confession.
- **Concealment of the claws.** For years he does not extrude them — partly volitional, partly fugue-driven suppression. He learns to *lose* a fistfight rather than risk display. This is the first installation of the inhibition that the *Old Man Logan* arc, eighty years later, will reproduce in extreme: when the weapon-self is contaminated by guilt, the conscious self refuses to deploy it at any cost. The mining-camp boy is the small-scale rehearsal for the Old Man.
- **Apprenticeship to Smitty.** The boxer-foreman Smitty becomes his first chosen male model: physically capable, decent, married, restrained. James/Logan learns to fight in the ring under Smitty's hand. Critically, he is taught *controlled* violence with rules — the first prosthesis for the unregulated capability the claws represent. This is the ancestor of his lifelong attraction to formal combat systems (Bushidō, judo, the kata practice that will appear in the Mariko years). Discipline as cage for the animal: the equation is set here.
- **Romantic substrate with Rose.** Slow, inarticulate, incomplete. They share quarters as cousins; the desire is mutual and unconsummated. Rose becomes engaged to Smitty. James does not protest, and the non-protest is its own datum — he has already, at sixteen or seventeen, installed the belief that he is unfit for the woman he loves; that *she should be with the safe man*. This belief survives every later iteration intact.
- **Reappearance of Dog.** Years in, Dog Logan tracks them down. He has been hired by the Howlett grandfather (or sent by Thomas Logan's ghost-by-proxy; ORIGIN is deliberately murky) to retrieve or kill James. The reappearance triggers everything that has been suppressed.

### III.a The Second Formation Event: Rose's Death

In the resulting fight — described and drawn so as to leave deliberate ambiguity about whether Dog kills Rose, or whether James does — James extrudes the claws in full berserker discharge and lunges. Rose intervenes. The claws go through her. She dies in his arms. He has now killed, with his own body, the first woman he loved.

The behavioral aftermath:

- Immediate flight from the camp on foot, into wilderness, without supplies.
- Sustained amnesia for the precise mechanics of the killing — across the entire later record, when he revisits this memory, the *blow itself* is the part that recurs as a fragment, not a sequence.
- Refusal of human society for what the record suggests is *years*, possibly close to a decade. He lives in the bush. He runs with a wolf pack (corroborated in WOLVERINE: THE END's flashback frames and in Aaron's WOLVERINE WEAPON X-era backstory work). He hunts, sleeps in dens, and — by his own later statement — forgets language for a period.

This is the second formation event, and it ratifies the first. Pattern now fully encoded, in three propositions the subject will operate from without consciously articulating them for a century:

1. *My violence kills the women I love.*
2. *Therefore, I should not love women, or, if I do, I should be prepared to lose them.*
3. *The animal my mother named is real and the only honest self I have. Civilization is a courtesy I extend; it is not what I am.*

The samurai counter-ideal has not yet been encountered. Until Japan, these three propositions go uncontested.

---

## IV. The Feral Interval (c. 1907–1914)

The years between Rose's death and Logan's first documented re-entry into human institutions are the most poorly documented in the file — *deliberately*, both in-universe (he does not remember them well) and out-of-universe (writers have left them as negative space). What can be assembled:

- **Lupine cohabitation.** He runs with a wolf pack in the Yukon and Northwest Territories. He is the only documented case in the record of him being accepted by predators as a peer rather than a threat. The healing factor presumably reads as anomalous robustness; the hypersenses align him to pack communication; the absence of human scent-load (no soap, no tobacco, no alcohol yet) lets him pass. The bond with one specific wolf — referenced obliquely in later "the dog with no name" motifs (LOGAN: A DOG'S LIFE, the "Patch" Madripoor stories, the recurring symbol of the wolf in his dreams) — is the first stable attachment after Rose, and it is non-human. The fact that he can attach non-humanly with more reliability than humanly is a marker of how completely human attachment has been associated with annihilation.
- **Loss of language.** He recovers it later but the published record is consistent that during this interval he does not speak. The first-person interiority bleeds out. When he re-emerges he speaks in short declarative sentences for years, a style retained for life.
- **First documented healing-factor stressors.** Frostbite to fingers and face, regenerated. A bear mauling (depicted in flashback in WEAPON X-era material) — survived. A gunshot from a trapper, the bullet pushed out as he sleeps. He learns, in this interval, what his body will and will not do. The recklessness toward his own body that the file flags as parasuicidal is installed here, by repeated empirical demonstration to himself that nothing will stick.
- **Aging anomaly.** He is, chronologically, in his twenties. He looks the same as he will in 1945, in 1975, in 2020. Whether he notices the absence of aging during the feral years is unclear (no mirrors). But by the time he returns to human settlement he has the somatic age of a man in his early-to-mid thirties, and there he will roughly remain.

A bridging incident, drawn from the LOGAN miniseries (Vaughan/Risso) and from Aaron's "Get Mystique" — *Truett Hudson*, a trapper, finds the feral man and brings him in to a Yukon roadhouse. Aaron's Mystique (running a brothel-cum-saloon in this period) encounters him in or near this state. The detail that matters: he is taught, by a woman with no investment in his welfare, to wear clothes again, to take whisky, to sit at a table. The reintroduction to humanity is mediated by a transactional female figure. This datum sets a pattern that will recur in his Madripoor "Patch" identity decades later: he is most functional in *liminal* social spaces (brothels, bars, frontier towns, port cities) where the social contract is thin and explicit, and least functional in fully regulated environments (officers' clubs, the Xavier mansion at first, board meetings).

---

## V. First Institutional Reintegration: The Great War (1914–1918)

The First World War is, paradoxically, the *therapeutic* environment that returns him to human society. The reasoning is grim but coherent: a context that requires sanctioned violence, demands no autobiographical self-disclosure, supplies a chain of command that asks no questions about parentage or origin, and rewards what he is best at — this is the first social ecology that fits him. He enlists (multiple flashback panels in Captain America-adjacent annuals, MARVEL COMICS PRESENTS material, and Aaron's run all place him in the Canadian Expeditionary Force, plausibly the Princess Patricia's Canadian Light Infantry).

Granular behaviors first documented in this period and retained for life:

- **Trench dissociation.** The berserker state — first seen in raw form in the Rose killing — is professionalized here. He is the man who comes back from no-man's-land alive when others do not. Officers note (in flashback dialogue) that he "goes somewhere else" during night raids. The amnesia for the engagement is consistent. He learns, crucially, that the dissociative state is *useful* — that institutions will reward him for entering it. From this point on, the berserker is not only a symptom but a service.
- **Cigar habit.** Documented as originating in the trenches. The cigar — slow-burning, hand-occupying, scent-masking against gas and rot — is functional before it is stylistic. He retains it for life because the functional reasons survive; the hypersenses still benefit from olfactory masking, the hands still benefit from occupation, the slow burn still paces breath.
- **Whisky tolerance regime.** The healing factor's metabolic acceleration means he discovers, in this period, that ordinary alcohol intake produces ordinary disinhibition only at extraordinary volume. The pattern of drinking by the bottle rather than the glass is installed. The drinking is, even at inception, anxiolytic rather than recreational — the contemporaneous letters and dialogues attributed to him in flashback never describe drinking *for pleasure*, only for *quiet*.
- **Camaraderie at unit scale.** He demonstrates, for the first time, the capacity for *peer* attachment in a male group — a capacity wholly absent since Dog. The men in his squad are the prototype of every later team-loyalty (Howling Commandos adjacency in WWII, Team X, Alpha Flight, X-Men). The unit, not the institution, is the loyalty object. This will be the load-bearing distinction of his entire political life.
- **First documented refusal of an order.** Recorded variably in different flashbacks: a refusal to execute prisoners, a refusal to fire on civilians, a refusal to shell a position with women present. Insubordination of a *specific* class — orders to harm the unarmed or the young — is hardwired by the time he leaves the war. It is the operationalization of proposition (1) above: knowing what his violence does, he will not direct it at those who cannot answer it.
- **First sustained period without an amnestic gap.** Apart from the berserker episodes themselves, the war years are, by his later testimony, among the *clearest* in his memory. The institutional structure provides the kind of external scaffolding for autobiography that his internal apparatus cannot supply. This will recur: he remembers his *deployments* better than his *peace*. Structure preserves narrative; freedom dissolves it.

The exit from the war is undocumented in granular terms. He demobilizes, presumably in Canada, in 1918 or 1919, and re-enters drift.

---

## VI. The First Japan (c. 1920s–1930s): Jasmine Falls and the Counter-Ideal

The Japanese reintegration is canonically placed in the interwar period (WOLVERINE vol. 3 #32 onward; corroborated in WOLVERINE: ORIGINS). He arrives in Japan in his condition of post-war drift — wandering Asia, doing harbor work and mercenary jobs — and is taken in by the Yashida clan and brought to the mountain village of Jasmine Falls. He studies under Bando Saburo.

This is the *single most consequential formation episode after the Howlett night*. Reasoning:

- For the first time, a *complete adult ethical system* is offered to him that takes the existence of his violence as a given and proposes to organize it rather than deny it. Bushidō is not the suppression of the warrior but the warrior's discipline. This is the first frame in his life that does not require him to choose between "animal" and "man" — it tells him an honorable man may also be a killer if he kills correctly.
- He learns kata, meditation, calligraphy, the tea ceremony — formal practices that impose external structure on internal states. The samurai practice is the *prosthetic affect regulation* that his nervous system cannot do unaided. He retains the practice for life, performing it most visibly in the Mariko years but maintaining it privately throughout.
- He meets Itsu. The relationship — quiet, domestic, the first he allows himself since Rose — produces a pregnancy. Itsu is murdered (Winter Soldier, per WOLVERINE: ORIGINS, in a hit ordered by Romulus) while pregnant; the fetus, cut from her, survives and becomes Daken. Logan does not learn of the survival for decades. From his perspective at the time, the equation holds again: *the woman I love is dead, and my presence is the proximate cause.* Proposition (1) is confirmed a second time, and the Japanese counter-ideal is — for the moment — disconfirmed at the very site of its installation.

The Itsu killing is the *closing event* of the formation period. After it, he is no longer being formed; he is iterating. The remaining 80+ years of behavior are variations on a structure now complete. What is added later — the Madripoor partnerships of 1937 (UNCANNY X-MEN #268), the Spanish Civil War, WWII and the bond with Rogers, Team X, Weapon X, the X-Men — adds *trauma load* and *relational data*, but does not alter the architecture installed between the Howlett night and Itsu's death.

---

## VII. The First Defining Choices and Their Fallout

Distilled, with the fallout traced forward:

| Choice | When | Fallout |
|---|---|---|
| To take the name "Logan" — his victim's name, his actual father's name | c. 1898, in flight with Rose | Lifelong refusal to settle a name. He answers to Logan, James, Patch, Weapon X, Death, and others, and the multiplicity itself becomes adaptive: no single name can be used to compel him. |
| To suppress the claws in the mining camp | c. 1899–1907 | Installs the lifelong template that the weapon-self can be inhibited at cost to the conscious self. The *Old Man Logan* arc is this choice run at maximum amplitude. |
| To love Rose silently while she becomes engaged to Smitty | c. 1905–07 | Installs the belief that he is unfit for the woman he loves and that the safer man should have her. Reappears, structurally, in his behavior toward Jean Grey vis-à-vis Scott Summers across the entire X-Men run. |
| To flee into the wilderness rather than face the camp after Rose's death | c. 1907 | Establishes geographic flight as the master coping behavior. Every later "I work alone" cycle, every disappearance to Canada or Madripoor, every wilderness retreat, is this choice repeating. |
| To enlist in the Great War | 1914–15 | Discovers that institutional violence can stabilize him. Sets the pattern that he will, throughout life, accept handler-relationships from organizations he does not trust because the structure manages a self he cannot. The Weapon X consent — to the extent there was any — and the Department H tenure both lean on this earlier discovery. |
| To accept Bushidō under Bando Saburo | interwar | Provides the only sustainable counter-identity to "the animal." Becomes the lifelong organizing aspiration and the criterion by which he judges his failures. The samurai ideal is the *only* internal authority he never finally repudiates. |
| To stay with Itsu and have a child | interwar | Confirms — when she is killed — proposition (1) at maximum intensity. Drives the next several decades of refusal to attach romantically without anticipatory grief. The fact that Daken survives, unknown to him, becomes the file's largest delayed-action charge: when the truth surfaces (WOLVERINE:


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Operational window: c. 1932 — c. 1975. From the Japanese integration through the Weapon X procedure, the Department H interlude, and the threshold crossing into Xavier's school. The four decades in which every later pattern is laid down in its mature, repeating form. Where Chronology II logged the feral century and the world-wars drift, this section maps the period in which the Subject acquires — and then has stripped from him, and then partially reconstructs — the architecture of a self.*

---

## I. The Japanese Integration (c. 1932 – 1946)

### Jasmine Falls: the only sustained period of regulated life in the record

The Subject arrives in the Yashida-clan village of Jasmine Falls in the early 1930s in a condition the source material consistently describes as *broken in three directions at once*: post-Great-War, post-Rose, post-feral. The village absorbs him on the unusual terms permitted by the Yashida elder Bando Saburo — board and instruction in exchange for labor and submission to a daily form. Behaviorally this is the single most important environmental intervention in his life prior to Xavier.

The granular pattern, reconstructed from *Wolverine* vol. 2 #1–4, the *Origin* II material, *Wolverine: The Origin* coda fragments, and the Itsu retconning in *Wolverine: Origins*:

- **Diurnal restructuring.** Pre-dawn rising, seated *zazen* before light, tea preparation as fine-motor discipline, kata in the morning, manual labor through midday, calligraphy and recitation in the afternoon, evening bathing, early sleep. The Subject's prior diurnal pattern — feral-nocturnal, opportunistic, sense-driven — is overwritten by an externally imposed cycle. This is the *prosthesis* (see workup §3, affect regulation): structure substituting for the internal regulatory function he never developed.
- **Somatic re-housing.** Bathing ritual (*ofuro*) is the first sustained tolerance of touch by another adult he is recorded to permit since the Howlett household; the cedar steam and rinse sequence becomes a lifelong sensory anchor. Decades later, in Madripoor and at the mansion, the unconscious tells are the same: he gravitates to hot water, to ritualized bathing, to the small acts of clean clothing and folded fabric. The body learned in Jasmine Falls that it could be tended.
- **Olfactory load reduction.** The village is small, agrarian, repetitive in its smell-set — rice, cedar, charcoal smoke, soy, mountain pine. The sensory storm that defined his urban and battlefield existence drops to a manageable baseline for the first time on record. The Subject's regulation improves in Jasmine Falls partly because the *input* improves; this is a permanent variable in his later geography (see Madripoor, Canadian Rockies — high-signal-to-noise environments preferred for self-restoration).
- **Linguistic acquisition.** Fluent colloquial Japanese, then Mandarin (mercantile), then enough Cantonese for Madripoor. Reading: *Hagakure*, *Book of Five Rings*, the Yashida house texts. The bilingual/bicultural acquisition is not affectation — it is part of the same structure-importation, and decades later it remains his code-switch under stress: when calming, he reaches for Japanese formal address; when issuing a final warning, often a *kanji*-rooted idiom.

### Bando Saburo and the first chosen father

The teacher–student relationship that the *Origin* II and *Wolverine* canon both insist upon does specific reparative work. Bando Saburo is the inverse, by every visible parameter, of John Howlett (sickly, emotionally distant) and of Thomas Logan (predatory, drunk, violent): he is steady, present, severe without cruelty, and — critically — he sees the Subject's capacity for violence not as the *truth* of him to be confessed, but as a *tool* to be governed. This reframing is the seed of every later non-suicidal moment the Subject achieves. The Howlett trauma collapsed the category *father* in one stroke; Bando Saburo is the first figure who lets the category be partially rebuilt, and rebuilt around *discipline rather than blood*. The lifelong preference for chosen kinship over biological kinship — most visible later with Xavier and with the surrogate-daughters — receives its formal grammar here.

### Itsu and the Daken event (c. 1946)

The marriage to Itsu, and her murder while pregnant by the Winter Soldier (*Wolverine: Origins* #16–18, Way), is the iteration of the Rose template at adult dose and with an obstetric catastrophe attached. Behaviorally observable consequences across the rest of the record:

- A second-tier permanent association: *pregnancy / impending motherhood* becomes a sensory-cue cluster that destabilizes him. The hyperacute olfactory system registers pregnancy reliably (hormonal shift detectable to him); he becomes notably more protective and notably more avoidant of pregnant women across all later eras (cf. interactions with Madelyne Pryor, with civilians in Madripoor, with Maria Hill in modern files).
- The decision — *forced upon him* by the Hand, then later by his own retreat — to abandon the body of Itsu, and to fail to know that the child survived, lodges as a structural shame. Daken's later existence as a hostile son is the *consequence-form* of that failure; the Subject's behavioral response to Daken is uncharacteristic for him (slowness, reluctance to kill, repeated tactical concessions) precisely because the shame is older than the encounter.
- The Jasmine Falls period *ends with this event*. The integration he had achieved — the only one — terminates in the canonical Rose-pattern outcome: *the one he loved died, and it is somehow on him*. The exit from Japan in the late 1940s is a flight in the original Howlett sense: identity dissolution and motion outward.

---

## II. Madripoor, Shanghai, and the Free-Lance Decade (c. 1946 – c. 1958)

### The Patch persona and the first deliberate identity-alteration

The Madripoor period (recorded primarily in *Wolverine* vol. 2 #1–10, Claremont/Buscema, and in flashbacks throughout the Hama run) is the first time the Subject *deliberately constructs* a dissociated identity rather than suffering one. "Patch" — the eye-patched, lower-Madripoor fixer who drinks at the Princess Bar and works for and against Tyger Tiger and General Coy — is operated as a *cover*, but the behavioral record indicates Patch is doing something more interior: he is a *container for the part of the Subject that can no longer believe in Bando Saburo's program*. Patch drinks more, fights more casually, sleeps with strangers, kills with less ceremony, and remembers less. The Subject can run Patch and tell himself that the samurai discipline is intact elsewhere; in fact Patch is *where the discipline goes when it cannot hold*.

This is the inaugural worked example of what the workup §4 names: identity alteration in the Şar sense, *consciously colluded with*. The post-Weapon X "Logan / James / Patch / Weapon X / Death" sequence is built on the template Madripoor establishes.

### Granular Madripoor pattern set

The following micro-behaviors are dated to this decade and persist verbatim into modern files:

- **The Princess Bar booth.** Back to wall, sight-line to door, no overhead light, ashtray right-handed, glass left-handed (preserves dominant hand). Replicated in *every* bar he occupies for sixty years across publications — Harry's Hideaway, the Salty Dog in Madripoor revisits, the Hellfire Club bar, even the staff mess at the Krakoan Quiet Council compound where the bar isn't actually a bar.
- **Cigar protocol.** Cut, not bitten, when in Patch mode (a Madripoor mercantile signal of class above the docks); bitten when in Logan mode. Across the rest of his life, observers can read his current self-state by which method he uses.
- **The three-drink rule.** He cannot get drunk by ordinary metabolism; he has discovered (Madripoor years) that he can *simulate* the affective effect of drunkenness by drinking with consistent rhythm — a drink per twenty minutes for a sustained interval — and surrendering to the simulation. This is the operational basis of all his later "drunk" behavior. He is performing intoxication to himself as a permitted regression. It is also why he prefers high-proof distillates: the throat-and-stomach signal is real and immediate even when the cortical effect is transient. Lifelong.
- **Sexual transience.** Madripoor establishes the pattern that runs through the next half-century: short, intense, geographically bounded liaisons (Seraph, Tyger Tiger, several unnamed). He does not bring partners home. He does not stay past three nights. The behavioral logic, observable across the file: extended intimacy reactivates the Rose/Itsu template, and the avoidance is prophylactic.

### Seraph, the second teacher

The bar-owner Seraph (introduced in flashback in *Wolverine* vol. 3 and *Logan: Path of the Warlord* material) is the second formative non-parental figure of this period. Where Bando Saburo taught structure, Seraph teaches *operational dissimulation* — how to lie with the body when one's scent betrays one's mood, how to use a bar as an intelligence node, how to keep three contradictory loyalties without any of them snapping. The "what people don't know about you is the only edge you'll ever have" doctrine the Subject articulates in much later issues (e.g. to Jubilee, to Kitty) is Seraph's, almost verbatim. She is also the only romantic-mentor figure on record; the death of Seraph (per the canon, at the hands of the Hand or in associated Madripoor conflict) writes another tally on the Rose ledger.

### The first Sabretooth "birthday"

The annual ritualized attempt by Victor Creed on the Subject's life is implicitly traced back to a Madripoor-era origin (the canon dates the formal pattern to the late 1950s in various Hama/Tieri retrofits). The Subject's later articulation — that the appointment is on his *actual* birthday, that Creed always finds him, that the failure to kill is the point — is grounded in the Madripoor years when the encounter became *predictable enough to plan around*. From this point forward the most reliable scheduled appointment in his life is his enemy's. Workup §5 notes the diagnostic significance; the *temporal stability* of the appointment is the point.

---

## III. The Team X Period (c. 1961 – c. 1968)

### Re-entry into institutional violence

Recruitment into Team X (CIA-adjacent, USAF cover, intermittent Department K coordination — the exact org-chart is deliberately fogged in the canon, *Wolverine* vol. 2 #48–50, Hama) places the Subject into a small cell with Victor Creed (Sabretooth), Christoph Nord (Maverick), John Wraith (Kestrel), Silver Fox, and Mastodon. The cell receives the *first* documented memory implantation procedures — pre-Weapon X, less invasive, designed to compartmentalize mission knowledge and to manufacture false biography that would survive interrogation.

The granular consequences:

- **Silver Fox as the third Rose iteration.** The cabin, the idyll, the Sabretooth intrusion on the Subject's birthday, the apparent death — the entire sequence (Hama, *Wolverine* #10 flashback continuity) is functionally identical to Rose and to Itsu, except that here it is *partially implanted*: the canon eventually establishes that Silver Fox survived and was herself a Team X asset, that some of his memories of her are constructed, that some are real and overwritten. He cannot tell which. This is the inflection point at which his autobiographical memory becomes *evidence to be cross-examined* rather than identity (workup §3, cognitive style). The cabin scene is real to him and false to the world; the world's version is real and false to him; he learns, by the late 1960s, that he can no longer answer the question *what did I lose, and to whom*.
- **The Creed cohabitation.** Years in close professional proximity to the man trying annually to kill him — sharing missions, billets, after-action drinking — produce the durable structural pattern: *Creed is the most consistent presence in my life and he is my enemy*. The disorganized-attachment dynamic (workup §3) acquires its operational form here. The Subject learns to function alongside the predator, to read his moods, to anticipate his attacks, to *miss him when he is gone*. None of this is articulated; all of it is behaviorally evident in every later Creed encounter — the recognition is too fast, the rage too fluent, the resolution always incomplete.
- **The implanted-memory tell.** From Team X forward, the Subject acquires a specific somatic response to recall: when a memory surfaces that he is uncertain of, he goes briefly still, head slightly tilted, breath suspended for one to three seconds, then exhales slow. Observers who know him (later: Charles Xavier, later still: Jean Grey, much later: Kitty) read this gesture as *the verification check* — he is sniffing the memory for falsity, in the literal somatic sense of testing whether it sits right in the chest. The tell originates in this period because this is the period in which the practice becomes necessary.

### The Carbonadium Synthesizer mission and the loss of Janice Hollenbeck

The Berlin-era mission (*Wolverine: Origins* and *Maverick* material) in which the Subject extracts and then loses Janice Hollenbeck under Romulus's manipulation places another Rose-template body on the ledger and confirms — though it will not be conscious for decades — that someone *above* Team X is curating his trauma deliberately. The behavioral marker: from approximately the Berlin mission onward, the Subject's sleep architecture becomes worse. He had been a four-to-six-hour sleeper since Jasmine Falls; from the late 1960s on, the canon's incidental scenes consistently show him sleeping in increments — ninety minutes, two hours — with the hyperacute senses operating as perimeter for the conscious mind he can no longer trust to wake on time.

### Pre-Weapon X disengagement and drift

By the late 1960s the Subject has exited Team X under conditions the canon never fully clarifies — partial defection, partial retirement, partial extraction by other intelligence interests. He is in Canada in this transitional period, doing odd jobs and intermittent contracts; he resumes Yukon habits (woods, trapping, solitary cabins) in cycles between contracts. This is the disposition in which he is acquired by the Weapon X program.

---

## IV. The Weapon X Procedure and Its Immediate Aftermath (c. 1968 – c. 1970)

### Abduction and the procedure

The defining trauma (Windsor-Smith, *Marvel Comics Presents* #72–84) requires unusual granularity here because every later behavior in this dossier refers back to it. The reconstructable specifics:

- **Abduction conditions.** Taken while compromised (drunk to the limit of healing-factor metabolization is the canonical implication; this is the basis of a later, unspoken vow he keeps imperfectly — *never be that drunk again where anyone can reach me*; the modern files show the three-drink rule as the operationalization).
- **Tank immersion.** Prolonged suspension in a viscous fluid medium with breathing apparatus, with sensory-deprivation goggling alternated with bright-light over-stimulation, EEG and neural-implant work, hormonal manipulation. This is the iatrogenic dissolution of the *baseline sensorium* he had relied on his entire life. Lifelong sequela: he cannot tolerate confinement in fluid; the *Death of Wolverine* drowning-in-adamantium event in 2014 is a callback the body never stopped expecting.
- **Bonding procedure.** Skeletal adamantium infusion under partial paralysis with insufficient anesthesia. The canonical depiction (Windsor-Smith's claustrophobic panels: gloved hands, occluded vision, the Subject's own voice narrating in fragments) is the source of his lifelong distrust of medical settings. He will, in later years, refuse Beast's infirmary except under duress; he will sit through field-medic care on himself; he will not lie supine voluntarily for examination. Hank McCoy, in 1980s files, develops workarounds (standing assessments, hand-held instruments) that the Subject permits.
- **Engineered dissociation.** The Cornelius/Hines/Professor triad's deliberate construction of the "animal" state — operant conditioning, kill-protocols on verbal triggers, electrical reinforcement — *manufactures* what the Şar framework would name a culture-bound iatrogenic dissociative reaction. The berserker state, in its mature 1970s-onward form, is not Logan's pre-existing rage with adamantium added; it is *the Weapon X state, partially under his own management*. He spends the rest of his life trying to either suppress it (Bushidō) or selectively license it (X-Men combat). He does not, ever, fully *own* it. It was authored by other hands.

### The escape

The escape from the facility — naked, blood-soaked, bone-claws and adamantium claws indistinguishable, walking through snow — is depicted as a fugue. The Subject does not retain coherent memory of the escape itself. The bodies of the Weapon X personnel he kills on his way out are catalogued post-hoc by the Hudsons; the Subject in later years has only fragments. This is the second great hole in the autobiographical record (after Team X) and it is *the wound from which the wound was made*. From this moment on the Subject knows, somatically if not yet verbally, that *he can do something terrible and not be present for it*.

### The Hudsons

James and Heather Hudson find him in the Canadian Rockies (the canon places this in the area near the eventual Department H wilderness installations). The behavioral significance of the Hudsons is enormous and frequently underweighted:

- They take him in *as a person*, not as an asset, before they know what he is. The home environment they create — small house, fireplace, dogs, ordinary food, Heather's deliberate domestic gentleness, James's matter-of-fact engineering rationality — is the second holding environment of the Subject's life (after Jasmine Falls). It does for him, in a few months, what Bando Saburo did in years: gives the dissociated self a place to *settle without performance*.
- Heather Hudson is the prototype of the later non-romantic, non-paternal female bond — the *peer-protector* template that becomes load-bearing with Storm, Carol Danvers (in revisits), and later Jean (in the non-romantic interactional layer beneath the idealization).
- He attaches to the Hudsons; he then leaves them; he then returns; he then leaves them again. This oscillation is the first clear post-Weapon X demonstration that he *cannot* sustain the holding environment he most needs — that approach activates the avoidance circuit. It is the operational confirmation of the disorganized-attachment hypothesis (workup §3) in a setting uncomplicated by erotic charge or threat.

---

## V. Department H, Alpha Flight, and the Hulk Encounter (c. 1970 – 1974)

### The first government asset role

Department H (the Canadian government's metahuman-affairs program, headed by James Hudson) is the institutional setting that takes him from Weapon X graduate to *Wolverine* as designated codename. The detail-level granular record:

- **The costume.** The yellow-and-blue mask-and-suit (the original Cockrum design, premiered *Incredible Hulk* #181, 1974) is *Heather Hudson's design*, per the canon. The Subject wears it without protest. Behavioral significance: the costume is given to him by someone in the second holding environment; he accepts it the way the Yashida student accepted the kataginu. The garment is a *role*, externally specified, that lets him operate without authoring himself. He will keep wearing variants of it for fifty years, even after he understands it is somewhat ridiculous. The fact that he keeps wearing it is the tell that the function — *imposed identity as relief from authoring one* — has never become unnecessary.
- **The codename.** "Wolverine" is given to him; he does not choose it. The animal it names is small, vicious, and disproportionately aggressive to its size — apt, but the aptness is *someone else's reading of him*. He never adopts it self-referentially in private. Across the entire later canon, in solo internal monologue he is *Logan*, sometimes *James*, never *Wolverine*. The codename is the public-facing alter; *Logan* is the working self; *James* is the suspended-in-amber pre-trauma self who only appears under specific recall conditions. This three-layer naming pattern stabilizes in this Department H period and persists.
- **Operational role.** Wilderness extraction, tracking, anti-incursion, occasional black-ops. The Department H deployments lean on the skill-set Team X built; institutionally he is doing the same work for a less ruthless flag. The behavioral cost of this continuity is hidden: he is still operating the *Weapon X body* (literal — the adamantium, the conditioned states) in the *Team X mode* (operational dissimulation), under a *new costume* (Wolverine). The integration is cosmetic. The internal architecture is unchanged.

### The Hulk fight (April 1974, *Incredible Hulk* #180–181)
