He does not betray volitionally. The canon contains no instance of him selling out a person to whom he has bonded for advantage, money, or self-protection. The defection from Department H to Xavier was a defection from a *handler*, not a peer. The various team-switches are categorically the same: he leaves institutions, not people.

What he *does* do — and what functions as betrayal from the bonded person's standpoint — is **disappear**. The withdrawal phase of the cycle reads, to the person left behind, as abandonment without notice. He vanishes from Kitty for stretches; he vanishes from Jubilee; he leaves the mansion for months without explanation; he goes north. The structure is *not* betrayal of loyalty but **flight from the unbearable internal state intimacy produces** — yet the relational damage is real, and bonded persons across the canon report it (Kitty's adolescent grievances in *Kitty Pryde and Wolverine*; Jubilee's complaints; Jean's frustration).

The other betrayal-vector is the **compelled betrayal**: episodes in which his agency is hijacked and he is made to harm bonded persons. *Enemy of the State* (Millar) is the paradigm — Hand/Hydra conditioning turns him on his own colleagues. *Old Man Logan* is the foundational instance. In each case the bonded persons survive (or do not) but the *relationship to himself* takes the betrayal damage: he treats himself as the betrayer regardless of agency, which is why the post-Mysterio response was fifty years of refused claws. The conscience punishes the dissociated weapon-self as if it had chosen.

## 7. How He Repairs — and the Limits of His Repair Capacity

Repair behavior, when it occurs, is **non-verbal, slow, and oriented to physical presence rather than apology**. He does not say sorry well. He returns. He stands in the doorway until invited in. He resumes the patrol. He shows up at the recital. He brings the blade. The bonded person is expected to read the return as the apology, and across the canon they do — Kitty does, Jubilee does, Ororo does, Kurt does.

When repair requires verbal accounting he is **poor at it and knows he is poor at it**, which produces a secondary avoidance: he will postpone or skip the conversation. Mariko in life received more verbal disclosure from him than any other adult partner, which the texts mark as the high-water line of his capacity. With Jean the verbal disclosure happens only at her deathbeds, repeatedly — he can speak the bond only when it is being severed, which is itself a disorganized-attachment signature: intimacy is tolerable only when its loss has already been secured.

Repair fails entirely in two cases: (a) when the bonded person was killed *by his hand* and the bond cannot be re-entered (Mariko, Itsu — both are processed through ritualized mourning rather than repair, e.g., the Bushidō annual observances); (b) when his memory of the relationship has been corrupted and he cannot locate the original bond (the Silver Fox dilemma — he cannot grieve cleanly what he is not sure he experienced).

## 8. Intimacy and Dependency — What He Can and Cannot Tolerate

He can tolerate:
- Sustained physical adjacency in silence.
- One-directional dependency *upon him* (a ward, a wounded ally, a hostage to be protected).
- Ritualized intimacy at fixed intervals (the chess game, the rooftop cigar, the dōjō session).
- Acknowledgement of bond by the other party without expectation of his verbal reciprocation.
- Being known by the other person without being *asked about* by them — Ororo's gift is that she perceives him without interrogating him.

He cannot tolerate, and decompensates under:
- Sustained eye contact during emotional disclosure.
- Being asked direct questions about his interior state in the absence of crisis.
- Being depended upon for emotional regulation by an adult peer (as distinct from a ward — dependency by a ward he can carry indefinitely; dependency by a partner activates the kill-template).
- Telepathic intimacy unmediated by long prior trust (Jean's and Xavier's psychic touches are tolerated; almost no one else's are).
- Unstructured leisure with a bonded person. He needs *task* between himself and intimacy. The mission, the patrol, the training session, the bar shift are the structures that permit closeness; without them he flees.
- Being thanked at length, formally, in public.

The dependency pattern is **asymmetric by design**: he is the depended-upon, never the depender. To be the depender activates the originating helplessness of the asthmatic Howlett child, and is intolerable. The only canonical exception is the Hudson household post-Weapon X, where for a brief period he is genuinely dependent on James and Heather Hudson to restore him to humanity — and the Hudson bond accordingly retains lifelong charge.

## 9. The Relational Template, Stated as a Single Sentence

Across every relationship of his recorded life, the operating equation is: *I will stand near you, learn your scent, teach you to survive me, protect you with my body until the moment my body is the thing that kills you, and then I will go north for a while and return when there is another of you to protect.* He has lived this sentence with Rose, with Itsu, with Mariko, with Jean, with Kitty, with Jubilee, with Laura, with the Krakoan young, and in inverted form with Creed. The container he has built around it — Bushidō discipline, mentorship structure, ritualized adversary, alcohol, and exile — does not dissolve the template. It manages it. The management is the work of his adult life, and on the days it holds, he is the best version of what was made of him. On the days it does not, he goes north, and someone he loves lights a candle and waits.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Subject: LOGAN — Defensive Architecture, Full Inventory

The defensive system in this subject is unusually legible because it has been stress-tested across more decades and more pressure-vectors than almost any documented case in the canon. What follows is a complete inventory of the mechanisms he uses to hold himself together, ranked roughly from most mature (deployed when arousal is low and time is available) to most primitive (deployed when arousal exceeds the threshold his physiology can buffer). The architecture is not static: under sufficient pressure he *descends* the ladder in seconds, and after the episode he *climbs* it again, often via alcohol and geographic withdrawal as transitional rungs. The structure is the structure of a chronic dissociative trauma survivor with an unusually wide functional range — broader at the top than is typical for the diagnosis (because of Bushidō training and surrogate-parental practice), but bottoming out lower than most patients ever reach (because his anatomy permits and his history has rehearsed murderous discharge as a reliable terminator of intolerable affect).

---

## I. MATURE DEFENSES (calm states, low arousal, available time)

### 1. Sublimation — Bushidō practice and martial form

The most successful integrative mechanism in his inventory. The Jasmine Falls period under Bando Saburo, the recurring returns to Japan, the kata practice, the formal courtesies he maintains with Mariko's circle, the willingness to study tea ceremony and calligraphy — these are not affectations. They are an *imposed external structure where internal regulation has failed*. Every formal Japanese ritual he performs is a prosthesis for an affect-regulation system that does not work at native speed. The bow, the sheathed sword, the seiza, the deliberate slowness of pouring tea — each is a behavioral inhibitor practiced often enough to become semi-automatic, narrowing the gap between cue and lethal discharge by inserting trained micro-delays. When he is in a Japanese-coded space (the Yashida compound, his own dōjō, formal kenjutsu practice), the berserker threshold rises measurably; when he is in a bar, an alley, or a wilderness camp, it lowers.

The sublimation extends beyond Japan. The X-Mansion teaching role, the cooking (he is a competent cook; this recurs across writers — Claremont, Aaron — and signifies the same thing: a slow, sensory, controlled activity that occupies the hyperacute senses constructively). Mechanical work on motorcycles. The cigar ritual itself, when performed slowly on a porch rather than chain-smoked in stress, is a sublimation: the controlled inhalation, the rotation, the ash-tap, the long exhale — a meditative substitute he can perform anywhere.

### 2. Humor — sardonic verbal style as affect throttling

The "*bub*" register. The dry, clipped, faintly mocking idiom in which he addresses everyone from Cyclops to gods. Functionally this is not personality; it is a defense. Humor in this register accomplishes three things: (a) it discharges low-grade aggression verbally that would otherwise accumulate toward the threshold; (b) it maintains relational distance from people he is beginning to care about, preventing the intimacy that activates the Rose/Itsu/Mariko template; (c) it signals to himself and others that he is *still on the human side of the line* — the berserker does not joke. When he stops joking, the file should escalate. Loss of the verbal humor register precedes nearly every berserker episode on record.

### 3. Altruism / generativity — mentorship of adolescents

The mentorships with Kitty Pryde, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor (Hisako), and X-23 function as reparative compensatory practice with structural defensive value beyond their interpersonal warmth. They give him a *self-concept slot* — "teacher of survival" — that conscious access to is incompatible with the "animal" self-image. While he is in the teaching mode, the animal mode is functionally suppressed; the two states are mutually exclusive in working memory. He uses this deliberately: when most destabilized, he seeks proximity to one of these younger women, and the proximity itself reorganizes him. It is the cleanest defense in his repertoire and the one with the lowest collateral cost.

### 4. Suppression (conscious) — the file-it-away cognitive style

Distinct from repression. He is capable of *consciously* setting aside emotional material to act on a tactical priority. The clearest examples: continuing operational function in the immediate aftermath of Jean's deaths, continuing operational function after killing Mariko at her request (*Wolverine* vol. 2 #57), continuing operational function under the adamantium-extraction recovery. This is genuinely mature; it is also the mechanism most easily mistaken from outside for callousness. The cost is paid later, typically in the alcohol-and-wilderness cycle.

### 5. Stoicism / anticipation — assumption of the worst case

He plans for betrayal, ambush, memory implant, and loss of the people he cares about because all of these have already happened to him repeatedly. Anticipation as a defense is mature in the Vaillant sense: it prepares affect in advance so that the actual event lands on already-prepared ground. The downside in his case is that the anticipated futures are so dark that they color the present — he treats most allies as future losses, which produces the approach-withdrawal cycle in his closest bonds.

---

## II. NEUROTIC-LEVEL DEFENSES (moderate arousal, partial integration)

### 6. Reaction formation — the protector role against the predator history

The fierce protectiveness toward adolescent girls is, structurally, reaction formation against a century of having been a weapon used to harm. It is not insincere — reaction formation never is, in the subject's experience — but its *intensity* (the willingness to die unhesitatingly for a teenager he has known a month, e.g., Jubilee in *Wolverine* vol. 2) marks it as more than ordinary altruism. He is repairing a balance sheet.

### 7. Isolation of affect — clinical narration of his own violence

He can describe, in flat technical detail, what he has done and what he will do. ("*The best there is at what I do, and what I do isn't very nice.*") The affect is sheared off the content. This permits operational function in roles that would otherwise produce paralyzing guilt. The cost is that the affect is not metabolized, only deferred; it returns in dreams (which the canon repeatedly shows him having) and in the berserker overflow.

### 8. Intellectualization — the cross-examination of memory

His habitual treatment of his own autobiography as *evidence to be tested* rather than *identity to be inhabited* is an intellectualizing defense. He asks of every memory: who planted this, who profits from my believing it, what does it contradict. This is adaptive given Weapon X, Team X, Romulus, Hand, and Apocalypse all having overwritten him — but the cost is a chronic identity-confusion state in which nothing autobiographical is fully owned. The defense protects him from manipulation at the cost of preventing integration.

### 9. Displacement — Sabretooth as the receptacle for unsorted rage

The annual "birthday" ritual with Creed and the more general organization of his violence-budget around a single hated peer is displacement at scale. Sabretooth absorbs the rage that would otherwise have to be directed at the Professor, Cornelius, Hines, Romulus, the Hudsons' killers, his own father, himself. As long as Creed is alive and available, the rage has a legitimate target and need not be examined. This is why removing Sabretooth would likely destabilize the system: the displacement vessel would be gone and the contents would have to be re-routed.

### 10. Undoing — the post-episode amends pattern

After berserker episodes, after drinking damage, after withdrawal cycles, he characteristically returns and *does the thing right*: makes the apology (rare, but recorded — to Kitty, to Jean, to Rogers), takes the dangerous job no one else will take, stands the watch for a younger teammate, offers the cigar. This is undoing in the technical sense: a discrete symbolic act intended to neutralize a prior act. It is not sufficient to discharge the actual debt, but it is sufficient to permit him to continue functioning.

### 11. Identification with the aggressor (partial, contained)

The adamantium claws he chooses to keep extruding *through his own dorsal hand fascia* — the bone claws beneath are sufficient — is a complex behavior with an identificatory layer: he wears, internally, the weapon the Professor made of him. He has taken the instrument of his violation and made it the instrument of his agency. This is partial identification with the aggressor, contained by the conscious moral framework (Bushidō, the protector role) that determines *whom* he uses it on. Without the containment it would be the Sabretooth pathway; with the containment it is the warrior pathway. He lives on the seam.

---

## III. IMMATURE DEFENSES (high arousal, time pressure, threshold approach)

### 12. Splitting — innocents vs. legitimate kills, with thin middle

Under threat, his cognitive categorization of persons collapses to two boxes: *to be protected* and *to be removed*. The middle category (civilian bystander, ambiguous combatant, defectable enemy) shrinks toward zero as arousal rises. In calm states the middle category exists and is well-populated; in escalation it disappears. This is classic splitting, situationally deployed rather than characterologically fixed, and it is why his violence in the field, while extreme, rarely targets unambiguous innocents — the splitting is doing protective work, sorting the field before discharge.

### 13. Acting out — violence as primary affect discharge

The default. When the verbal humor register fails, when the Bushidō structure is not available, when alcohol has not yet been deployed, the affect is discharged motorically. The claw extrusion itself is a hybrid act — half warning display (neurotic-level signaling) and half acting out (the laceration of his own hands provides a small somatic discharge that takes the edge off the larger one). Bar fights, motorcycle riding at lethal speeds, picking on a known adversary when no legitimate target is available — all acting out in service of affect regulation.

### 14. Somatization (inverted) — pain as self-medication

The healing factor inverts the normal somatization vector. Where most patients somatize psychological pain into physical symptoms, he uses physical injury and pain to *displace* psychological pain that has no other outlet. The pre-fight readiness, the willingness to take unnecessary damage, the recklessness with his own body — these have a regulatory function. Physical pain is something his system knows how to process and conclude; psychological pain is not. He converts the latter into the former whenever he can.

### 15. Substance use — ethanol and nicotine as chemical anxiolysis pursuit

Behaviorally a defense rather than a pleasure. The healing factor metabolizes ethanol at rates that require intake far beyond normative thresholds to produce any effect; the fact that he continues to drink at those volumes indicates that the *behavior* of drinking — the bar, the bottle in the cabin, the ritual pour — is itself doing regulatory work even when the chemical effect is marginal. Cigars function similarly: the slow oral fixation, the breath control imposed by smoking, the sensory occupation of an otherwise hypervigilant olfactory system with a known reliable stimulus. Both substances are deployed prophylactically (before predicted stressors) and reactively (after episodes).

### 16. Geographic flight / wilderness withdrawal

The Yukon return, the Canadian wilderness cabins, the recurrent disappearances into northern forests for weeks or months at a time. These are not vacations. They are environmental management: removing himself from the sensory-and-relational load that his hyperacute senses and his attachment template cannot filter, into an environment where the only stimuli are weather, terrain, and animals — none of which activate the trauma circuitry. He returns from these cycles measurably re-regulated and then re-decompensates as social load rebuilds. The cycle is lifelong and recurs across writers.

---

## IV. PRIMITIVE / PSYCHOTIC-ADJACENT DEFENSES (threshold breach)

### 17. Dissociation — the berserker state proper

The defining defense and the symptomatic core. Under threshold breach (a specific olfactory cue: blood-of-a-protected-person, scent-of-a-canonical-enemy, the chemical signature of Weapon X facilities; or a specific cognitive cue: confirmation of memory implant, revelation of betrayal by an attached figure), consciousness narrows or splits. The behavior becomes automatized — combat motor programs run without conscious oversight — and anterograde amnesia for the episode follows. This is *not* anger and not Intermittent Explosive Disorder; per the Şar framework, it is an acute dissociative reaction within his chronic dissociative syndrome. The defensive function is total affect-and-conscience evacuation: the part of him that would have to live with what is about to happen is taken offline for the duration, and a separate state-dependent behavioral mode executes. He returns to himself, sometimes hours later, with bodies around him and gaps in recall.

### 18. Identity alteration — modal selves as compartmentalization

"James Howlett," "Logan," "Patch," "Weapon X," "Death," "the Old Man," the Krakoan resurrectee — these are not aliases for operational cover. Each is a behaviorally distinct mode with its own affective baseline, its own permitted range of action, its own relational repertoire, and its own partial amnesia for the others. "Patch" in Madripoor *cannot quite remember* being the X-Mansion mentor; "Death" under Apocalypse genuinely is a different operational personality with access to a different memory and value set. This is identity alteration on the dissociative spectrum, deployed defensively to compartmentalize incompatible self-states that would otherwise produce intolerable cognitive dissonance. The "James Howlett" identity in particular is held in a separate compartment from "Logan" — when the Howlett memories return whole (*House of M*), the integration is incapacitating, which is why they are normally kept apart.

### 19. Amnestic compartmentalization — the deliberate non-integration of recovered memory

Even when memory returns (post-*House of M*, post-*Origin*), he does not fully integrate it. He treats recovered autobiographical material with the same intellectualizing skepticism he applies to everything else, *and* he behaviorally avoids the contexts that would activate it. This is a learned defense: full integration has been demonstrated, in his own history, to be incapacitating. He has chosen, at some level, to remain partially amnestic because the alternative is the *House of M* collapse repeated indefinitely.

### 20. Conversion to inhibition (the *Old Man* mode) — total behavioral shutdown

The inverse symptom of the same disorder. When the dissociative weapon-self has been so contaminated that any access to it is intolerable (Mysterio's deception, the slaughter of the X-Men under hallucination), the defense system locks down the entire motor expression and refuses to extrude the claws for fifty years. This is conversion at the behavioral level: the conflict is solved by removing the capacity for the conflicted action. Catatonic in spirit, ambulatory in form. It is the most primitive defense in his repertoire because it costs the entire functional self to maintain.

---

## V. COMPENSATORY ARCHITECTURE — the positive-cluster summary

The *positive* compensations (Bushidō, mentorship, cooking, mechanical craft, formal courtesy, generativity toward the young) and the *negative* compensations (alcohol, geographic flight, sexual transience, berserker discharge, exile cycles, the displacement vessel of Sabretooth) are not separate systems. They are the same regulatory system operating at different rungs of the arousal ladder. The positive cluster works at low-to-moderate arousal and produces the integrated, generative, mentor-warrior presentation that the X-Men know. The negative cluster works at high arousal and at post-episode recovery, and produces the lone-wanderer-in-the-wilderness presentation that the rest of the world knows. He cycles between them on a schedule set by external stressors and internal contamination load.

The architecture's load-bearing fact is this: *the positive compensations are the prosthesis, not the structure*. There is no underlying regulated self that the prostheses adorn. The prostheses *are* the regulated self, assembled across a century from Bando Saburo's lessons, from Xavier's holding, from the faces of the girls he has trained to survive him, from the ritual cuts of the cigar, from the imposed slowness of a tea bowl. Remove the prostheses and what is underneath is the boy in the snow outside the Weapon X facility, the boy in the Alberta hallway with two dead fathers, the feral child among the wolves. He knows this. The knowledge is the substrate of the architecture's vigilance: he maintains the prostheses with the discipline of a man who has been without them and remembers, in the partial way he remembers anything, what that was.

The container holds because he keeps building it. It was not designed to. That is the operational truth of the defensive system, and the reason the file's recommendations for any interaction with the subject begin with *do not disturb the prostheses* and end with *do not be present when they fail*.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*A decade-by-decade reconstruction of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept across the documented life. Frameworks invoked: Şar's dissociation-spectrum model (2014, 2022) for the trauma-spectrum core; Main/Solomon disorganized attachment for the interpersonal substrate; Herman's tripartite Complex PTSD model (safety/remembrance/reconnection) for the recovery arcs; Linehan's affect-regulation lens for the dysregulation course; Janet's classical hierarchy of dissociation (primary/secondary/tertiary structural dissociation per van der Hart) for the identity-alteration trajectory.*

---

## Decade 0 — Childhood, ca. 1882–1897 (Alberta, Howlett estate)

**Affect regulation.** Constitutionally fragile baseline — the child is documented (Jenkins, *Origin* #1–6) as asthmatic, allergic, sickly, kept indoors, prone to crying jags and night terrors. Affect is regulated almost entirely *externally*: by Rose, the redheaded servant girl who functions as the de facto attachment figure, and secondarily by Elizabeth Howlett, whose own depressive/psychotic decompensation (she has lost a previous child, is institutionalized intermittently) makes her a *withdrawn* primary caregiver — present, biologically maternal, emotionally absent. John Howlett the elder (the *social* father) is warmer but distant; Thomas Logan (the *biological* father, working the grounds as hired hand) is intermittently violent, charged, and uncategorized in the child's mind. This is the textbook setting for disorganized attachment per Main/Solomon: the caregivers are simultaneously sources of need-meeting and of fear, and the child cannot construct a coherent strategy.

**Cognitive style.** Bookish, observant, internalizing. Pre-trauma James Howlett is *not* the laconic operator he will become; he is verbal, articulate for his age, with a tendency to retreat into reading and into Rose's company. Pattern-recognition is already there in nascent form — the child notices that the household is full of secrets the adults will not name (his parentage, his mother's collapses, Thomas Logan's status). He learns young that perception and naming are different acts, and that the second is dangerous.

**Self-concept.** "Weak." "Sickly." "The fragile one." He has internalized the family's verdict on his body. He is the *boy who must be protected* — a self-concept which the rest of his life will be spent inverting through compulsive role-reversal (he will be the one who protects, never again the one protected).

**Pivotal event (the rupture).** Thomas Logan kills John Howlett in front of the child. The first bone-claw extrusion occurs in the same instant the category of "father" collapses: the man being killed is the social father; the man killing him is the biological father; the man James himself kills in response is therefore *also* his father. Three fathers, one corpse, in seconds. In Janet's framework this is the inaugural structural dissociation — the moment a primary action system (defense) splits off from the apparently-normal personality. The somatic claws are the literal externalization of that split: a defensive subsystem that was *anatomically inside* him and that he did not know about, erupting through the skin. The fact that his first use of his mutation is patricide-of-his-biological-father-while-defending-his-social-father is the etiological signature of every subsequent identity disturbance.

---

## Decade 1 — Adolescence and flight, ca. 1897–1907

**Affect regulation.** Catastrophically reorganized. The accidental killing of Rose by his own claws during the brawl with "Dog" Logan terminates the only durable affect-regulatory relationship of his life so far. He flees, takes the name "Logan" (the killer's name — a self-punitive identity choice that he will not reverse for a century), and disappears into the Yukon. Affect regulation in this period is achieved via *withdrawal from all stimuli that elicit affect*: he lives in mining camps where men do not speak, then leaves the camps for the wilderness itself, living for an unspecified span among a wolf pack. The wolf-pack period (referenced repeatedly across Origin and *Wolverine: The End*) is, clinically, prolonged dissociative absorption — a sustained altered state in which the human-relational apparatus is taken offline and the sensory/predatory apparatus runs the organism.

**Cognitive style.** Concretizes. Verbal-internal cognition atrophies; sensory-tactical cognition expands. He is operating a body whose senses outscale any human's; the cognitive style adapts to the instrument. Language drops out. He thinks, by the end of this decade, in *trails, scents, wind, sightlines* — not sentences.

**Self-concept.** "Animal." The first self-naming. This will become a lifelong self-stigmatizing identity that pre-rejects intimacy and pre-justifies violence. It is not, importantly, false self-concept in the way clinicians usually mean — he *is* operating in a feralized state. The disorder is that he will retain "animal" as the core self-descriptor for the next hundred-plus years, long after the behavioral evidence has shifted.

---

## Decades 2–4 — Reintegration, drift, early combat, ca. 1907–1937

**Affect regulation.** Slowly and partially relearned. Returns to human society in stages; works as a logger, miner, rancher in western Canada and Alaska. Affect is now regulated by *physical exhaustion* (manual labor) and *isolation by trade* (work where men do not require him to speak). Ethanol enters as a regulator in this period — it does not work well on his physiology, so the dose escalates immediately to functionally heavy use, a pattern that will never reverse.

**Cognitive style.** Begins to reintegrate language and tactical thinking. Picks up military-adjacent competencies during the run-up to and through WWI. Develops the laconic verbal style that will be his lifelong public register: economy of words, dry humor used as a distance-regulator. The humor is mature defense (per Vaillant's hierarchy) — already he is using sublimation and humor in calm states while remaining dissociation-prone under threat.

**Self-concept.** Begins to bifurcate. "Animal" remains the core. Layered above it: "soldier," "drifter," "the kind of man who passes through." He is constructing a *socially viable* surface persona over a core identity he believes to be unfit for ordinary life. The bifurcation is functional and will become the lifelong structure.

**Combat exposure.** WWI trench warfare. Behaviorally significant: he encounters mass dissociation as a *generation-wide phenomenon* (shell shock); his own dissociative episodes are statistically normalized in the trench environment in a way they will never be again. This decade is the only one in his life in which his pathology is environmentally congruent.

---

## Decade 5 — Japan, Jasmine Falls, ca. 1937–1941 (the Yashida years)

**Affect regulation.** The single most successful regulatory period of his documented life. Bushidō practice under Bando Saburo is, functionally, a manualized affect-regulation protocol: imposed posture, breath, ritual, meditation, formal etiquette, kata. Where his internal affect-regulation apparatus is broken, Japanese formal practice provides an *external prosthesis* — a complete behavioral envelope that does the regulating from the outside in. This is the same logic as DBT skills training or as monastic Rule: when endogenous regulation fails, externalize the structure totally.

**Cognitive style.** Receives, for the first time since childhood, a *contemplative* training. Bushidō is not anti-tactical — it is hyper-tactical — but it requires sustained attention to interior state and to ethical framing in a way his prior trades did not. He develops what will become his lifelong dual cognition: combat-tactical foreground, ethical-aesthetic background, with the second silently shaping the first. The samurai cognition is laid down in this decade and never leaves him.

**Self-concept.** The *first articulated alternative* to "animal." Bando Saburo and the Yashida household offer him "man-of-the-code," a viable identity in which his violence has form and his life has meaning. He partially accepts it. The relationship with Itsu deepens the offer.

**Termination of period.** Itsu is murdered while pregnant (the act is later retconned to the Winter Soldier, *Wolverine: Origins*). The Rose pattern recurs: the woman he loves dies *because of who he is and what surrounds him*. He does not learn of Daken's survival for decades. The Bushidō prosthesis is not abandoned — it will be carried for the rest of his life — but it is invalidated as a *life-program*. The samurai-ideal becomes from this point forward a private religion held against a self he believes will never be worthy of it.

---

## Decade 6 — WWII, Spanish Civil War interlude, ca. 1936–1945 (overlapping)

**Affect regulation.** Combat as homeostasis. He is most regulated when sanctioned violence is available and structured. The Cap relationship (mutual respect, functional teamwork) shows him still capable of peer bond in adulthood when the peer is morally legible.

**Cognitive style.** Operational, mission-bounded, professionally lethal. The Madripoor partnership with Carol Danvers and Natasha Romanoff (*Uncanny X-Men* #268) shows the lifelong template forming: he works best in small ad-hoc cells with morally serious women, in cities with operational ambiguity. He is poorly suited to mass armies and well-suited to clandestine triads.

**Self-concept.** Stable for the duration of the war. He is *for something*, against a legible enemy, with peers. Postwar collapse will be severe in proportion.

---

## Decades 7–8 — Postwar drift, Team X, ca. 1945–1968

**Affect regulation.** Deteriorates badly. The end of WWII removes the structure; the Bushidō prosthesis is geographically distant; alcohol use escalates. He drifts through CIA-adjacent black-ops work that lacks the moral clarity of the war. Team X (with Sabretooth, Maverick, Mastodon, Silver Fox) provides a peer cell but a corrupt one — the implanted-memory protocols (*Wolverine* vol. 2 #48–50) begin *here*, with his consent functionally engineered.

**Cognitive style.** This is the decade in which he loses the ability to trust his own autobiography. The Silver Fox romance is implanted, partly real, partly false, partly overwritten — he will never reliably know which. Cognitively this produces what I will call *epistemic vigilance toward the self*: he learns to treat his own memories as hostile-source intelligence to be corroborated, not as identity. This is a profoundly adaptive response to his actual epistemic situation and a profoundly disabling one for ordinary selfhood.

**Self-concept.** "Asset." For the first time he is *categorized as a tool by an institution* and has internalized it. The animal-self gains a bureaucratic synonym. This will be the lever Weapon X uses.

---

## Decade 9 — Weapon X, ca. late 1960s/early 1970s (the Windsor-Smith sequence)

**Affect regulation.** Destroyed. The Weapon X procedure — adamantium bonding under partial anesthesia, repeated drugging, chemically and operantly induced berserker states, weaponized deployment against animals and humans under remote control (*Marvel Comics Presents* #72–84) — is iatrogenic catastrophic dissociation. The Professor/Cornelius/Hines triad *explicitly engineer* a split state in which the host is unconscious of what the weapon is doing.

In Şar's framework this is the maximal dose: chronic, agentic, repetitive trauma inflicted by perpetrators whose explicit goal is the production of dissociation. The identity-alteration spectrum that his childhood opened is now driven, by deliberate design, into its severe range.

**Cognitive style.** Reduced for the duration of captivity to peri-traumatic narrowing — perception of the surgical table, of restraints, of the voices over the intercom. Autobiographical cognition is offline. When he escapes, in the berserker fugue that kills the staff, he is operating *entirely* in the defensive action system; the apparently-normal personality is offline for the kill sequence and partially absent from the wilderness flight that follows.

**Self-concept.** Bottoms out. By the time the Hudsons find him naked in the snow, there is essentially no autobiographical self online — he is operating as a frightened predator with no name. The Hudsons (James and Heather) provide the first post-trauma holding environment. In Herman's CPTSD framework this is the *safety* phase, and it is the only adequate safety phase he will receive in his life until Xavier.

---

## Decade 10 — Department H, Alpha Flight, defection to Xavier, ca. early–mid 1970s

**Affect regulation.** Improving from floor, still poor. The Hudsons stabilize him enough to function. Department H provides bureaucratic structure (mission, hierarchy, paychecks) without offering integration — he is, again, an asset. Affect is regulated by the available substitutes: work, alcohol, isolation between deployments.

**Cognitive style.** Re-acquires language, autobiographical narrative (such as it is — heavily fragmented, heavily implanted), tactical competence. Begins to suspect that what he remembers is not what happened.

**Self-concept.** "Government weapon, on loan." When he encounters the Hulk in his first canonical appearance (*Incredible Hulk* #180–182), he is operating as a deployed asset. The defection to Xavier (*Giant-Size X-Men* #1) is, behaviorally, *another flight from handlers* — structurally identical to the flight from the Howlett estate and from Weapon X. The repeated pattern: catastrophic violence → flight from controlling environment → arrival at a holding environment.

---

## Decades 11–13 — Claremont X-Men, ca. 1975–1991

This is the longest documented stretch of relative integration and the most clinically informative.

**Affect regulation — early.** Initial X-Men period: still highly volatile, picks fights with Cyclops as displacement, drinks heavily, takes long solitary leaves. The Jean Grey idealization is *unconsumed longing* — load-bearing precisely because it is not acted on; she functions as a regulator-by-fantasy.

**Affect regulation — middle.** The 1982 Japan limited series (Claremont/Miller) is, biographically, the *attempt to reclaim Jasmine Falls* — to convert the private religion of Bushidō back into a lived program through marriage to Mariko Yashida. The attempt fails for external reasons (Mastermind's interference, Shingen, the broken engagement) and the affect-regulation gains are partially preserved: he returns to the X-Men perceptibly more regulated, with the "be a man, not an animal" formulation now actively held as a self-instruction.

**Affect regulation — late.** Mariko's poisoning death (*Wolverine* vol. 2 #57), delivered by his hand at her request, is the most concentrated repetition of the Rose/Itsu pattern in the canon. The post-Mariko decade shows quantifiable behavioral hardening: more drinking, longer absences, more solo arcs.

**Cognitive style.** This is the decade in which the *teacher* cognition emerges and stabilizes. The Kitty Pryde bond (*Kitty Pryde and Wolverine*, 1984) is the prototype: he discovers that he can transmit survival-cognition to a young person without harming them, that *pedagogical* relating is a mode of attachment that does not activate his catastrophic patterns. The cognitive style during teaching is *patient, granular, anticipatory of failure modes* — utterly unlike his combat cognition and utterly unlike his romantic cognition. It is, behaviorally, the healthiest cognitive register he possesses.

**Self-concept.** Bifurcation matures and stabilizes. The conscious self-statement crystallizes in this period — "the best there is at what I do, and what I do isn't very nice" — which is a fully formed self-stigmatizing identity-script that pre-empts intimacy and pre-justifies violence in a single sentence. *Underneath*, behaviorally evidenced, is a moral conscience strong enough to drive the Mariko arc, the Kitty bond, the Kurt friendship, the loyalty to Xavier. The two layers are now structurally stable: animal-mask above, samurai-ideal below, with the gap between them managed by alcohol and geography. This is the configuration that will hold, with variation, for the next thirty publishing years.

---

## Decade 14 — 1990s: adamantium loss, identity excavation

**Affect regulation.** Severely tested. Magneto's adamantium extraction (*X-Men* #25, 1993) is a somatic re-traumatization — the metal that Weapon X put in is now violently removed, the healing factor catastrophically overdrawn, and he regresses behaviorally (bone-clawed, increasingly feral, the "devolution" arcs). Affect-regulation in this period is the worst since Weapon X itself; he is barely held by the team and frequently absent from it.

**Cognitive style.** *"Logan: A Dog's Life"* / *Wolverine* vol. 2 #48–50 sequence (Hama) is the canonical statement that he can no longer distinguish memory from implant. Cognitive style in this decade is *forensic toward the self* — he is, effectively, his own cold-case investigator, treating his autobiography as a contaminated evidence file. This is genuinely novel cognition for him; it is the beginning of a tertiary-process awareness of his own dissociative structure rather than merely living inside it.

**Self-concept.** Most unstable since Weapon X. The "animal" identity reasserts (bone claws, regressed states); the samurai-ideal recedes; teacher-self is intermittently absent. He is, in this decade, closest to the floor he last touched in the snow with the Hudsons.

---

## Decade 15 — early 2000s: *Origin*, *Enemy of the State*, paternity revelations

**Affect regulation.** *Origin* (2001) restores, narratively, the pre-Weapon X autobiography. Clinically the effect on him is ambiguous — knowing he was James Howlett does not return the regulation that was destroyed; it provides a coherent prequel to the disorder. *Enemy of the State* (Millar) is yet another agentic override — the Hand brainwashes him into killing colleagues. The pattern of *will-overwrite by hostile institution* (Weapon X, Team X, Hand, Hydra, Apocalypse-as-Death, Romulus, later Persephone) is by this decade the central organizing trauma of his adult life, *more* than the originating Rose/Howlett scene. He has now been *taken over* so many times that the experience of authentic agency is itself anxiogenic.

**Cognitive style.** Adds *paternal* cognition — Daken's existence is revealed (*Wolverine: Origins*), and the failure-of-fatherhood becomes a new cognitive preoccupation. He is bad at this. Daken has been raised by enemies specifically to weaponize the paternal wound, and Logan's available paternal cognition is largely defensive-protective (good for adolescent girls in immediate danger, poor for adult sons engineered to hate him).

**Self-concept.** "Failed father" enters the lexicon and does not leave. The samurai-ideal's main private indictment in this decade is paternal: a samurai protects his line; he did not protect Itsu, he did not raise Daken, and he is being shown the bill.

---

## Decade 16 — late 2000s: X-23, *Old Man Logan*

**Affect regulation — X-23 line.** Laura Kinney provides the *reparative* counterpart to Daken: the opportunity to do fatherhood differently, with a young female under direct threat from the institutional-violation apparatus that made him. He handles X-23 with comparative competence — patient, present, pedagogically careful, willing to let her be feral and to teach her the same survival-cognition he taught Kitty and Jubilee. The X-23 mentorship is the most regulated paternal cognition he ever shows.

**Affect regulation — Old Man Logan track.** The *Old Man Logan* presentation (Millar/McNiven, 2008) is the *inverse symptom of the same disorder*. Mysterio tricks him into slaughtering the X-Men under the perceptual hallucination that they were villains. The response — fifty years of complete behavioral inhibition, vow of nonviolence, refusal to extrude the claws — is, clinically, profound depressive and dissociative shutdown layered on the CPTSD core. The conscious self has determined that the weapon-self is too contaminated to be allowed motor access; the cost is near-total agentic suppression, anhedonia, and a flat affect that meets episodic MDD criteria as a trauma-driven secondary syndrome.

**Cognitive style.** The split widens. In the prime continuity he is functioning at career-best pedagogical capacity (X-23, the Jean Grey School in subsequent years); in the *Old Man* variant he is functioning at career-worst behavioral inhibition. Both presentations are the *same disorder* solving its insoluble problem differently — one by sublimation into teaching, the other by total motor inhibition.

**Self-concept.** Dual ledger formalizes. He explicitly thinks of himself in two ways now and knows he does — the headmaster/mentor self and the unredeemable killer self. The Bushidō ideal is invoked openly more often in this decade than in any previous; it is held as standard, not as program.

---

## Decade 17 — 2010s: Jean Grey School, *Death*, *Return*

**Affect regulation.** Headmaster-era Wolverine is, behaviorally, the highest-functioning version of him on record. The Jean Grey School institutionalizes the teacher-self; *running a school for traumatized mutant adolescents* is the literal occupational embodiment of his reparative function. Affect-regulation is at lifetime best because the structure of the role *requires* regulation and the population under his care *deserves* it.

**Death of Wolverine** (2014) — drowns in adamantium, encased in the metal that has defined him. The image is exact: the iatrogenic substance that made him a weapon becomes his sarcophagus. Clinically, the *Death* arc reads as the long-deferred completion of an unconscious wish — the unkillable man is finally killed by the substance of his unkillability.

**Return of Wolverine** (2018) — resurrection with renewed memory fragmentation and Persephone-implanted kill triggers. Cognitively this is the *nth* iteration of the same structural fact: institutional actors implant compulsions, he must excavate them under fire. The forensic-toward-the-self cognition that began in the 1990s is now his routine operating mode.

**Self-concept.** "Teacher" rises to near-parity with "animal" in the conscious lexicon. He does not believe he has earned it; he occupies it because students require it; the occupation, over time, does some of the work that belief would have done.

---

## Decade 18 — Krakoan era, 2019+

**Affect regulation.** Institutionalized at the species level. Resurrection protocols mean death/dissociation is now a normative cycle the culture supports rather than a


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Section 4 of the UATU dossier. Cross-reference §1 (longitudinal history), §3 (psychological structure), and clinical provenance Şar (2014, 2022).*

---

## 4.0 Framing the Assessment

A psychiatric workup on this subject has to be built differently from a standard intake. Four facts dictate the methodology:

1. **The chart spans ~130 chronological years and ~50 publication years.** Symptom course can be tracked at a granularity unavailable in clinical practice. We are not inferring chronicity — we are reading it off a continuous record.
2. **The autobiographical record is corrupted at the source.** The patient himself cannot reliably distinguish autobiographical memory from material implanted by Weapon X, Team X, the Hand, Hydra, Romulus, and Apocalypse. Standard self-report instruments (CAPS-5, SCID-D, DES-II) would produce data with a known and quantifiable validity problem; the corruption itself is diagnostically informative but must be controlled for.
3. **The somatic substrate is non-normative.** Healing factor, hypersenses, retarded aging, and an adamantium-bonded skeleton mean that physiological correlates of psychiatric phenomena (HPA tone, autonomic reactivity, hepatic load, sleep architecture) will not behave per textbook. Symptom *quantity* criteria (alcohol units, injury severity, sleep deprivation tolerance) require rescaling; symptom *function* criteria do not.
4. **The trauma exposure is at or beyond the maximum tolerated dose described in the human literature.** This is relevant because it pushes the differential toward the dissociative spectrum (Şar 2014) rather than toward narrower trauma categories — chronicity, agentic violation, and developmental onset are all maximally present.

With those qualifications declared, the picture is, I will argue, coherent — and the coherence is itself the strongest piece of diagnostic evidence.

---

## 4.1 Primary Diagnosis: Complex PTSD (ICD-11 6B41)

I lead with CPTSD rather than PTSD because the DSM-5-TR PTSD category, while met, is grossly insufficient as a primary descriptor. The ICD-11's separation of CPTSD captures the developmental, repeated, agentic-violation phenotype this subject embodies. All six required clusters are present, with overdetermination.

**A. Exposure criteria (CPTSD A).** The threshold requires "an event or series of events of an extremely threatening or horrific nature, most commonly prolonged or repetitive events from which escape is difficult or impossible." Logan's exposure history exceeds this threshold by orders of magnitude:

- *Developmental:* the Howlett massacre and the contemporaneous revelation of his biological paternity (*Origin* #1–6) — single-event onset with category-collapsing meaning (the father-figure dies, the killer is the bio-father, the protective servant is the first kill).
- *Adolescent/young adult:* feral years; loss of Rose by his own claws — accidental fatal harm to first love object.
- *Adulthood — repeated:* two world wars, Spanish Civil War, postwar covert ops, Madripoor, Jasmine Falls and the murder of Itsu, Team X with documented sustained memory implantation, Weapon X (the indexical event), Department H handling, Hand brainwashing in *Enemy of the State*, Romulus' century-long manipulation, Apocalypse's overwrite into Death, Persephone's kill triggers in *Return of Wolverine*.
- *Iatrogenic and agentic*: the majority of these are not impersonal disasters but acts of will by identifiable persons — Cornelius, Hines, the Professor, Romulus, Apocalypse, Mystique, Mysterio. Agentic-violation trauma is the canonical etiological signature for the dissociative spectrum (Şar 2014).

**B. Core PTSD triad — present and chronic.**

- *Re-experiencing:* nightmares (recurring across Claremont, Hama, Aaron runs), olfactory-cued flashbacks (the cigar/blood/specific perfume triggers, repeatedly depicted), and the structurally unique presentation of *re-experiencing material the patient cannot verify as autobiographical*. He has intrusive memories he must then forensically assess. Treat this as re-experiencing with secondary derealization layered on top.
- *Avoidance:* the wilderness exile pattern is the macro-form (Yukon, Canadian Rockies, Madripoor disappearances, post-*Old Man Logan* withdrawal). The micro-form is topical avoidance — refusal to discuss Itsu, Mariko, the Weapon X facility, except under duress. Avoidance is partial, not phobic; he can be coaxed onto the material by trusted persons (Xavier, Jean), which preserves treatment access.
- *Hyperarousal:* anatomically reinforced and therefore unremitting. The hypersenses mean the autonomic system is being cued by olfactory and auditory data the conscious self has not yet processed. Startle response is suppressed by training but reactivity is preserved. Sleep is shallow and brief; he wakes claws-out, which is documented across multiple writers and constitutes a behavioral marker of hyperarousal-related parasomnia.

**C. CPTSD-specific disturbances (the three that distinguish CPTSD from PTSD).**

1. *Disturbances in affect regulation.* The berserker state is the apex presentation; below it, a chronic floor of irritability and a documented inability to titrate response between low-level annoyance and lethal force once a specific threshold is crossed. The alcohol intake is the affect-regulation symptom externalized. The Bushidō practice and meditation periods are the *attempted* regulation strategy — note that he sought this prosthesis out himself in Jasmine Falls, which is consistent with insight into the deficit.
2. *Negative self-concept.* The "animal" self-description, "the best there is at what I do, and what I do isn't very nice," and the persistent pre-emptive rejection of intimacy ("you deserve better") constitute a stable, ego-syntonic negative self-concept that has resisted decades of contrary evidence (Xavier's faith, Jean's love, Kitty's devotion). The negativity is not depressive cognition — it is *identity-level* and behaviorally enforced.
3. *Disturbances in relationships.* The approach-withdrawal cycle with every romantic object, the protective-then-explosive pattern with peers, and the inability to sustain integration into any institution that has not earned a years-long trust audit. He can form bonds; he cannot trust them to survive him, which is the relational expression of belief #2 in §5.

CPTSD is met cleanly. The diagnosis carries an implicit prognostic and treatment frame (phase-based, stabilization-first, trauma processing only after affect regulation is secured) that matches what we observe him doing for himself across the canon — the Japan periods, the mentorship roles, the codified rituals are the patient's *self-administered* phase-one stabilization work.

---

## 4.2 Co-Primary Diagnosis: Dissociative Disorder, mixed amnestic and identity-alteration features

Per Şar (2014, 2022), dissociative amnesia, depersonalization, derealization, identity confusion, and identity alteration constitute a single severity spectrum produced by chronic developmental/traumatic stress, with the highest reported childhood-trauma frequency of any psychiatric condition. I name this co-primary, not secondary, because in this subject the dissociative phenomenology is not a downstream PTSD feature — it is a parallel, independently severe, structurally organizing condition. Suppressing the CPTSD label would still leave a stand-alone dissociative disorder of high severity. Suppressing the dissociative label would leave a CPTSD picture that cannot account for the berserker amnesias or the identity-mode switching.

The Şar framing is specifically the correct lens because it refuses to silo "rage," "amnesia," and "identity alteration" as comorbidities. In this subject they are one syndrome with one etiology.

**Symptom mapping onto the spectrum:**

- *Dissociative amnesia (DSM-5 300.12; ICD-11 6B61).* Multi-decade autobiographical gaps documented since Wein/Cockrum (1974); selective amnesia for traumatic episodes (Weapon X facility content surfaces in fragments across decades); and the unique *systematized* amnesia from Team X memory implantation, where false memories occupy the slot true memories would. The *House of M* sequence — where suppressed memory returns *whole* and he becomes briefly incapacitated by grief — is a near-clinical demonstration of how much material the amnesia was buffering.
- *Depersonalization / derealization (DSM-5 300.6; ICD-11 6B66).* Repeatedly self-described: he watches himself act, particularly in or just after a berserker episode; the body that heals is experienced as not-quite-his-own; the "animal" self-talk is partly a depersonalization artifact codified into identity.
- *Identity confusion.* He cannot reliably answer the question "who are you?" with a stable autobiographical narrative. He has organized around the question rather than answering it. *Origin* was, narratively, the answer; clinically, the post-*Origin* canon shows that recovered memory did not resolve the confusion, which is consistent with the dissociative literature — identity confusion in chronic dissociation does not remit upon memory recovery alone.
- *Identity alteration (the contested feature).* The James Howlett / Logan / Patch / Weapon X / Death sequence is *not* alias-for-cover. Each is a behaviorally distinct mode with characteristic affect, posture, vocal register, threat threshold, and partial mutual amnesia. "Patch" in Madripoor is not Logan-in-disguise; he holds different attitudes, different vices, different relationships. "Death" under Apocalypse was a near-total override. The berserker state is the most acute identity-alteration episode — a circumscribed mode with motoric automatism, narrowed or absent declarative consciousness, and post-episodic amnesia.
- *Acute dissociative reactions.* The berserker episodes belong here categorically. Their phenomenology — sudden onset under threat-overload, altered consciousness, automatic motor behavior, post-event amnesia, remorse — is the classical acute dissociative presentation, not an explosive anger episode.

**Specific category placement.** I place him at **Other Specified Dissociative Disorder** (DSM-5 300.15) / ICD-11 6B65 — "dissociative disorder with mixed amnestic and identity-alteration features, on the chronic complex dissociative end of the Şar spectrum." This is deliberate: I am not diagnosing DID (see differential, §4.5).

---

## 4.3 Secondary Diagnosis: Alcohol Use Disorder, moderate–severe by functional criteria

DSM-5 quantity/frequency criteria misapply because tolerance is anatomically inflated by the healing factor — he must consume well past lethal human thresholds to achieve any anxiolytic effect. The functional criteria, however, are met cleanly:

- *Use to manage affect:* documented across every era; drinking spikes after dissociative episodes, after losses, after memory intrusions.
- *Continued use despite consequences:* social and occupational consequences are present (judgment in calm only, never in alcohol-blunted state in his case — he uses *for* the blunting), and the consequences accrue at the relational level.
- *Tolerance:* extreme and metabolically forced.
- *Larger amounts than intended / unsuccessful efforts to cut down:* the Japan periods are partial attempts; success is partial.
- *Craving:* the cigar-and-whiskey ritual is overlearned and cued; this is a craving signature.

I read the AUD as a downstream symptom of the CPTSD/dissociative complex — self-medication of intolerable affect and intrusive material — and would expect it to attenuate, not remit, with successful trauma stabilization. It does not warrant primary status, but it does warrant naming, because untreated AUD is a major predictor of poor CPTSD outcome and because the substance use is itself shaping behavior (sleep, judgment in non-combat contexts, intimate availability).

---

## 4.4 Symptom Presentation in Behavior — A Cross-Walk

A diagnostic list is sterile without behavior. The following maps named symptoms onto observable patterns documented in the longitudinal record:

| Symptom (clinical) | Behavioral expression (observed) |
|---|---|
| Re-experiencing | Wakes claws-out; freezes briefly at specific olfactory cues (specific perfumes, antiseptic, particular gun-oil); flinches at surgical settings; cannot remain in laboratories or restraint apparatus without escalation. |
| Avoidance | Refuses certain geographies (the Weapon X site, certain Tokyo districts post-Mariko, the Yukon at certain seasons); changes the subject with physical movement, not verbal redirect; uses humor as topical deflection. |
| Hyperarousal | Sits with back to wall; will not sleep facing a door; tracks all exits within seconds of room entry; sleeps in 90-minute cycles, easily roused; quick to claws-out on unexpected touch even from intimates. |
| Affect dysregulation | Sardonic verbal warnings as a self-titration attempt; cigar ritual as a deliberate slow-breathing prosthesis; the threshold to lethal force, once crossed, is non-recoverable mid-episode. |
| Negative self-concept | Self-stigmatizing speech ("I'm not fit for this"); refusal of leadership positions even when competent; pre-emptive distancing from new intimates; the "animal" frame as identity ballast. |
| Relational disturbance | Approach-withdrawal cycles measured in weeks to months with romantic objects; durable peer bonds only with persons who have earned years of trust audit; protective generativity reserved for adolescents under his explicit guardianship. |
| Dissociative amnesia | Refers to his own past in conditional tense ("if that even happened"); keeps physical mementoes as memory anchors because internal memory is untrusted; cross-checks his recollections against others' (Xavier, Creed) before accepting them. |
| Identity alteration | Distinct vocal register, posture, and ethical floor in "Patch" mode vs. X-Men field operator vs. Bushidō student vs. berserker; partial amnesia between modes, more pronounced for the berserker episodes. |
| Depersonalization | Observes own wounds with clinical detachment; treats own body as instrument rather than self; the healing factor reinforces this — the body that repairs itself is hard to inhabit as self. |
| AUD-functional | Cigar-and-whiskey ritual; bar as preferred public space; drinks alone after kills; sober only when handling children, which is itself diagnostic. |

---

## 4.5 Differential Diagnosis — What Logan Is NOT, and Why

The differential is where diagnostic discipline is enforced. Each exclusion below is argued from positive behavioral evidence, not from absence.

### 4.5.1 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder (DSM-5 301.7 / ICD-11 6D11.2)

The surface presentation — chronic violence, instability of residence and employment, disregard for legal authority — invites ASPD. The diagnosis fails on every required internal criterion:

- *Empathy:* demonstrably present and operative, particularly with the vulnerable. Reparative care of Rogue when she was a fugitive enemy combatant; the years of patient instruction of Jubilee with no instrumental return; the deliberate gentleness with X-23 in the face of her hostility.
- *Remorse:* present, chronic, and behaviorally costly. The post-berserker shame cycle, the lifelong guilt about Rose and Itsu and Mariko, the *Old Man Logan* fifty-year nonviolence vow — these are remorse acted on.
- *Internalized moral code:* the Bushidō ideal is not performance; it is held when it costs him and abandoned only under dissociative override.
- *Capacity for durable loyalty:* the Xavier bond, the Rogers bond, the Kurt Wagner bond — multi-decade fidelity inconsistent with ASPD's relational pattern.

The canon helpfully includes the ASPD control case in **Victor Creed (Sabretooth)**: same hypersenses, similar trauma exposure, similar combat training, no empathy, no remorse, no code, no loyalty. The two characters were built to make this distinction visible. The contrast is diagnostic.

### 4.5.2 Not Dissociative Identity Disorder (DSM-5 300.14 / ICD-11 6B64)

DID requires *two or more distinct personality states with marked discontinuity in sense of self and agency, accompanied by alterations in affect, behavior, consciousness, memory, perception, cognition, and/or sensory-motor functioning,* with the states having elaborated, autonomous self-experience. Logan's identity-alteration phenomena fall short:

- The modes (Patch, Howlett, the Bushidō student, the berserker, Death-under-Apocalypse) lack autonomous, elaborated biographies. They are state-dependent behavioral configurations, not personalities with separate names-for-themselves and separate first-person narratives.
- Inter-mode amnesia is *partial and porous,* not the dense compartmentalization of DID. He retains general awareness across modes even when specific episodes are amnestic.
- The induction of modes (Death, Hand-controlled) by external agents argues for a high-dissociability substrate that adversaries can exploit, not for an internally organized alter system.

OSDD on the high-end of the Şar spectrum is the more parsimonious and more accurate placement.

### 4.5.3 Not Intermittent Explosive Disorder (DSM-5 312.34)

IED requires that the explosive episodes not be better explained by another mental disorder. They are better explained here — as acute dissociative reactions within the CPTSD/dissociative complex. Additionally, IED episodes are typically *ego-dystonic discrete events in an otherwise non-violent life*; Logan's life is structured around violence, the episodes have characteristic dissociative phenomenology (consciousness alteration, post-event amnesia) absent in classical IED, and the triggers are trauma-specific (Sabretooth's scent, the Weapon X cue set, harm to a protected adolescent) rather than diffuse frustration-aggression cues. IED is the wrong shelf.

### 4.5.4 Not Major Depressive Disorder as primary

The *Old Man Logan* presentation does meet MDD criteria episodically — anhedonia, psychomotor retardation, hopelessness, vegetative signs adjusted for healing factor, suicidal ideation expressed as a wish for finality. But it is trauma-driven (the Mysterio-induced massacre is the proximate cause), context-locked (resolves when the protective stance becomes possible again), and does not recur as an autonomous mood disorder across decades. It is best read as a trauma-related depressive reaction within the CPTSD frame, not as comorbid MDD. The lifelong baseline is dysthymic-flavored but does not cleanly meet Persistent Depressive Disorder criteria either — affect is too reactive, anhedonia incomplete (mentorship, combat skill, certain sensory pleasures remain rewarding).

### 4.5.5 Not Bipolar I or II

No discrete hypomanic or manic episodes meeting duration or symptom-cluster criteria. The affective oscillations are *trauma-cued and event-bounded,* not autonomous, not cyclic, not associated with the cognitive expansiveness, decreased sleep need (against a normal baseline), or goal-directed hyperactivity of mania. Behavioral activation in combat is task-specific, not manic. The differential is worth naming because the *amplitude* of his affective swings invites the question; the *structure* refutes it.

### 4.5.6 Not Schizophrenia-spectrum disorder

No primary psychotic features. The intrusive memories are trauma-intrusive, not hallucinatory; the identity disturbances are dissociative, not delusional (he does not believe he is multiple persons — he is uncertain which one he is, which is a different epistemic posture). No formal thought disorder. No negative symptoms in the schizophrenia sense.

### 4.5.7 Not Substance-Induced Disorder as primary

The AUD is consequent to, not causal of, the CPTSD/dissociative complex. Symptom presentation predates sustained alcohol use (the feral years, the Howlett-era dissociation) and persists in sobriety attempts. Substance-induced framing is excluded.

### 4.5.8 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

The relational instability and identity disturbance superficially invite BPD. They are better explained by CPTSD plus dissociative disorder: the identity disturbance is dissociatively-structured rather than affective-instability-structured; the relational pattern is *approach-withdrawal organized around a load-bearing belief about lethality to intimates*, not the abandonment-terror pattern of BPD; chronic emptiness is present but is dissociative-flavored (depersonalization) not BPD-flavored. Self-harm is absent in the BPD sense (his recklessness toward his body is parasuicidal-equivalent but is rationalized by the healing factor and serves a different intrapsychic function — testing finitude, not regulating affect through pain).

### 4.5.9 Not a primary anxiety disorder

Hyperarousal is anatomically and traumatically driven, not anxiety-disorder driven. No specific phobias, no panic with autonomic phenomenology distinct from threat-cued hyperarousal, no generalized worry cognition. The differential is brief because the evidence is brief.

### 4.5.10 Not Adjustment Disorder

Excluded by chronicity, severity, and the multiplicity of qualifying events. Adjustment Disorder is a residual category for sub-threshold reactions to identifiable stressors; this subject is supra-threshold to every relevant criterion.

---

## 4.6 Comorbidity Map

The diagnostic picture is best represented as a layered complex rather than a list:

- **Layer 1 (etiological core):** chronic developmental and repeated adult trauma with maximal agentic-violation loading.
- **Layer 2 (primary psychiatric):** CPTSD + chronic complex dissociative disorder (OSDD-spectrum). These are co-primary and mutually reinforcing — the dissociative architecture buffers what the CPTSD cannot tolerate, and the dissociative episodes generate new traumatic material the CPTSD must then process.
- **Layer 3 (secondary):** Alcohol Use Disorder, moderate-severe by functional criteria; episodic trauma-related depressive reactions meeting MDD criteria in *Old Man Logan*-type contexts; trauma-related parasomnia (claws-out waking).
- **Layer 4 (somatically driven contributors):** sensory-overload-related hyperarousal (anatomical, not psychiatric, but psychiatrically consequential); chronic adamantium load with intermittent toxicity exposure events.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Section 6 of the UATU dossier. Exhaustive catalog of observable tells, micro-patterns, and decision habits across the full state-space of his life. Granularity is the point: this is the section a watcher uses to predict him in the next ninety seconds.*

---

## 6.1 Baseline / Calm State

Calm in him is not absence of arousal; it is *managed* arousal at a level most humans would call vigilance. The baseline tells:

- **Stance.** Weight slightly back on the heels, shoulders dropped but not relaxed, hands loose and *open* — fingers never interlaced, never in pockets past the first knuckle. The dorsal hands are kept available. He does not cross his arms in any setting where exits are not yet logged; when he does cross them, the exits are logged.
- **Eyeline.** Habitual scan in a flattened figure-eight: doorway, nearest civilian, nearest object that could become a weapon, ceiling vents/rafters, doorway again. Cycle period roughly six to nine seconds in a public room, shortens to three or four in an unfamiliar one. He does not appear to be looking; the scan is peripheral.
- **Olfactory micro-tell.** A short, single inhalation through the nose on entering any room — under a second, often masked by clearing his throat or by the cigar. He is taking the room's olfactory inventory. A second sniff, half a beat later, means something in the first inventory did not parse.
- **Speech.** Clipped, declarative, contractions heavy ("ain't," "didn't," "gonna"). Drops articles under stress, retains them in calm. The Canadian English substrate surfaces in vowels (*about*, *sorry*) when fatigued or drunk; suppresses in formal company. Calls men "bub," "pal," "slick"; calls women he respects by name and women he doesn't by "darlin'" — the latter is *not* flirtation, it is distancing.
- **Cigar discipline.** In calm states the cigar is lit, drawn from at regular intervals (~30–45 seconds), ash tapped with the thumb against the index finger rather than against a tray. The ash on the floor is, itself, a small territorial mark.
- **Drink.** Beer in calm public settings, paced; whiskey neat when alone or grieving; sake when in any Japanese context, which carries ritual weight for him and is *never* drunk to excess.
- **Resting hands.** When seated, dominant hand under the table or behind the hip — the claw hand kept out of casual sightlines. This is unconscious and almost invariant.
- **Sleep.** Light, polyphasic when on operations; four to five hours when settled, often on the floor or in a chair rather than a bed unless the bed is in a defensible room. Wakes fully alert, no transition. Will not sleep with his back to a door.
- **Reading.** Yes, despite the persona — Japanese poetry, military history, the occasional pulp Western. Reads with the book held low so the eyeline stays on the room.

## 6.2 Low-Stakes Social

- **Bars** are his preferred social terrain because they pre-script the rules. He sits at the corner of the bar, not the middle; back to the wall, sightline on the door, bartender between him and the till. Tips in cash, always over twenty percent, because he wants to be remembered as easy and forgotten as a face.
- **With strangers** he uses a downshifted register — slower, friendlier, almost rural — that lowers the temperature of any room. This is deliberate camouflage; the energy cost shows later as irritability.
- **Pool, darts, cards.** Plays competently below his actual capacity to avoid attention; will let a local win the second game. The decision to *stop* downshifting is a tell that the encounter has gone operational.
- **Humor.** Dry, self-deprecating, often at the expense of his own height, age, or hair. Almost never punches down at someone present. Punches up at authority figures reflexively, even allies (Cyclops, Xavier, Rogers) — this is affection coded as insult.
- **Physical contact.** Initiates rarely; receives stiffly from adults, naturally from children and from a small inner circle (Kurt's shoulder-clap, Ororo's brief embrace, Kitty's hug). Pat on the back from strangers will produce a quarter-second freeze he then covers.

## 6.3 Stress (Sub-Threat)

The shift from calm to stressed is not the comic-book teeth-bare; it is quieter and earlier.

- **First tell:** the cigar stops being drawn from. It is held, sometimes goes out, is not relit. The hand around it tightens.
- **Second tell:** the figure-eight scan shortens and *locks* — repeated returns to a single point in the room. The point is the threat vector he has identified before he has consciously identified it.
- **Third tell:** breathing drops into the diaphragm, audibly slower, deeper. He is oxygenating.
- **Verbal:** sentences shorten. Contractions thicken. The "bub" register replaces names. Sardonic register replaces friendly register. Warnings are given exactly twice and are explicit: "*Don't.*" "*Walk away.*" There is no third warning.
- **Postural:** weight shifts forward onto the balls of the feet; the dominant hand drifts to mid-line, fingers curled but not fisted. The non-dominant hand goes to a position that protects civilians (between him and a child, or pushing a stranger behind him without looking).
- **Decision habit:** under sub-threat stress he prefers *de-escalation by withdrawal* — he will leave a bar, abandon a meal, walk out of a briefing — rather than escalate. The withdrawal is mis-read as fear or sulk; it is in fact his most disciplined behavior. He has learned, over a century, that he is the most dangerous thing in most rooms, and his ethical baseline is to remove himself from rooms where he might be needed too easily.

## 6.4 Threat / Combat-Imminent

- **Pre-extrusion micro-tell.** Half a beat before claws come out: a small flexion of the wrists, fingers extending then curling, and a brief downward glance at the hand — checking the angle. To an experienced observer this is a quarter-second window.
- **The sound.** *SNIKT* is canonical; behaviorally, he sometimes extrudes only one claw, sometimes two, rarely all three on warning. Three claws out without target is escalation theatre. Two claws is genuine warning. One claw is intimacy with the threat — usually a held knife to a throat, used in interrogation rather than killing.
- **Pain management.** Extrusion lacerates the dorsal hand; he never visibly registers the pain on extrusion in public. In private, after combat, the small wince when he flexes is observable.
- **Verbal warnings.** Cease entirely once claws are out. He does not banter mid-combat with serious adversaries. He banters with Sabretooth, which is a separate ritual (see 6.13).
- **Combat decision-tree.** Threat assessment in order: (1) civilians present? — if yes, dominant priority is geometry, moving the fight away from them. (2) Allies' positions? — he maps and protects flanks unprompted. (3) Adversary capability? — he tests with a probing engagement before committing. (4) Lethal or non-lethal? — *defaults non-lethal against humans* unless they have crossed specific lines (harm to children, Hand/Hydra/Weapon X affiliation, attack on a named loved one). This default is poorly publicized but consistent across canon.
- **Movement.** Low center of gravity, short steps, never crosses his feet. Uses verticality more than most fighters his size — he goes *up* (tables, walls, rafters) earlier than expected because his density (adamantium skeleton) makes downward force devastating and his healing makes falls trivial.
- **Olfactory tracking mid-combat.** He fights partially with eyes closed in dense melee or smoke — the eyelid flutter is a tell that he has switched to scent-led targeting.

## 6.5 Threshold-Breach / Berserker State

Distinct from threat-state. Triggers are specific and stable:

- **Trigger set:** (a) harm or imminent harm to a protected young person; (b) olfactory recognition of Sabretooth, Hand pheromones, or specific Weapon X personnel; (c) restraint plus pain plus chemical (the Weapon X re-enactment cocktail); (d) discovery of a fresh memory implant or compulsion.
- **Onset signs (the last warning anyone gets):** the eyes lose their tracking saccades and *fix*; breathing goes shallow and rapid; a low sub-vocal growl that he is not aware of producing; a complete cessation of speech; pupils dilate even in bright light.
- **During:** motor automatism — efficient, economical, lethal, with no banter and no facial affect. Combatants describe him as "quiet," which is the diagnostic feature. He will pursue past tactical sense. He will not distinguish surrender. He has, in canon, killed adversaries who had dropped weapons; he does not remember doing so.
- **Termination:** typically external — a trusted voice (Xavier telepathically, Jean historically, Kurt physically, Kitty by name), or the complete absence of remaining targets. Self-termination is rare and slow.
- **Aftermath behaviors (invariant):** (1) brief disorientation, looks at his own hands as if unfamiliar; (2) retracts claws and flexes fingers; (3) physically withdraws from the scene — walks out, often without speaking; (4) seeks alcohol within the hour; (5) seeks solitude within the day; (6) seeks wilderness within the week if the episode was severe.

## 6.6 Intimacy — Romantic

- **Approach pattern.** Slow, indirect, often initiated by the woman. He stages himself nearby — leans on doorframes, shares cigarettes, offers small competences (fixes a bike, walks her home) — without verbal courtship. The verbal register goes *quieter*, not flirtier.
- **First touch.** Almost always her hand on his first. When he initiates, it is the back of his knuckles to her cheek or jaw — the *outside* of the hand, the non-claw surface. This is unconscious and significant.
- **Sexual register.** Reported (Mariko, Yukio, Domino, Jean in alternate timelines, Storm in some) as attentive, considerably gentler than the persona predicts, somewhat reverent. Aftercare is competent. He does not stay the whole night unless the relationship has duration.
- **Withdrawal pattern.** Triggered by: her expressing future-plans; her being threatened on his account; his own dream-cycle producing a Rose/Itsu/Mariko intrusion. The withdrawal is geographical — he leaves, often without a conversation, often with a note. The pattern is so consistent it constitutes informed consent for anyone who knows him; he is, in his own framework, refusing to put her in the death-position.
- **Verbal declaration.** Rare. When it comes it is plain and once. He does not repeat it. The absence of repetition is misread as cooling; it is in fact reverence — he treats the words as load-bearing and refuses to wear them out.

## 6.7 Intimacy — Surrogate-Paternal (the most regulated mode)

This is the cleanest behavioral zone in his entire repertoire. With Kitty, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, X-23, and the rotating cast of adolescents he has shepherded:
