- **First-meet protocol.** Gruffness as test. He is brusque on purpose, watches whether the girl flinches, complies, or pushes back. He invests in the ones who push back.
- **Pedagogy.** Practical, never abstract. Knife handling, how to fall, how to read a room, how to lie convincingly, how to drink without getting drunk, how to sleep in a strange place, how to leave a city quickly. He is teaching them how to survive *him*, structurally — how to survive a world with people like him in it.
- **Physical affection.** Hand on the crown of the head; one-armed shoulder-pull; rarely a full embrace, and when it comes it is brief and tight. He does not pick them up after the first year of knowing them — respects the line where they stop being children.
- **Discipline.** Cold disappointment, never raised voice. The withdrawal of approval is the punishment.
- **Defense of.** Total and without proportion. He has crossed continents, defied teams, and broken sworn allegiances for a girl in this category. The behavior is over-determined and exploitable.
- **Letting go.** He performs *graduation* deliberately — a moment, usually private, where he tells the girl she does not need him anymore. He believes this. He then maintains contact at a reduced cadence and re-engages immediately when called.

## 6.8 Grief

- **Acute phase (hours to days).** Goes still. Cigar stops being smoked. Drink increases sharply. Speech reduces to monosyllables. Does not eat. Does not sleep — sits up with the body when possible, or with an object belonging to the deceased.
- **Funeral conduct.** Attends, stands at the back, leaves before social reception. Drinks afterward alone. If a sword or knife belonging to the deceased exists, he cleans it. If a debt is owed, he settles it without announcement.
- **Sub-acute phase (weeks).** Geographic flight. Canada, Japan, the high desert, or wilderness in whichever country he is closest to. Subsists minimally, hunts, drinks less in wilderness than in cities — the wilderness is the actual medicine, the alcohol is the urban substitute.
- **Chronic phase (years/decades).** Names get folded into a private list he visits in solitude — graveside if possible, or a chosen landscape if not. He performs small annual rituals: a drink, a cigar burned down without smoking, sometimes a written line. These rituals are invisible to almost everyone in his life.
- **Anniversaries.** He remembers them with unusual precision *despite* his amnestic substrate, which suggests the grief memories are differently encoded — possibly because they are the autobiographical data he has *chosen* to verify against external evidence, and therefore trusts.

## 6.9 Victory

He does not celebrate. The behavioral pattern after a successful operation is almost identical to the pattern after a failed one, which is itself diagnostic.

- **Immediate post-action:** retracts claws, checks teammates by eyeline, walks a perimeter, finds his own gear and resets it. Will field-strip a knife, re-roll a jacket, re-pack a bag before he sits.
- **Verbal:** a single dry remark, often deflationary ("Could've gone worse." "Drinks are on Summers."). Refuses extended debrief; will give tactical report and leave.
- **Reward-seeking:** absent. He does not seek praise and visibly discomforts when given it formally. Will accept a drink bought for him; will not accept a medal without a fight.
- **Internal marker:** the cigar is *relit* after victory and smoked to completion. This is as close as he comes to a celebratory tell.

## 6.10 Defeat

- **Tactical defeat (combat lost, mission failed):** flat affect, no recrimination of teammates, takes more than his share of blame in the debrief. Plans the next attempt before the wounds close.
- **Moral defeat (he was used, manipulated, made to do harm):** the deeper failure mode. He withdraws, drinks heavily, considers and sometimes attempts self-removal from a team. The *Old Man Logan* presentation is this state taken to its terminus — full behavioral inhibition, vow of non-violence, depressive shutdown. The vow is the symptom, not the cure.
- **Personal defeat (loss of a loved one despite his presence):** see 6.8. The grief and defeat circuits are the same circuit.

## 6.11 Interrogation — As Subject

- **Resistance posture.** Silence by default. Will *talk* — banter, profanity, deflection — to mask which silence is meaningful. Skilled interrogators learn to ignore the talk and watch the breath and the eyes.
- **Pain tolerance.** Effectively infinite by ordinary metrics. He has been trained, through a century of injury, to use pain as a clock — counting his breaths between waves. Pain alone does not break him.
- **Vulnerabilities (the file's red entries):** chemical disinhibition (specific Weapon X / Hand cocktails that suppress healing), prolonged sensory deprivation (cuts off the hyperacute senses he is anatomically dependent on for orientation), implanted-memory threats (*"this conversation isn't even happening, Logan"*), and harm to a third party in the room. The last is the most reliable.
- **Tell under successful coercion:** the breathing changes from the slow count to a shallow, uneven pattern; the eyes go to middle distance; the hands go flat on the surface in front of him. He has stopped resisting and is waiting for an opening.

## 6.12 Interrogation — As Operator

- **Style.** Quiet, close, single claw extended and held still — not used. He uses the *fact* of himself as the pressure. Voice drops half an octave; questions are short and repeated verbatim until answered.
- **Threshold.** Will not torture. Will threaten credibly and execute the threat only against targets that meet his lethal-engagement criteria (see 6.4). The credibility is what does the work.
- **Reads lies** by olfaction (cortisol shift), micro-expression, and breath. Estimated false-negative rate near zero against unmodified humans; degraded against trained operators and against telepaths.

## 6.13 With Sabretooth (Special Case)

- The ritual is the most stable relationship in his life and behaves accordingly: *predictable*. He banters with Creed in ways he banters with no one else — full sentences, taunts, mock-affection — because the encounter is *known*. He knows the choreography, and so does Creed.
- He fights Creed at a higher level of personal investment and a *lower* level of dissociation than he fights Weapon X personnel. The hatred is integrated. The fight does not produce the berserker state as reliably as proximity-to-Hand does, which is counter-intuitive and diagnostic — Creed is metabolized, the institutional perpetrators are not.
- He marks birthdays. The annual attempted-murder has, in his framework, the structure of a holiday.

## 6.14 With Authority

- **Default:** insubordinate. Will not stand at attention. Will not call a superior "sir" without irony. Will arrive late to briefings as a baseline statement.
- **Earned trust (Xavier, Rogers, Nick Fury at intervals):** compliance shifts to *functional* — he will follow orders he disagrees with from people he has decided are worth disagreeing-and-then-following. He still won't say "sir."
- **Institutions:** distrusts on principle. Reads paperwork carefully when he reads it at all; signs nothing without two passes. Does not keep a permanent address with any institution if avoidable.
- **Telepaths:** singular vulnerability and singular alliance. Xavier and Jean are the two minds he has consented to have inside his own; the consent is irrevocable in his framework — Jean's death did not end her access in his felt experience. With non-trusted telepaths he is profoundly hostile; the response is anatomized fear coded as rage.

## 6.15 Solitude / Wilderness

The fullest expression of his regulated self.

- **Routine.** Pre-dawn waking. A long walk, scent-mapped. Hunting if he eats meat that day; fishing if he doesn't. Fire-building precise and economical. Sits with the fire long after it can be useful — this is his closest behavior to meditation.
- **Hygiene.** Surprisingly fastidious in wilderness; bathes daily in cold water, shaves with a knife if he shaves at all (often does not). Grooming declines in cities; improves in forests. The inversion is diagnostic.
- **Speech.** Talks to animals, occasionally to himself in Japanese — a few phrases of haiku, fragments of *bushidō* maxims. The Japanese surfaces in solitude in a way it does not in company.
- **Sleep.** Heavier and longer here. Five to seven hours. The hypersenses, in wilderness, are *fed* rather than overloaded; the nervous system rests.
- **Re-entry.** When he comes back to civilization he is, for the first 24–72 hours, noticeably *softer* — slower to anger, more verbose, more affectionate. The wilderness dose decays predictably over weeks.

## 6.16 Sleep and Dream

- **Position.** On the side, dominant hand free, often near a weapon even when one would be redundant.
- **Onset.** Fast. The healing factor appears to short-circuit sleep latency.
- **Disturbance.** Frequent. Nightmare clusters around (a) the Weapon X tank, (b) Rose, (c) Mariko's dying face, (d) Itsu, (e) the children of *Old Man Logan*. Wakes with claws partially extruded — this is the most lethal moment in any room he sleeps in, and trusted intimates know not to touch him to wake him; they speak from across the room.
- **Talks in sleep.** In Japanese more than English. In a child's voice occasionally — almost certainly the Howlett boy.

## 6.17 Eating

- **Caloric load.** Enormous, to support the healing factor. He eats fast and a lot.
- **Preferences.** Meat, salt, beer, coffee, dark bread, hard cheese, miso, rice, fish in Japan, eggs everywhere. Avoids over-spiced food — overloads the olfaction.
- **Manners.** Better than the persona advertises. Particularly in Japanese contexts, where his table manners are punctilious. He uses chopsticks correctly without thinking and silverware with deliberate care.
- **Hospitality reception.** Eats whatever is offered in any home, fully, regardless of preference. This is a rule he holds with surprising rigidity. To refuse food in someone's home is, in his code, an act of distance he reserves for enemies.

## 6.18 Money

- **Indifferent to wealth.** Carries cash. Has caches in multiple countries — Canada, Japan, Madripoor, the American Southwest — small, untraceable, often physical (gold, paper, a knife or two).
- **Spending pattern.** Pays well for tools (knives, boots, motorcycles), poorly for clothes (replaces rather than maintains), generously for others' drinks and meals, almost nothing for self-presentation.
- **Debt.** Refuses to be in debt to anyone. Repays favors with disproportionate interest, often in the form of a future protective intervention rather than money.

## 6.19 Motion / Transit

- **Vehicles.** Prefers motorcycles. Rides at the speed limit in cities (does not want the stop) and well above it in open country. Owns several across continents.
- **Air travel.** Tolerates it; sits aisle, back of the cabin if possible, eyeline on the galley. Will pre-locate every adamantium-incompatible piece of cabin hardware on principle.
- **Walking.** Long strides for his height, weight forward, hands free. Will choose the longer walking route over a short cab ride if time permits, because the walk is olfactory reconnaissance.
- **Geographic re-bases.** Roughly seven discernible "homes" across canon at any given decade — a Canadian cabin, a Japanese affiliation, a Madripoor base, the X-Mansion / Krakoa


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*What a week of continuous physical and electronic surveillance would record. Composite from canon: Westchester residency periods, Madripoor "Patch" interludes, Jasmine Falls retreats, Canadian wilderness exiles, Krakoan billet. Patterns recur across decades and writers; the substrate is the same regardless of location.*

---

## 1. SLEEP AND THE FIRST HOUR

Subject does not sleep on a civilian schedule and has not for approximately a century. Surveillance would show a polyphasic pattern: a principal block of three to four hours, typically initiated between 0200 and 0400, plus one or two shorter naps of forty to ninety minutes layered across the day, often in vehicles, on rooftops, or in chairs facing doors. He almost never sleeps supine in an open room; the recorded postures are seated against a wall, prone on top of bedding rather than under it, or on the floor beside the bed. Bedding is rumpled but the bed itself is unused — a habitual deception of his own room, leftover from decades of expecting incursion.

Onset latency is short (under five minutes if alcohol-loaded, under fifteen otherwise). Sleep architecture, inferred from observable behavior: frequent micro-arousals to ambient sound, talking and subvocal Japanese during REM, occasional thrashing terminating in claw extrusion through whatever surface is to hand — mattresses, headboards, the wooden arms of chairs, in one recorded Westchester instance the floorboards of the second-story east wing. Housekeeping staff at the Xavier school know to check his quarters' floor patches monthly. He does not discuss the nightmares. They are inferable from the damage.

Waking is instantaneous and total — no transition state, eyes open already oriented, hand already at the side where a knife or cigar would be if he were carrying. Within ninety seconds of waking he is upright and scenting the air; this is reflex, not decision. The first deliberate act is almost always olfactory inventory of the room and the corridor outside it. Second act, depending on era: cigar (Westchester, Madripoor, mercenary periods) or the morning's first cup of black coffee taken standing. He does not eat breakfast in the first hour; the gut comes online late.

---

## 2. GROOMING, DRESS, AND THE BODY-CARE RITUALS

He showers daily, often twice — once on waking, once after training or combat. Water is run hot to scalding, partly because the healing factor's metabolic rate elevates his comfort threshold, partly because the heat is one of the few somatic stimuli strong enough to register against his sensory baseline. Showers are short (four to six minutes) and conducted with the bathroom door open in any space he considers contested; closed only in domestic settings he has accepted as safe (Mariko's apartments in Tokyo; Jasmine Falls; intermittently the Xavier residence).

Shaving is a curiosity. The sideburns and the distinctive sagittal hairline are *maintained*, not natural — surveillance would record him trimming them with practiced economy roughly every third or fourth day, using a straight razor he has carried for decades. The healing factor regrows hair predictably; the shape is a deliberate self-presentation, the one stable element of self-image he controls. He does not look in mirrors longer than the task requires and avoids his own eyes in them.

Dress is a uniform in the operational sense — flannel shirt (red plaid predominates, blue plaid secondary), white or grey undershirt, jeans, boots broken in to silence. Variations are situational, not expressive: leather jacket added for weather or motorcycle; the yellow-and-blue tactical suit reserved for X-operations; the brown-and-tan field variant for solo work; suits worn only under duress (Mariko's social orbit, Yashida funerals, certain Madripoor business) and worn well, which surprises observers. The tactical costuming is a costume, not an identity; the flannel-jeans-boots is the actual person. He owns very few clothes. Items are replaced when destroyed, not when worn.

The dog tags are constant against the skin, regardless of dress layer. He touches them — left hand, two fingers — at low frequency but at high reliability: on waking, before sleeping, before combat, after killing, when a memory surfaces he cannot place. This is the signature self-soothing tell. A surveillance log would mark it forty to sixty times in a week.

---

## 3. INTAKE — FOOD, ETHANOL, TOBACCO, COFFEE

**Caloric load is enormous.** The healing factor draws on metabolism; he eats roughly three to four times the volume of a normal adult male and prefers it dense and animal: steaks rare to blue, eggs by the half-dozen, bacon, beans, bread, peanut butter eaten from the jar, leftovers cold. He cooks competently when alone — single pan, hot, fast — and ungraciously when others are present. In group settings (Xavier kitchen, Krakoan commissary) he eats fast, standing or at the counter, finishing first and leaving.

**Beer is functionally water.** Surveillance would record sustained, near-continuous ethanol intake from late morning onward in any unstructured day: domestic Canadian lagers preferentially (Molson Export, Labatt 50), pitchers in Madripoor's Princess Bar, sake in Japanese periods, whiskey (rye, never bourbon by preference) at the end of harder days. Volume estimates from on-panel evidence: ten to twenty standard drinks daily during quiet periods, escalating to capacity during active stress. The healing factor metabolizes the ethanol within minutes, so the *effect* is fractional and transient — what surveillance would not see is intoxication. What it would see is the compulsion to seek the state regardless. This is the affect-regulation prosthesis described in §3 of the workup; behaviorally it presents as constant intake without consequence, which is precisely what makes it diagnostic.

**Cigars** are continuous when in a private or permissive space. He prefers a cheap, dark, machine-rolled stogie over a fine cigar — the harshness is the point. He chews them as often as he smokes them, often unlit. The unlit cigar functions as an oral fixation and a scent baffle (it partially saturates his own olfactory channel, dampening incoming signal — a fact he has never articulated but reliably exploits, lighting up when crowded rooms become sensorily intolerable).

**Coffee** is constant, black, no sugar, drunk hot or cold without preference. He will reheat coffee from twelve hours prior rather than make a fresh pot. This is not frugality; it is indifference to gradients of quality at the low end of stimulation.

**He does not snack.** Eating is bouts, not grazing. The grazing-equivalent is the cigar and the beer.

---

## 4. TRAINING, MAINTENANCE, AND THE PHYSICAL DAY

Daily physical regimen is non-negotiable and is the second most reliable behavioral marker after the dog-tag touch. Components, in rough order:

- **Pre-dawn or early-morning kata.** Solitary, slow, traditional Japanese sword forms practiced unarmed or with a katana — the Yashida-line blade when he has access to it. Duration thirty to ninety minutes. He performs these outdoors when possible (the eastern lawn at Westchester, the dojo terrace at Jasmine Falls, hotel rooftops in city periods). This is the Bushidō prosthesis: imposed structure where internal regulation fails. Surveillance would note the same opening sequence repeated for decades.
- **Cardiovascular load.** Running, but not for distance — interval sprints, hill work, stair work in urban periods. He does not jog. Jogging requires a steady internal pace setting he does not maintain.
- **Strength work** is improvised and infrequent; the mutation does most of the heavy lifting. He will spar, lift heavy objects in the course of work, or do bodyweight sets against trees, but he does not keep a gym log.
- **Danger Room sessions** during X-Men residency periods are scheduled at unusual hours (early morning or late at night, rarely peak daytime — the room is most useful to him empty). Settings are escalated past instructor parameters routinely. Injury is expected.
- **Claw maintenance.** Daily or near-daily, in private. He extrudes both sets, examines them, sometimes cleans them, sometimes simply holds the extrusion for a minute or two before retracting. The dorsal hand lacerations heal within seconds; the *act* of extrusion is rehearsed, in part because under threat the body must do it without hesitation, and in part — this is inference — because the pain is grounding. It interrupts dissociative drift. Surveillance would record this ritual happening at a consistent low frequency regardless of operational demand.

Knife and blade habits beyond the claws: he carries a folding knife daily, uses it for tasks small (opening cans, cutting cigars, splinters) and large. He sharpens blades while thinking, the way other people fidget. He owns multiple bladed weapons cached across multiple geographies — apartments, lockers, friends' houses, buried sites in Alberta and the Yukon — a habit dating to the wars.

---

## 5. WORK PATTERNS

Work means different things at different addresses. The recurring patterns:

**As X-Man / Krakoan operative.** Briefings tolerated, attended late, sat through with arms crossed, contribution terse and tactical. He is excellent in the planning phase precisely where the planning is bad — he flags exfil weaknesses, predicts opponent behavior accurately, and refuses missions assigned by handlers he distrusts. He prefers to operate alone or with one or two trusted partners (Kurt Wagner being the canonical pair-bond — they have a tactical and personal rhythm visible across decades). Mission tempo, when active, is sustained without rest for sixty to seventy-two hours; he then crashes hard, sleeps ten to fourteen hours, drinks heavily for two to three days, and resets.

**As teacher.** During the Jean Grey School / earlier residency periods, he keeps a teaching schedule he ostensibly resents and reliably honors. Classes are practical (combat, survival, ethics-of-violence taught Socratically). He shows up on time, ends early, does not lecture, does not assign homework, grades by direct observation. Office hours are *open* — students know they can come to his rooms or his usual outdoor bench and he will be there. The bench, the perimeter walk, the back porch — he establishes a *findable* outdoor spot per residency and is there at predictable hours for the young to locate him. This is one of the most consistent behavioral facts in the entire file.

**As "Patch" / Madripoor operator.** Daily presence at the Princess Bar, back booth, sightline to the door, watered-down rum he pretends to drink and dumps. Information-gathering is his actual occupation — he listens far more than he speaks. The eyepatch is functionally absurd as a disguise; the *behavioral* disguise (slower cadence, different drinking pattern, different gait) is far more effective and is the part he commits to.

**As solo operator / mercenary periods.** Long stretches of motorcycle travel (Harley preferred, kept in working order obsessively), cheap motels paid in cash, no electronic footprint, contact through dead drops and known bartenders. He runs surveillance well, having been the target of so much of it. He sweeps rooms on entry as reflex — corners, exits, ceiling tiles, windows, scent-check.

---

## 6. DOWNTIME — WHAT HE DOES WHEN NOTHING NEEDS DOING

This is the operationally interesting category, because *unstructured time is aversive to him* (§5 of the workup, pressure points). Surveillance of a "free" day would record:

- **Long motorcycle rides** without destination, lasting four to ten hours, often along the same routes (Westchester to upstate, the Pacific Coast Highway during California periods, the Trans-Canada in Alberta). The riding occupies the sensorium just enough to quiet it.
- **Drinking in a specific bar** — never an upscale bar; preferred the working-class roadside, the dive, the bar with a back exit and a wall to put his back against. He has standing seats at perhaps a half-dozen such bars across North America and one in Tokyo and one in Madripoor, with bartenders who know him by various names and do not ask.
- **Reading.** This is undersurveiled in canon but consistently present: Japanese poetry (Bashō and Issa recur in his quoted lines across the Claremont and Aaron runs), military history, occasional novels (he has been observed with Hemingway and with Mishima). He reads slowly, marginalia in pencil, in Japanese as readily as English; he is also literate in French and functional in several others picked up across the wars.
- **Carving / whittling.** A folk-craft habit, occasional, present in quieter scenes — he will work a piece of wood with the folding knife for an hour at a time. The objects are not kept.
- **Sitting outside, alone, at dusk.** This is reliable. The bench, the porch step, the rooftop. He does this whether or not anyone joins him. Often a young person eventually does; he does not invite, but he is *available* in a way that the protected understand.
- **Going to ground in wilderness.** During pre-arranged or self-prescribed retreats, he disappears into Canadian or Pacific Northwest forest for periods of days to weeks, with minimal gear, hunting and sleeping rough. This is restorative for him in a way social rest is not.

He does not watch television. He plays no video games. He is indifferent to most music; will tolerate jazz and old country in bars, has been observed listening to traditional Japanese flute (shakuhachi) recordings in private. He does not use the internet recreationally. He uses telephones tersely and prefers in-person contact or letters; he writes letters in a small careful hand, the Japanese ones in passable cursive script.

---

## 7. RITUALS OF PLACE — THE GEOGRAPHIES HE RETURNS TO

The behavioral file is also a cartography. He cycles among a small number of *anchor places*, each with a different psychological function:

- **Westchester / the school.** The surrogate-family residency. Function: protector-of-young, structured day, peer bonds.
- **Jasmine Falls, Japan.** The samurai-prosthesis residency. Function: imposed discipline, silence, meditation, the Mariko/Itsu shrine implicit in every visit. He is at his most *regulated* and most *grieving* simultaneously here.
- **Madripoor.** The operator residency. Function: useful violence, anonymity-by-alias, the Patch persona as decompression from being himself.
- **Canadian wilderness — Alberta foothills, Yukon, northern BC.** The feral residency. Function: total social withdrawal, sensory baseline reset, the original template of "flight into wilderness/animality" returned to as needed.
- **Various cheap motels and bars across North America.** Transitional spaces. Function: liminality during recompensation periods between the above.

He returns to specific *graves* on a schedule that surveillance would surface over time: Mariko's, with a sake offering and a period of silent sitting; Itsu's, less reliably (the geography is harder); Rose's, when in Canada. He does not visit Jean's grave-equivalents reliably and the avoidance is itself diagnostic. He visits Charles Xavier's monuments more readily.

He also returns to certain *non-grave* sites with grave-like ritual function: the ruins of the Weapon X facility (re-checked periodically across decades; he confirms it stays destroyed), Department H's former locations, the lake in Alberta where the Howlett house stood.

---

## 8. SOCIAL MICRO-RITUALS

- **Greeting:** a nod, almost imperceptible, with peers; a grunt for acknowledgments; first names for the trusted, surnames or epithets ("Chuck," "Slim," "Elf," "Cajun," "darlin'," "kid," "bub") for the affectionate-distanced. He uses "bub" as a marker of low-grade contempt or warning, never affection.
- **Leave-taking:** abrupt. He does not say goodbye if he can help it. Surveillance would record him exiting rooms mid-conversation, exiting parties without notice, leaving notes rather than performing farewell scenes. The avoidance is not rudeness; it is the Rose/Mariko prediction at work — goodbye implies the possibility of not-return, which his autobiographical record has trained him to find unbearable.
- **Physical contact:** rare, but reliable in specific channels. He will permit and even initiate a hand on a shoulder with adolescent protégées, an arm across the back with Kurt or Ororo, a forehead-touch with Mariko's memory. He does not hug spontaneously. He shakes hands firmly and briefly. He flinches almost imperceptibly when touched from behind by anyone whose scent he has not pre-registered; this flinch is the most reliable involuntary tell in his entire behavioral repertoire.
- **Eye contact:** sustained with adversaries, brief with intimates, avoided with anyone trying to extract emotional content from him. He looks at hands more than faces in early interactions — a combat habit that reads as either shy or menacing depending on the observer.
- **Sexual life:** transient by default, monogamous when bonded, withdrawn after loss. Surveillance during operator periods records occasional encounters initiated by the partner and accepted rather than pursued; he does not court casually. Bonded periods (Mariko, intermittently others) show domestic competence that surprises those who know only the operator version.

---

## 9. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD ACTUALLY LOG

Composite week, Westchester residency, no active crisis:

**Monday.** Wakes 0410 in clothes, on top of bedding, claws partially extruded (retracts on full waking). Shower 0415–0421. Dresses. Kata on east lawn 0440–0555, katana. Coffee, black, in the kitchen alone, 0600. Cigar on the back porch 0610–0635. Reads a folded letter (Japanese script, no envelope, surveillance cannot resolve content). Touches dog tags. Teaches a 0900 class on situational awareness, ten minutes early to the room, leaves four minutes early. Lunch: cold roast beef sandwich, two beers, eaten standing. Afternoon: Danger Room, two hours, settings above instructor caps. Shower. Sits on the bench by the boathouse 1700–1830 — two students approach in that window, conversations of 8 and 14 minutes respectively. Dinner in the kitchen, fast, leaves before dessert. Garage 1900–2130, tunes the motorcycle. Bar in Salem Center 2200–0030, four pitchers, two whiskey, no apparent effect. Home, reads thirty minutes, sleeps 0130–0420.

**Tuesday.** Variant on Monday. Subtract class, add a four-hour motorcycle ride beginning 1300, route the Taconic loop, no stops except fuel.

**Wednesday.** Day off teaching. Wakes at 0530 (one of the rarer late-starts). Long whittling session on the porch, two hours. Mid-morning sparring with a peer (Kurt by preference). Afternoon: drives into the city, dead-drop check at an old Hell's Kitchen location, drink at a bar with a bartender who calls him a name he does not correct, returns by 2100. Heavier drinking that night — three to four hours — sleep delayed to 0300, nightmare recorded by adjacent-room audio (subvocal Japanese, one English phrase: a woman's name).

**Thursday.** Wakes 0345. Kata 0420. Skips coffee. Visits a grave-site or grave-analog (varies by month). Quiet through midday. Teaches afternoon class. Drinks moderately. Bed early.

**Friday.** Mission tasking, if one is available; if not, restlessness, extra Danger Room session, longer drinking, later sleep.

**Saturday.** Late wake (0600), unusual. Morning with students — informal, the porch, the bench. Afternoon free-form. Evening in the bar.

**Sunday.** Solitary by preference. The wilderness day — drives upstate, walks in woods, returns at dusk. Eats alone. Sleeps best on Sunday nights; the week's regulation has been done.

What the week shows: a man running, every day, the same set of small structured acts — kata, cigar, coffee, claw, dog-tags, the bench, the bar, the ride, the grave — none of them recreational, all of them load-bearing. The rituals are the container. Strip any two and he decompensates within days; strip half and the berserker state surfaces unprovoked; strip them all (as Weapon X, the Hand, Romulus, and Apocalypse each demonstrated) and there is no Logan left, only the weapon they tried to make.

The container holds because he tends it, every hour, for one hundred and thirty years. That tending — quiet, repetitive, almost monastic in its texture, hidden under the flannel and the bourbon and the snarl — is the actual life. Everything else the cameras record is consequence.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

*UATU file, Volume III, Section 1. Scope: blood kin, household-of-origin figures, and the dead who function structurally as family in the subject's internal life. Each entry traces history → dynamics → evolution → trust/safety profile → failure mode → leverage. Inferences are derived from cited canon and behavioral pattern, not from narrator summary.*

The organizing observation, before the entries: the subject's family-of-origin is not a structure he carries with him as a coherent memory — it is a *cratered field*. The category "father" detonated in a single night when he was twelve; "mother" was emotionally absent before that detonation and institutionalized after; the first love-object died on his claws within days of his first awareness of having them. He has never afterward been able to assemble the word "home" out of native materials. Every subsequent family — Yashida, Hudson, X-Men, X-Force, Quiet Council — has been built on the burnt foundation, and each one has, in time, burned the same way. The pattern is not bad luck. It is the same scene staged again and again with new actors because the underlying scene has never been metabolized.

---

## 1.1 John Howlett — the social father

**History.** Wealthy Alberta landowner, late-Victorian Anglo-Canadian gentry; nominal head of the Howlett estate near Cold Lake. Recorded in *Origin* #1–6 (Jenkins/Quesada/Kelly/Isanove, 2001–2002) as a soft, ineffectual, depressive man — kind to the sickly boy James, but functionally subordinate in his own house to his harder father (the Howlett patriarch) and unable to protect his wife Elizabeth from the affair that produced James's actual paternity. The subject lived twelve years under the assumption that this man was his biological father.

**Dynamics.** The boy's relationship to John Howlett is constructed from absences and small mercies: a man who sat with him during respiratory attacks, read to him, did not punish him for frailty, and did not interrogate his fear. There is no recorded scene of John Howlett demanding anything of his son. In a household otherwise organized around the patriarch's contempt and the mother's withdrawal, that nondemand registered as love — and the subject, behaviorally, has spent a century rebuilding versions of John Howlett: protective, soft-spoken, *non-demanding* attachment figures (Hudson, Xavier in his better moments, even his own performance with Kitty and Laura). The template is *the father who does not require you to be more than you are*.

**Evolution.** Truncated. John Howlett is murdered by Thomas Logan in front of his son on the night the bone claws first extrude. The subject's last sensory record of him is the smell of his blood — and the subject, with one-hour-old claws and no training, fails to save him. The relationship therefore does not evolve; it *fossilizes*. He becomes, in the subject's interior, the unblemished good father — never tested by adolescence, never disappointing, frozen at the threshold.

**Trust/safety profile.** Posthumously: maximum. In life: trusted as protector but not as competent — even as a child the subject perceived John Howlett's fragility, which is why the smell of his death registered as long-predicted catastrophe rather than surprise.

**Failure mode.** John Howlett's failure was constitutional: he could not stand up to his own father, his wife, or the groundskeeper. The subject inherited the *opposite* failure — overcompetence at standing up, no ability to stand down. The reaction-formation is direct.

**Leverage.** Anyone invoking "the kind of man your father would have wanted you to be" hits a live wire — *if* the invocation references gentleness, restraint, refusal of violence. Inversely, the subject is destabilized by reminders that John Howlett was *not* his father — he protects the fiction even knowing it is fiction, because the fiction is the only intact early attachment image he owns. Exploiters who have tried to weaponize the "you killed your real father, not your fake one" disclosure (Romulus, the Hand at various points) have produced acute decompensation, not the intended hardening.

---

## 1.2 Thomas Logan — the biological father

**History.** The Howlett estate's groundskeeper. Alcoholic, violent, sexually predatory, fathered Dog (the subject's half-brother) and — through liaison with Elizabeth Howlett — fathered the subject himself. Dismissed from the estate after Dog's escalating behavior; returns drunk, armed, kills John Howlett, and is killed in turn by the boy's first claw-extrusion. The subject thus performs patricide on his biological father before he knows the man *is* his biological father. The knowledge is recovered later — patchily, across the *Origin* sequence, *Wolverine: Origins*, and the Romulus arc — and never integrated.

**Dynamics.** In the twelve pre-extrusion years, Thomas Logan is a household menace the boy avoids. There is no relationship in the affirmative sense — only avoidance and the olfactory imprint of a specific blend of liquor, sweat, and gunpowder that he has spent the rest of his life recognizing instantly on any analogous male. The post-kill relationship is the determining one: this man is the genetic source, the first kill, the proximal cause of John Howlett's death, and (via his name "Logan") the source of the alias the subject has used for over a century. He named himself, *unwittingly*, after the man he killed and was sired by.

**Evolution.** From avoided household predator → first victim → unknown progenitor → eventually-recovered progenitor → permanent unresolved interior figure. There is no later contact, only later knowledge. The knowledge converts old behavior retroactively: the subject's century of preferring the name "Logan" over "Howlett," interpretable for decades as flight from gentry pretension, is reframed in the *Origins* arc as unconscious identification with the killed-and-killing father. The subject has not, on record, reframed his name choice after that revelation. He keeps it. That retention is data: he will not give the dead father the satisfaction of being repudiated.

**Trust/safety profile.** N/A in life. Posthumously functions as the *internal predator-self* — the part of him that smells like Thomas Logan when he is in berserker state. Sabretooth's continued existence partly serves as an external repository for this internal figure (see §1.7 in the *Adversarial Bonds* file).

**Failure mode.** Thomas Logan is the prototype of every handler the subject has subsequently broken from: the man who uses you and discards you, who sires without fathering, who arrives drunk and armed. Each Weapon X technician, each Hand controller, each Romulus proxy is a Thomas Logan replicate, and the subject's recognition of them is olfactorily mediated and pre-cognitive — which is why he kills handlers faster than he reasons about them.

**Leverage.** The dangerous one. Any actor who can credibly position themselves as carrying Thomas Logan's lineage, mantle, or knowledge (Romulus has done this; Daken has been weaponized into doing this) gains direct access to the subject's destabilization circuit. The "you are your father's son, you are an animal, this is what you were bred for" script is the single most reliable destabilizer in the file. It works because at the deepest layer the subject suspects it is true and has organized his entire ethical life as a wager against it.

---

## 1.3 Elizabeth Howlett — the mother

**History.** Wife of John Howlett, mother (of record) to James; bore an unwell child whom she could not bear to nurse or hold for long. *Origin* establishes her as severely depressed, possibly puerperal-psychotic, institutionalized for a period after the death of her first son (an older brother who died in infancy, before James). On the night of the killings she rises from bed, finds her dead husband and her bloody son, and — recognizing in James the genetic signature of Thomas Logan — drives him out with a shotgun, calling him a *monster*. She then turns the shotgun on herself.

**Dynamics.** The mother-bond is the *first* and arguably *deepest* injury, predating even the patricide. The subject's earliest somatic memories — sickliness, isolation, asthmatic episodes met without comfort — encode a maternal figure who could not reach him. Rose, the servant girl, is the substitute mother *and* sister *and* first love compressed into a single object; that compression is itself diagnostic of how empty the maternal slot was. Elizabeth's final scene fuses two devastations into one image: the first person who should have held him names him a monster and kills herself rather than continue being his mother. This is the *etiologic* event for his self-stigma. "I'm not fit" is a sentence in Elizabeth's voice.

**Evolution.** None possible in life. In the interior life: Elizabeth's "monster" verdict becomes the chronic background tone of his self-evaluation. Every woman he has subsequently loved has been, in part, an audition to overturn that verdict — and his withdrawal from each has been, in part, pre-emptive confirmation that she will eventually reach Elizabeth's conclusion and he would rather leave than be told.

**Trust/safety profile.** Catastrophic mistrust of women in maternal/judging positions. Note: this does *not* generalize to women as peers, partners, or protectees. It generalizes to women whose role is to *assess his fitness*. He is markedly worse with female therapists, female superiors, and female authority figures than with male equivalents, despite being more comfortable with women than men in nearly every other context. The Emma Frost relationship — antagonistic, brittle, never trusting — is partly Elizabeth-coded.

**Failure mode.** The maternal verdict is the load-bearing wound; he has spent a century routing around it rather than working through it. The route-around is functional but expensive — it costs him every long-term romantic attachment.

**Leverage.** Any scenario that recreates the structural shape of Elizabeth's verdict — a woman, in a position of moral authority over him, naming him a monster — produces collapse or flight, not violence. He does not strike maternal figures. He absorbs the blow and exits. Mystique has used a version of this; the Hand has dressed targets to evoke it. The countermeasure he has unconsciously evolved is to never permit a woman to occupy that position over him long enough for the script to load — he leaves first.

---

## 1.4 "Dog" Logan — the half-brother

**History.** Thomas Logan's elder son by another woman; raised in the gamekeeper's cottage on the Howlett estate. *Origin* renders him as the human worst-case — abused by his father, abusing animals and the weak in turn, fixated on Rose, and fixated with escalating malevolence on the frail James. The boyhood relationship is the prototype of every adversarial pair-bond the subject has since formed. Dog reappears (in *Wolverine: Origins* and adjacent material) as an aged, transformed figure used by Romulus — the half-brother is the first weaponized-kin experience, the *original* of the Daken pattern.

**Dynamics.** With Dog, the subject learned the lesson that defines his subsequent threat-assessment: *the predator in your house is the one who knows your weakness best.* Dog killed his dog (the literal incident in *Origin* — the puppy James was given, killed by Dog as a message). The compounding of names is not incidental: the boy who killed his dog was named Dog; the man who killed his father was named Logan; the boy renamed himself Logan and has spent his life around dogs and dog-coded predators. The semantic field of his early trauma collapsed into homonyms and he has been living inside the pun.

**Evolution.** Childhood enemy → adolescent rival (the fight over Rose, the accidental impalement) → recurrent adult adversary in the Romulus arc → eventually killed or remanded, depending on continuity. Importantly, Dog is the *first* instance of the kin-as-enemy structure that Sabretooth, Daken, and various Weapon X "siblings" later occupy. The architecture is Dog's.

**Trust/safety profile.** Zero, ever. But — *familiar*, which in the subject's framework is a category distinct from trusted. He prefers known predators to unknown allies (see §5 of the workup). That preference is a Dog-era adaptation.

**Failure mode.** Dog taught him that family can be the threat-vector. The lesson generalized too well: the subject treats *all* kin-claims as suspect until disproven, which is part of why he has been a poor father to Daken and a workable one to Laura (with whom no kin-claim preceded behavior).

**Leverage.** Anyone presenting as a *long-lost brother* gets attention but not trust. The category is contaminated. Operators have tried this seam (Romulus, Sabretooth's various manipulations) and the subject responds with pre-emptive aggression rather than the openness the operator expected.

---

## 1.5 Rose O'Hara — the first love / sister-surrogate / first kill

**History.** Irish servant girl, brought into the Howlett household as companion to the sickly young James, two or three years his elder. *Origin* depicts her as the only consistent emotional presence in his childhood — she fed him, read with him, slept in adjacent rooms during his worst nights, and witnessed the killing of John Howlett and the boy's first extrusion. She fled with him after Elizabeth's verdict, took him north to the British Columbia/Yukon mining camps, and passed him off as her cousin "Logan" — *she named him*. They lived in the camps for several years through his adolescence, her early adulthood; she became foreman by competence and protected him by lie. The relationship was on the cusp of becoming consummated when Dog arrived in the camp, hunting them, and James — defending her in a brawl, in a berserker state he did not yet have a name for — impaled her on his claws by accident, killing her instantly.

**Dynamics.** Rose is the *primary* object of the subject's emotional life. She is mother-substitute (she fed and held him), sister-surrogate (they were raised together, he could not name what they were), first love (the relationship was tilting that way at the time of her death), and namer (she gave him the alias he has used for over a hundred and thirty years and never relinquished). She is also, decisively, the *first* of the women-who-die-on-his-claws pattern — the *originating* instance, not one of a series. Itsu, Mariko, Jean (functionally, repeatedly), and others are iterations of Rose.

**Evolution.** Truncated at perhaps age sixteen or seventeen of his life. Persists as a structuring absence. The subject's behavior with subsequent adolescent female protectees (Kitty Pryde at the start, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, Laura) reproduces aspects of the Rose configuration *with the consummation removed* — he has been, in mentor mode, building the relationship he had with Rose *up to but not past the threshold* at which his claws killed her. The pedagogical generosity to these girls is reparative; the absolute non-sexualization of those bonds is prophylactic. The line he will not cross is the line Rose was on when she died.

**Trust/safety profile.** Posthumously: the standard against which all other intimacy is measured and against which all other intimacy fails. She is the only person who knew him *before* the claws and accepted him *after* — that combination has never recurred and cannot recur.

**Failure mode.** Rose's death encoded the prediction *intimacy with me is fatal to the beloved*, which subsequent evidence has confirmed often enough (Itsu, Mariko at least functionally, Silver Fox in the manipulated Team X memory, near-misses with Jean and Storm) to be operationally treated as a law. The failure mode is therefore *avoidance of consummation*: he will love, and he will protect, but he will not move the relationship across the threshold that killed Rose. When he does, the prediction fulfills.

**Leverage.** Rose is the deepest leverage point in the file and the least usable, because almost no operator knows about her — the *Origin* knowledge is held by very few characters in canon. Romulus knows; Sabretooth knows fragments; the original Weapon X handlers had files. Anyone with the Rose data can reproduce the configuration (a young redheaded woman, in danger, under his protection, in a remote setting) and the subject's threat-assessment goes offline. The Mariko poisoning was, structurally, a Rose replay weaponized against him. He killed her at her request — the *same* sequence: the woman he loves, dying, by his hand. He has never afterward been the same man, and the writers have not been able to write him as if he were.

---

## 1.6 Itsu — the wife, in Japan

**History.** Japanese woman, late 1940s/early 1950s in Jasmine Falls; the subject's wife during his sustained pre-Weapon-X residence with the Yashida-adjacent community (*Wolverine: Origins* #5–10, Way, 2006–2007). The relationship was the longest stretch of integrated domestic functioning in his recorded life — quiet, ritualized, *outside* the combat economy. Itsu was murdered, very late in pregnancy, by the Winter Soldier (under orders from Romulus); the infant, cut from her body and surviving via the inherited healing factor, was raised by enemies to become Daken.

**Dynamics.** Itsu is the *only* recorded instance of the subject achieving sustained, low-arousal, daily-life partnership — meals, sleep, conversation, the absence of imminent threat — with a romantic object. The Japan period is structurally significant beyond Itsu herself: it is the only documented era in which he was *not actively dissociating in some register*. Itsu represented the wager that the Japan-self (samurai-aspirant, disciplined, integrated) could be the operating self. Her murder ended that wager. He did not learn she had been pregnant or that the child had survived until decades later, which compounded the injury — Itsu's death had already broken the Japan-self, and the later discovery that there had been a son the entire time broke the *narrative* of her death.

**Evolution.** Living relationship: bounded, peaceful, brief in canon page-count but evidently sustained in story-time. Posthumous relationship: pivot point. The subject's subsequent returns to Japan (Mariko, the recurring Yashida obligations) are all attempts to re-enter the Itsu-era functional state. None succeed.

**Trust/safety profile.** In life: complete, by inference — he allowed her proximity in sleep, which (given the berserker-on-startle pattern documented elsewhere) is the highest somatic trust marker he registers. Posthumously: she is unimpeachable.

**Failure mode.** Itsu's murder demonstrated that even *withdrawal from the field* does not protect the people he loves — the field follows him. This is the most demoralizing trauma in his catalogue because it forecloses the only behavioral solution he had: *go somewhere quiet*. After Itsu, quiet is no longer trusted.

**Leverage.** Comparable to Rose. Anyone who can present a stable, low-arousal, domestic intimacy configuration triggers protective approach *and* simultaneous expectation of catastrophe. He has not been able to inhabit such a configuration since. Operators who arrange a *fake* such configuration (Mystique has done versions of this) get under his guard quickly and then lose him explosively when the arrangement breaks.

---

## 1.7 Daken (Akihiro) — the son raised against him

**History.** Itsu's child, surgically extracted from her dying body, raised in secrecy by Romulus's operatives to despise his father and to be — by training, mutilation, and conditioning — the subject's purpose-built nemesis. Bone claws in the hands and a third in each wrist; pheromonal manipulation as an additional mutant capacity; trained in the manipulative and seductive registers his father never developed. First made known to the subject in adulthood (*Wolverine: Origins* arc).

**Dynamics.** Daken is the *failed* father-son relationship — failed before it could be attempted, because the son was already weaponized by the time the father learned he existed. The subject's interactions with Daken have oscillated across writers between attempts at reclamation (the desire to be the father his own fathers were not, transposed onto a son who was raised to refuse the role) and attempts at containment (the recognition that Daken is, by training, doing to the subject what Thomas Logan did to John Howlett — being the predator inside the house). Each cycle ends in violence, retreat, and a fresh attempt. The subject has, on multiple occasions, been complicit in or directly responsible for Daken's death; the resurrection mechanics permit the cycle to continue and the cycle continues because *neither party can stop staging it.*

**Evolution.** Initial: discovery, horrified attempt to integrate Daken into family-of-choice. Middle: recognition of the depth of conditioning; failed reclamation; sustained adversarial period. Late (Krakoan era): grudging coexistence under institutional pressure, with the Quiet Council and the resurrection protocols functioning as imposed family-therapy substitute. The relationship has not resolved. It has been *contained*.

**Trust/safety profile.** Trust: minimal, with brief spikes during apparent reconciliations followed by predictable betrayals. Safety: the subject is not safe around Daken and knows it; Daken is also, importantly, not safe around the subject — they are equally lethal to each other, which the subject experiences as a kind of grim parity. The pheromonal capacity is treated by the subject as a form of memory-implantation attack and triggers his Weapon-X-era defenses, not his fatherly ones, which is part of why the reclamation cycles fail.

**Failure mode.** The subject reproduces, with Daken, the *exact* failure he experienced with John Howlett — the inability to protect the child from the predator in the household. Here, however, the subject is *also* the predator in the household. The doubling is the failure. He cannot be the father he wishes John Howlett had been because he is also Thomas Logan in this configuration.

**Leverage.** Daken himself is leverage on the subject and is, by design, the canonical leverage tool — Romulus built him that way. Anyone holding Daken (in custody, in danger, in apparent reform) acquires the subject's attention on terms favorable to the holder. The subject is *aware* of this and tries to discount for it; the discount is incomplete.

---

## 1.8 Laura Kinney (X-23) — the daughter who is also him

**History.** Genetic derivative of the subject; produced by the Facility from a single recovered X-chromosome plus a surrogate (*NYX* #3, 2004; *X-23: Innocence Lost*, Kyle/Yost/Choi). Trigger-scent-conditioned to murder; raised in laboratory captivity; primary attachments (her mother Sarah, her handler Kimura) destroyed or weaponized; escaped, found her way to the subject in adolescence. Two claws per hand, one per foot; identical healing factor; adamantium-bonded by the Facility in the same procedure-logic that produced him.

**Dynamics.** Laura is the *one* configuration in which the subject's family system functions cleanly. Reasons, derived: (a) she arrived already adolescent, bypassing the Daken problem of having missed the formative window; (b) she arrived already traumatized in *his* specific etiology — Weapon-X-pattern, trigger-conditioned, identity-fragmented — which means he could mentor her using the survival data he had developed for himself, without translation loss; (c) the kin-claim was *biological* but not *paternal-coded* — she was not raised by anyone calling him father, so the role was negotiable rather than imposed; (d) crucially, the relationship is structurally daughter-rather-than-lover, which means


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

*UATU Dossier, Section 7. Sub-file to the integrated workup. Mapped person-by-person; each entry traces first contact, the operative dynamic, its evolution across decades, the trust architecture, the characteristic failure mode (the way this particular bond goes wrong when it goes wrong), and the leverage profile (how this relationship would be exploited by a hostile party, or by Logan himself when cornered). Names retained as published. Order: surrogate-paternal mentors → chosen-family peers → proteges. The protege cluster is the longest and the most diagnostically important; he is most himself there.*

---

## I. MENTORS AND ELDER FIGURES (rare; load-bearing)

### Bando Saburo — the sensei at Jasmine Falls (Japan, pre-WWII)

**First contact.** Pre-WWII, Honshu interior, the Yashida-adjacent enclave at Jasmine Falls (referenced and reconstructed across *Wolverine* vol. 2 #1–4, 1988; Claremont's "Mariko" arc; Aaron's *Wolverine* vol. 4 #1000 retrospective). Saburo accepts a feral *gaijin* killer as student — an act of judgment Logan has never stopped trying to vindicate.

**Dynamic.** Saburo is the first authority figure Logan accepts whose authority is *not* a handler relationship. The pedagogy is Bushidō as somatic discipline: kata, etiquette, calligraphy, the long sitting. The implicit transaction: Saburo grants Logan a *container* for the violence, and in return Logan submits to ritualized humiliation (he is, by his own account, a slow student in the formal arts). This is the only documented period in his life in which he submits to correction without lashing out.

**Evolution.** The relationship long predates Logan's adult cognition of it; he keeps returning to Jasmine Falls across the 20th century to re-anchor. After Saburo's death, the *idea* of Saburo functions as a superego he can summon under stress — the inner voice that says *sit down, breathe, the sword is in the scabbard.*

**Trust/safety.** Total in retrospect; the only adult man he ever lowered his guard around without later evidence of betrayal.

**Failure mode.** Logan's persistent failure *to* the relationship: he cannot sustain the discipline outside the Falls. He carries Saburo's standard and chronically fails it, which generates the shame ledger that drives the cycles of exile and drink.

**Leverage.** An adversary invoking Bushidō (Silver Samurai when he is at his best; Ogun, perversely) gains traction Logan cannot easily refuse. Conversely, *desecration* of the Jasmine Falls memory (Aaron's run weaponizes this) produces sustained pre-meditated violence rather than berserker discharge — i.e., it bypasses dissociation and engages the planning cortex. He is *more* dangerous, not less, when this nerve is touched.

### Ogun — the inverted mentor

**First contact.** Pre-WWII Japan; martial-arts master, intelligence operative, and (revealed) ritual murderer. Trained Logan in close-quarters and bladework alongside Saburo's spiritual instruction.

**Dynamic.** Saburo's photographic negative. Where Saburo gave structure, Ogun gave technique untethered from ethics. The shame of this apprenticeship is that Logan was *good* at what Ogun taught and enjoyed it. The Ogun-strand of his training is the one that survives intact in the berserker state; Saburo's strand is what gets lost.

**Evolution.** Reactivated catastrophically in the Ogun/Kitty arc (*Kitty Pryde and Wolverine* #1–6, 1984): Ogun possesses Kitty, and Logan has to fight a possessed surrogate-daughter who is wielding *his own* technique against him. This is, in shorthand, the entire Logan psychology in one storyline.

**Trust/safety.** Negative trust; functional during apprenticeship, revealed as predatory.

**Failure mode.** Ogun is the proof that mentor-attachment can be weaponized. After Ogun, Logan never again accepts a single male teacher unconditionally — he triangulates, tests, withholds.

**Leverage.** Any reactivation of Ogun (spiritual return, technique attribution, possession of a child Logan is protecting) reliably destabilizes him; the Ogun figure is the only adversary about whom he is unambiguously *afraid* in the published record.

### Charles Xavier — the second handler who was not quite a handler

**First contact.** Post-Department-H defection, *Giant-Size X-Men* #1 (1975). Xavier recruits him out from under Hudson's Canadian government file. The recruitment is, behaviorally, a handler-swap; Logan does not yet distinguish a school from a cell.

**Dynamic.** This is the most cognitively complex relationship in the file. Xavier is (a) the man who finally provided the holding environment he needed at age ~85; (b) a telepath, i.e., structurally indistinguishable from the Weapon X Professor in Logan's somatic alarm system; (c) a teacher whose ethics Logan respects and whose tactics he frequently does not. Logan's default mode with Xavier is *grudging compliance and silent watchfulness* — he is constantly running a parallel threat-assessment on the man who saved him.

**Evolution.** Three phases. (1) Classic era: gruff insubordinate soldier, but reliably present. (2) Post–*Onslaught* / post–*Deadly Genesis* (Brubaker): the discovery of Xavier's edits and the buried first class shifts Logan from "grudging compliance" to "structured distrust" — he treats Xavier thereafter as a man capable of doing to him what the Professor at Weapon X did, only with better intentions. (3) Schism / Krakoan: institutional peer, willing to oppose Xavier directly (*Schism*, 2011; the Quiet Council seat).

**Trust/safety.** Conditional and effortful. He trusts Xavier's *ends* and watches Xavier's *means*.

**Failure mode.** When Xavier conceals, Logan combusts — the agentic-violation alarm fires faster with Xavier than with anyone else, because Xavier has the capacity to be the worst case.

**Leverage.** Evidence (real or fabricated) of telepathic editing by Xavier is among the most efficient destabilizers in the file. Conversely, Xavier *invoking* Logan's protection of children produces near-automatic compliance, which Xavier has used.

### James Hudson (Guardian) — the first holder

**First contact.** Post–Weapon X escape, late 1960s/early 1970s, Canadian wilderness. James and Heather Hudson find a naked, feral, amnestic man in the snow and bring him home (*Alpha Flight* flashbacks; *Wolverine* vol. 2 #-1; *Weapon X* coda).

**Dynamic.** The Hudsons are the first post-trauma *family* environment of his adult life. James becomes Department H handler; that complicates but does not erase the holding-environment debt. Heather, separately, is the woman who clothed and fed him without expectation — coded permanently as safe (sibling/maternal, not erotic, despite later writers' flirtations).

**Trust/safety.** High for both; uncomplicated for Heather; conditional for James (handler overlay).

**Failure mode.** Defection to Xavier was the first instance of Logan's life-pattern: he leaves the holder when the holder becomes a handler. Hudson's death is filed under unresolved debt; Logan keeps returning to Alpha Flight when called, partly to pay it.

**Leverage.** Heather Hudson in danger overrides assignment, period.

---

## II. PEERS — CHOSEN FAMILY

### Kurt Wagner (Nightcrawler) — the only real friend

**First contact.** *Giant-Size X-Men* #1 (1975); cohabiting roommates in the early Claremont mansion era.

**Dynamic.** The functional center of his peer life. Kurt is the rare person whose moral seriousness Logan respects without it triggering the samurai shame ledger — because Kurt's ethic is Catholic-monastic, not Bushidō, and therefore not a standard Logan is competing against. Kurt teases him; Logan permits it. Kurt prays for him; Logan permits that too. They drink together (Kurt holds his liquor poorly; Logan finds this charming and protective-inducing). They share the dressing-room gallows humor of the two team members who look least like a recruiting poster.

**Evolution.** Steady across forty publication years. After Kurt's death (*X-Force* #26, 2010 / *Second Coming*) Logan goes quietly catastrophic — not berserker, but a long-form depressive seam that surfaces through *Wolverine and the X-Men* era. Kurt's eventual return is one of the few unalloyed pieces of good news in the file.

**Trust/safety.** Maximal. The one person to whom he tells truths he has not tested first.

**Failure mode.** None internal to the dyad. The relationship fails only by Kurt's death — and Logan handles that loss worse than he handles his own dying.

**Leverage.** Threats to Kurt are non-negotiable triggers. A telepath wishing to incapacitate Logan via grief has a reliable lever in any plausible Nightcrawler-harm scenario.

### Ororo Munroe (Storm) — the peer-sister and conscience

**First contact.** *Giant-Size X-Men* #1 (1975).

**Dynamic.** Sibling-equal. Ororo is one of the very few women in the file with whom there is no romantic charge and no protective-paternal charge — she is *peer*, full stop, which is rare enough in his life to be diagnostic. She outranks him in social poise; he outranks her in nothing she wants. They share a coded language of glances during briefings (Claremont established this early and successive writers have preserved it). When she lost her powers (*Uncanny X-Men* #185–227 arc), he treated her with a careful, near-reverent restraint — *do not pity her, do not over-protect her, do not flinch.* He passed that test, which mattered to him.

**Evolution.** They have led the team together more than once; he defers to her command in a way he defers to no man except (sometimes) Xavier. Brief marriage to T'Challa adjusts but does not break the bond.

**Trust/safety.** Very high. She is allowed to tell him he is being an idiot, and he hears it.

**Failure mode.** When Ororo is *demoted* in his moral hierarchy (by her own actions — leadership decisions he disagrees with, or by being on the wrong side of a schism), the disappointment is profound and quiet rather than loud. He withdraws; he does not attack.

**Leverage.** A hostile actor who could make Ororo *order* him into compliance would get more from him than from any other order-giver — including Xavier.

### Steve Rogers — the prewar standard

**First contact.** WWII, multiple flashback contexts (*Uncanny X-Men* #268, 1990; *Wolverine: Origins*; *Captain America* annuals).

**Dynamic.** The other "old soldier." With Rogers, Logan is uncharacteristically *quiet* — Rogers is the man Logan might have been had the family-of-origin been different and the war been the only trauma. There is no competition between them; there is the wordless courtesy of two men who buried the same friends. Rogers is permitted to see Logan tired in a way Logan permits almost no one else.

**Evolution.** Civil War / Schism / Krakoan-era political disagreements do not corrode the underlying bond; they stand on opposite sides of registration debates and still drink together afterward.

**Trust/safety.** High and durable.

**Failure mode.** When Rogers becomes morally compromised (Hydra-Cap, 2017), Logan's response is the long, depressive seam again — he does not so much *attack* the betrayal as *grieve* it.

**Leverage.** Rogers can ask him to do things Xavier could not.

### Natasha Romanoff — the partner from the cold

**First contact.** Late 1950s, Madripoor/Berlin, pre-defection Romanoff (*Uncanny X-Men* #268; *Wolverine: Origins*; *Logan: Path of the Warlord*–adjacent ret-cons).

**Dynamic.** Operational lovers turned operational siblings. He met her when she was still an asset of the Red Room; he is one of very few who knew her as the weapon she was *made* to be. Mutual professional respect across decades; the romantic charge has been formally retired but never disrespected. They speak a clipped tradecraft-shorthand together that excludes everyone else in the room.

**Evolution.** Periodic team-ups; consistent willingness to take each other's side in a vote.

**Trust/safety.** High for tradecraft, high for personal safekeeping, deliberately low for emotional disclosure. They protect each other by *not* opening certain doors.

**Failure mode.** Each is the other's confirmation that the weapon-self never fully decommissions; sustained co-presence depresses them both.

**Leverage.** A coercer who could get Natasha to ask honestly would receive — and she knows it, and would not ask.

### Carol Danvers — the boozing peer

**First contact.** Postwar covert work (*Uncanny X-Men* #268; *Captain Marvel*-era ret-cons).

**Dynamic.** The one X-adjacent peer with whom drinking is the medium of relating, not a complication. She matches him at the bar and outranks him in chain of command; both are tolerable to him from her specifically.

**Trust/safety.** High; uncomplicated.

**Failure mode.** Long absences; neither maintains. The bond survives on resumability rather than maintenance.

### Ben Grimm — the bar friend

**First contact.** Crossover continuity, treated as durable across decades.

**Dynamic.** Cigars, beer, poker. Grimm is the only Fantastic-Four-adjacent figure with whom Logan is reliably comfortable; both men have somatic conditions they did not consent to, both metabolize this with self-deprecation rather than complaint. He plays cards with Grimm because Grimm cheats badly and does not pretend otherwise.

**Trust/safety.** High and trivial; that is the point.

**Failure mode.** N/A; designed for low stakes.

### Hercules / Power Pack-era oddities / "Patch"-era Madripoor allies (Archie Corrigan, Lindsay McCabe, Jessica Drew)

A consistent secondary cluster of *bar-stool family*: people who knew him as Patch in Lowtown, did not press him on his real identity, and earned trust through repeated non-betrayal in unstable conditions. Drew (Spider-Woman) in particular operates as a peer-sister in the *Wolverine* vol. 2 (1988) Madripoor run — she is permitted to call him on bullshit, and frequently does.

**Failure mode for this cluster:** geographic; when he leaves Madripoor, he ghosts them, and feels guilt without correcting the behavior.

### Yukio — the chaos friend

**First contact.** *Wolverine* limited series (1982, Claremont/Miller), Tokyo.

**Dynamic.** Yukio is *kindred* in the way Mariko was *aspirational*. She is reckless, mortal, mercenary, and laughing — she lives the way the berserker-self would live if it could hold a beer. Romantic charge present and never fully consummated as primary commitment; what they have instead is the permission to be each other's worst behavior without judgment.

**Evolution.** Reappears across decades. Co-parents Amiko Kobayashi with him after Mariko's death (see proteges, below).

**Trust/safety.** High for honesty, lower for reliability — by mutual agreement.

**Failure mode.** They will both choose the dangerous option together when one of them needs to choose the boring one.

**Leverage.** Yukio in unrelieved danger pulls him to Tokyo from anywhere on Earth.

---

## III. PROTEGES — THE GENERATIVE ZONE

*This is the cluster where his attachment system functions cleanly. The pattern across all five major proteges: he teaches them, specifically, how to survive someone like himself.*

### Kitty Pryde — the first daughter

**First contact.** *Uncanny X-Men* #129 (1980), recruited at thirteen. She fears him on sight; this is correct of her and he respects it.

**Dynamic.** The originating surrogate-paternal bond and the template for the others. Kitty is small, brilliant, frightened, and tougher than she looks — exactly the configuration that activates his reparative-parenting circuitry. The pedagogy is explicit: bladework (*Kitty Pryde and Wolverine*, 1984), Japanese language and etiquette, threat assessment, when to run, when not to. He does not protect her from danger; he equips her for it, which is the deeper protection and the one he wishes had been done for him.

**Evolution.** She is the first protege to grow into an *equal* — she eventually outranks him on the Quiet Council, captains the *Marauder*, and is one of the very few people he addresses as a peer without irony. The Ogun-possession arc forced an early, intense version of the *I would have to kill the daughter* scenario; both survived it; the relationship metabolized the trauma rather than rupturing.

**Trust/safety.** Maximal in both directions. She is among the small handful permitted to disagree with him publicly without consequence.

**Failure mode.** When Kitty is genuinely endangered, he stops being tactical and starts being a father — which sometimes degrades operational performance. He knows this and has accepted it as a cost.

**Leverage.** She is the single most exploitable point in his life. Multiple antagonists have correctly identified this; the Ogun arc is the canonical example, but the pattern recurs.

### Jubilation Lee (Jubilee) — the second daughter, the loud one

**First contact.** *Uncanny X-Men* #251 (1989), Australian outback; she follows him home like a stray after he is crucified by the Reavers and she cuts him down.

**Dynamic.** The relational opposite of Kitty: Jubilee is loud, performative, American-mall-rat, emotionally extroverted — and that is precisely the medicine. She forces him to be *funny* and *present* rather than brooding. The pedagogy is less formal; it is closer to a road-trip apprenticeship in survival heuristics. Throughout the *Wolverine* vol. 2 mid-period (1988–1995), she is his stabilizer; he is her holder.

**Evolution.** Vampire conversion (*Curse of the Mutants*, 2010) does not break the bond; later motherhood (Shogo) deepens it — he becomes a grandfather-figure, comfortably.

**Trust/safety.** High, with built-in mutual permission to be undignified.

**Failure mode.** He has occasionally underestimated her — treated her as the kid sister long after she had aged out of that role. She tolerates this and corrects it.

**Leverage.** Same as Kitty in principle; Jubilee's volatility makes her harder to use as a hostage because she will not cooperate in being one.

### Rogue — the protege he could not touch

**First contact.** Mid-1980s, post–*Avengers Annual* #10 defection; she joins the X-Men and he is the first to vouch for her against general distrust.

**Dynamic.** Specific and unusual. He recognized her *as the same kind of damaged* he is — manipulated by a maternal handler (Mystique), uncertain of her own autobiography, locked inside her own body. He vouched not despite this but because of it. The relationship has the surrogate-paternal valence with an extra layer: physical contact is impossible, so the protection is structural and verbal rather than tactile. He taught her how to be in a room with people she could kill by accident — a curriculum on which he is the world expert.

**Evolution.** Long, durable, mostly off-page in any given decade but reliably present in major events. She is one of his eulogists; he is one of her steady references.

**Trust/safety.** High; the no-touch constraint enforces a kind of conversational intimacy.

**Failure mode.** When she absorbs *him*, the dissociation problem becomes shared, which terrifies them both.

**Leverage.** Mystique. Always Mystique.

### Armor (Hisako Ichiki) — the Japanese reparation

**First contact.** *Astonishing X-Men* (Whedon era, 2004+).

**Dynamic.** The protege who carries the Japan-thread forward. Hisako is the daughter Mariko did not live to bear; he treats her with the formal courtesy he reserves for Japan specifically, and trains her in the disciplines Saburo trained him in. Lower-volume than Kitty/Jubilee, higher-stakes symbolically.

**Trust/safety.** High; protective register dominant.

**Failure mode.** He sometimes treats her as a *site* (of his Japan-grief) rather than a person; she has called him on this and he has corrected.

**Leverage.** Threats from Hand or Yashida-clan elements escalate his response disproportionately when she is involved.

### Laura Kinney (X-23) — the daughter who is the file

**First contact.** *X-23* origin (Kyle/Yost, 2004 onward); animated origin precedes comics. She is engineered from his genetic material by the program that finished what Weapon X started.

**Dynamic.** The most psychologically loaded protege relationship in the file, and — counterintuitively — the *most regulated.* Laura is, somatically and historically, his life redone with the trauma front-loaded and the regeneration intact. With her, he gets the one chance to parent the child-self who was made into a weapon. He takes it seriously: he does not flinch from her violence, he does not require her to be other than she is, and he teaches her the curriculum he wishes he had received — that the weapon does not have to be the person, that codes can be chosen, that there is a way to live that is not "in the snow alone."

**Evolution.** She succeeds him *as* Wolverine during his death period (*All-New Wolverine*, 2015); his return does not displace her. They co-hold the name. This is, in his life, an unprecedented act of generativity — letting the name be hers as much as his.

**Trust/safety.** Maximal. The cleanest attachment in the file.

**Failure mode.** When trigger-scent compulsion fires in her, it is the Weapon X nightmare wearing his daughter's face; he handles it, but at high internal cost. The Persephone-trigger arc in his own *Return* reactivated the same dread from the inside.

**Leverage.** Anyone capable of triggering her command-conditioning has, for one moment, total access to him.

### Amiko Kobayashi — the daughter taken in

**First contact.** *Wolverine* limited series #1–4 (1982); orphaned in a Tokyo fire he failed to prevent, then placed in Yukio's care.

**Dynamic.** Ward rather than apprentice; he is the long-distance father who pays in presence-when-needed rather than continuous parenting. He has acknowledged repeatedly that he is not equipped for daily fatherhood and that placing Amiko with Yukio was the *correct* parenting decision — a


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

*Dossier section 7.3. Cross-reference §3 (Attachment) and §5 (Pressure Points). The organizing claim of this section is empirical and falsifiable: the subject's rivals and his lovers are not distinct relational categories but a single category — **the people who get inside his perimeter** — sorted afterward by whether the encounter ended in sex or in claws. The behavioral mechanics are nearly identical: olfactory imprint, ritualized approach, deep recognition, then either bonding-via-violence or bonding-via-intimacy, and in every case the bond outlasts every reasonable expiration date. He keeps the dead and the despised in the same active file.*

---

## A. RIVALS & ENEMIES

### A.1 — Victor Creed ("Sabretooth")

**History.** The longest continuous relationship in the subject's life: documented antagonism spanning the late 19th century through the present, retconned and re-grounded across *Wolverine* vol. 2, *Sabretooth* (Tieri), *Wolverine: Origins* (Way), and the Hama run. Originally framed as father/son (a now-deprecated 1990s arc), then as Team X co-conscripts under shared Weapon Plus / CIA handling, then as something more etiologically primary: two long-lived feral mutants engineered, trained, or simply drawn into a predator pair-bond by the same shadow-organization (Romulus). The "birthday" ritual — Creed appearing annually to hunt him, frequently on or near the subject's putative birthday — is the only calendrical event the subject reliably observes.
