**Dynamics.** Mirror-pair, with one variable flipped: same senses, same healing factor, same century of war, same handlers, same memory-implants — and where the subject organized himself around the Bushidō ideal, Creed organized himself around the absence of any ideal at all. Creed is the subject's ASPD control case (cf. §4 Differential): the demonstration of what the subject would have been without the samurai-mask, without the protected-young attachment, without Rose. The hatred is therefore *constitutive* — Creed is the disowned material made into a person and given olfactory signature. He smells like the subject smells to himself in the worst moments.

**Evolution.** Five phases. (1) *Pre-WWII competitive coexistence* — colleagues, drinking partners in some accounts, with the violence latent. (2) *Team X period* — institutional sanction of their mutual aggression, with implanted memories blurring who did what to whom. (3) *Birthday-hunt era* (1980s–90s) — Creed escalates by targeting the subject's surrogate-children (Jubilee, intermittently; the *Wolverine* vol. 2 #10 home invasion at the Xavier mansion is canonical). (4) *Tyger Tiger / Madripoor period and after* — the rivalry weaponized by third parties (Hand, Apocalypse, Romulus). (5) *Krakoan period* — institutional cohabitation forced by resurrection protocols; the subject votes for Creed's exile to the Pit, an act of permanent containment short of murder. He cannot bring himself to make Creed permanently dead because Creed permanently dead is a subject permanently undefended against himself.

**Trust / safety.** Zero trust, complete predictability. This is the paradox: Creed is the most *legible* person in the subject's life. The subject knows the smell, the cadence, the opening move, the verbal repertoire ("Hey, runt"), the preferred targets. There is no ambiguity, no implanted memory between them that matters, no possibility of disappointment. In disorganized-attachment terms (§3), Creed functions as the dependable hostile object — the only durable presence from the pre-Weapon-X life that has neither died on the subject's claws nor been overwritten in his head.

**Failure mode.** The subject cannot end Creed and cannot ignore him. Attempts at resolution (the decapitation in *Wolverine* vol. 3 #55 by Muramasa blade; the various Krakoan votes) are structurally reversible and the subject lets them be reversed. When Creed is briefly "good" (the Tieri-era heart-implant arc) the subject is destabilized — he treats the reformation as a deeper insult than the predation.

**Leverage.** Anyone who controls Creed controls a guaranteed lure for the subject — used by Romulus, Hand, Mystique, and intermittently by SHIELD analogues. Conversely, the subject's behavior in Creed's presence is the most predictable behavioral signature in the file: arrive, escalate to claws within ninety seconds, fight to incapacitation, leave without conversation. If you need the subject in a specific geographic location on a specific day, deliver Creed there. (Cf. operational note in §5 — Creed's permanent removal is the *more* destabilizing option.)

---

### A.2 — Romulus

**History.** Introduced *Wolverine: Origins* #10 (Way, 2007). Ancient lupine-lineage mutant; positioned retroactively as the engineering intelligence behind a century of the subject's life — Team X assignments, the Weapon X procurement, the Daken project, Sabretooth's grooming, the recurring "test" of pitting the subject against beloved figures.

**Dynamics.** The unseen handler made visible. Where Creed is the disowned material as person, Romulus is the *agency* of violation as person — the personification of every instance in which the subject's autobiography was written by someone else. Hatred here is structurally different from Creed-hatred: cold, not hot; goal-directed, not ritual.

**Evolution.** The subject did not know Romulus existed for most of his life — that is the point. Discovery (Origins arc) produces not catharsis but a worsening of the identity-confusion syndrome: every memory the subject had reorganized around "my choice" must be re-examined for Romulus's fingerprints. The arc ends with imprisonment rather than execution because killing Romulus would not retroactively make the implanted decades the subject's own.

**Trust / safety.** Negative-infinity trust. Operational safety: low; Romulus's principal weapon was always proxy.

**Failure mode.** The subject's hunt for Romulus produces some of his most dissociated stretches of behavior on record — he becomes mission-shaped, sheds peripheral attachments, and treats the people around him as either assets or obstacles. The Romulus pursuit is the closest the conscious self comes to operating in the berserker mode without the berserker affect — *cold dissociation*.

**Leverage.** Now largely defused (Romulus contained), but the principle generalizes: any figure who can credibly claim to have authored portions of the subject's past activates the same compromised-cognition state. Mystique, Apocalypse, the Hand, and to a lesser extent Nick Fury all have partial access to this leverage profile.

---

### A.3 — The Weapon X Triad (Professor Thorton, Dr. Cornelius, Dr. Hines)

**History.** *Marvel Comics Presents* #72–84 (Windsor-Smith, 1991), with Cornelius recurring (*Death of Wolverine: The Logan Legacy*, *Death of Wolverine* 2014). The operational team that performed the adamantium bonding and the post-bonding behavioral conditioning.

**Dynamics.** Not enemies in the rivalrous sense — perpetrators in the clinical sense. The subject's relationship to them is the relationship of a torture survivor to torturers: depersonalized in the moment, then re-personalized retrospectively as the memory leaks back through the implant scaffolding. The *Death of Wolverine* arc — Cornelius attempting to repeat the procedure on a new generation — re-traumatizes by *literal reenactment*; the subject dies in a bath of liquid adamantium, i.e., re-bonded to the substance of the original violation. The somatic-symbolic loop closes.

**Trust / safety.** Inapplicable / lethal.

**Failure mode.** Sensory cues associated with the procedure (laboratory smells: ozone, surgical antiseptic, hot metal; the timbre of monitoring equipment; the click of restraint locks) reliably produce hyperarousal and frequently berserker dissociation. The subject avoids medical settings, refuses anesthesia where possible, and has on multiple occasions broken out of clinical environments unprovoked because the environmental cue load crossed threshold. He does not narrate this constraint to himself as flashback; he narrates it as preference. It is flashback.

**Leverage.** Any operation that wishes to incapacitate the subject psychologically rather than physically will recreate the Weapon X sensorium. Hydra (in the *Enemy of the State* arc) understood this.

---

### A.4 — The Hand (Matsu'o Tsurayaba, principal contact)

**History.** Recurring across the Claremont/Miller *Wolverine* (1982), the Hama run, *Wolverine* vol. 2 #57 (Mariko's poisoning, ordered/enabled via Hand-allied intrigue), and *Enemy of the State* (Millar, 2004) — in which the Hand and Hydra succeed at re-conditioning the subject into a brainwashed assassin who slaughters allies.

**Dynamics.** The Hand sits at the intersection of three of the subject's most loaded affective registers: Japan (the redemptive ritual space; §1), the violation of consent (memory/will overwrite; §4 etiology), and the recurring targeting of loved women. Matsu'o specifically delivered the poison that put Mariko in the position where she had to ask the subject to kill her. The subject's response — an annual ritual mutilation of Matsu'o, cutting off one piece each year on the anniversary of Mariko's death, sustained for many years until *Wolverine* vol. 3 #56 grants the final mercy stroke — is the cleanest behavioral diagnostic in the entire file. Compare to the Sabretooth birthday-hunt: same ritual structure, *inverted role*. The subject is here doing to Matsu'o what Creed does to him. This is one of the few places where the subject acknowledges, behaviorally, that he and Creed share an operating system.

**Trust / safety.** Lethal opposition, but with a paradoxical *familiarity*: the Hand operate in his own moral idiom (warrior code, ritual obligation, blade discipline), which makes them legible adversaries he can engage without dissociating in the way Cornelius's antiseptic-and-restraint sensorium produces.

**Failure mode.** The Hand penetrate his perimeter because they look like the version of himself he wants to be. *Enemy of the State* exploits exactly this: the conditioning works in part because the ritual framing (blade, kneel, oath) is congenial to the Bushidō self-image. The samurai ideal is the back door.

**Leverage.** Anyone who can deliver a credible Japanese ritual context can land an instruction the subject would resist from any other quarter. Operationally, this is the Mariko-pattern weaponized.

---

### A.5 — Apocalypse / En Sabah Nur (the "Death" overwrite)

**History.** *X-Men* #182–186 (Milligan, 2005); *Apocalypse Twelve* arc precursors. Apocalypse re-bonds the previously-extracted adamantium and converts the subject into Death, fourth horseman, with overwritten loyalty.

**Dynamics.** Of all the override events, this is the one that combines somatic violation (re-bonding to adamantium, repeating Weapon X) with ideological violation (forced service to an opposed worldview). It is the *complete* version of the recurring agentic violation pattern: body, will, and memory simultaneously.

**Trust / safety.** None; threat-class is closer to environmental hazard than to adversary.

**Failure mode.** Post-Death, the subject's identity-confusion syndrome worsens for a measurable arc — he is documented asking allies, repeatedly, whether specific past actions were "really me." This is the cleanest canonical depiction of identity-alteration aftermath on the Şar (2014) spectrum.

**Leverage.** Apocalypse demonstrated that the subject can be ridden by an outside intelligence given sufficient power asymmetry. Anyone who can credibly threaten a repeat (Selene, Genesis in the *Wolverine: Origins* arc, certain Sinister variants) activates a defensive posture the subject barely controls.

---

### A.6 — Magneto

**History.** Adversary across decades of X-Men canon; the relationship hinges on a single decisive event: *X-Men* #25 (1993), the magnetic extraction of the adamantium through the subject's skin, leaving him near-dead and exposing his original bone claws.

**Dynamics.** Not a personal hatred — an institutional one, complicated by occasional alignment (Krakoan Quiet Council). Magneto is one of the few adversaries the subject *respects* in the warrior sense; the extraction is the most physically catastrophic single injury in his medical record and yet does not produce the obsessive return that Weapon X or Romulus produce. The reason matters: Magneto's violation was *combat*, not betrayal. The subject's moral calculus distinguishes sharply.

**Trust / safety.** Provisional, contingent on context. In war: standard X-Men adversary protocols. In council: workable.

**Failure mode.** The subject overestimates Magneto's predictability because Magneto, like the subject, operates from a stated code. Disregards how much Magneto's code permits.

**Leverage.** Low — Magneto is not a button-pusher; he is a peer-level threat. The subject behaves with comparative composure around him.

---

### A.7 — Mystique (Raven Darkhölme)

**History.** Lovers, intermittently, across the Loeb/Bianchi *Wolverine* "Get Mystique" arc (2008) and earlier hinted encounters in the pre-X-Men decades — placed by various writers in the American West circa late 19th century. Then enemies for most of the modern period; she repeatedly puts protected persons in lethal contexts (Jubilee endangered, Daken manipulated, members of the X-Men misled by her shapeshifting).

**Dynamics.** The most categorically destabilizing person in the subject's relational field, because she is *simultaneously* a lover-coded figure and an enemy-coded figure and she controls which she presents as. Her shapeshifting weaponizes the olfactory trust the subject relies on — she can to varying degrees mask scent, and she knows which faces (Jean's, in some accounts) will land hardest. Mystique is the proof that the lover/enemy distinction is unstable in this subject's psychology: she is filed in both folders and he cannot reliably retrieve from one without the other coming with it.

**Evolution.** Early lover → distant antagonist → personal target ("Get Mystique" — he hunts her across continents and shoots her in the Afghan desert, an unusually cold and procedurally final act for him) → continued reappearance. The hunt is conducted in a notably *un*-berserker mode: cold, planned, durational. Compare Romulus pursuit.

**Trust / safety.** Negative trust under any face, including faces he wants to trust. This is the operational cost of having known her intimately.

**Failure mode.** A Mystique posing as a protected person occupies the worst quadrant of his pressure-point matrix (children-in-danger crossed with implanted-recognition); response time degrades, judgment narrows, he is exploitable in this specific configuration as in no other.

**Leverage.** Anyone employing Mystique against him buys themselves one free violation of his perimeter before he readjusts.

---

### A.8 — Daken (Akihiro)

**History.** Biological son with Itsu (*Wolverine: Origins*), raised from in-utero murder by Romulus / the Winter Soldier delivery context, conditioned for decades to despise the subject. *Dark Wolverine*, *Daken: Dark Wolverine*, the eventual drowning death in *Uncanny X-Force* #34 (Remender, 2012) at the subject's hands.

**Dynamics.** Daken occupies a category by himself: enemy-as-son. Every other adversarial relationship in the file is between the subject and an unrelated person; this one collapses the rival category into the failed-fatherhood category. Daken is the inverse of X-23 — same kind of genetic continuation, opposite kind of formative regime, opposite outcome.

**Evolution.** Discovery → attempted reclamation → repeated betrayals → containment attempts → the drowning in the Tar Pit during *X-Force*, in which the subject holds his son underwater until the regenerative cycle exhausts. This is the single most morally costly act on the subject's ledger and he carries it. The Krakoan-era partial reconciliation does not unmake the act; it accumulates onto it.

**Trust / safety.** None operational; unbearable nonetheless.

**Failure mode.** Daken can route around every defense the subject has by occupying the protected-young category and the lethal-enemy category simultaneously. The subject's response is to outsource Daken-handling where possible — he cannot reliably regulate his own behavior in his son's presence.

**Leverage.** Daken alive is a permanent destabilizer. Daken dead is a permanent shame ledger. There is no configuration of Daken that does not cost the subject something.

---

### A.9 — Lady Deathstrike (Yuriko Oyama)

**History.** Introduced *Daredevil* #197, repurposed across *Wolverine* vol. 2 and Reaver-era arcs (*Uncanny X-Men* #251 — the crucifixion). Adamantium-laced cybernetic adversary; vendetta inherited from her father, Lord Dark Wind, whose adamantium-bonding research underwrote the Weapon X procedure.

**Dynamics.** A vendetta the subject does not entirely contest, because he agrees with the premise that the adamantium-bonding lineage produced monstrous outcomes — he is one of them. Yuriko's hostility is directed at his existence as a *thief* of her father's process. The fights are physically punishing but psychologically clean: she is not trying to overwrite him, only to kill him.

**Trust / safety.** Hostile, predictable. He fights her with a strange courtesy.

**Failure mode.** Underestimates her durability because he reads her as grief-driven rather than ideologically driven; she is both.

**Leverage.** Low individual leverage; significant when paired with Reavers, Hand, or Cornelius-lineage actors who can frame her as part of a Weapon X reenactment.

---

### A.10 — Omega Red (Arkady Rossovich)

**History.** *X-Men* vol. 2 #4–7 (Lee, 1992). Soviet-era Weapon X analog; carbonadium tentacles, "death spore" pheromonal emission, shared Team X / Maverick / Sabretooth backstory tissue.

**Dynamics.** Adversary as Cold War mirror — Russian Weapon X to his American Weapon X. The subject's response is more political than personal: Omega Red represents the *generalization* of his violation to other state actors and other subjects. It deepens the conviction that he was one of many, which is paradoxically stabilizing (depersonalizes the Weapon X trauma to a category) and destabilizing (multiplies the number of handlers in the world who can do this again).

**Trust / safety.** Hostile.

**Failure mode.** The "carbonadium synthesizer" McGuffin recurringly puts the subject in possession of leverage over Omega Red, which he handles instrumentally rather than emotionally.

**Leverage.** Moderate; primarily a node in larger Weapon X conspiracies.

---

### A.11 — Ogun

**History.** *Kitty Pryde and Wolverine* limited series (Claremont/Milgrom, 1984). The subject's former sensei in Japan; revealed to be a body-jumping demonic adept who possesses Kitty Pryde, forcing the subject to either kill his student or destroy his teacher.

**Dynamics.** The diagnostically purest version of the recurring trap: the *teacher* who shaped the samurai ideal is revealed as a corrupting agent, and the *student* he was reparatively parenting is made the weapon. Every category — mentor, surrogate child, Bushidō, Japan — is simultaneously violated. The subject's behavior in the arc is unusually controlled and unusually grieving; he treats the rescue of Kitty as a Bushidō obligation rather than a berserker provocation, which is among the strongest evidence in the canon that the samurai practice *works* as a regulator when the loaded person is a protected child.

**Trust / safety.** Posthumous lethal; the ghost recurs.

**Failure mode.** Ogun is the proof that anyone the subject calls "sensei" has structural access to the most regulated part of him. He has not taken another teacher.

**Leverage.** Historical lessons from Ogun continue to shape his combat repertoire; he uses the techniques while disowning the source, an unstable compromise.

---

### A.12 — Shingen Yashida

**History.** Mariko's father; principal antagonist of *Wolverine* limited series #1–4 (Claremont/Miller, 1982).

**Dynamics.** The duel in which Shingen humiliates the subject with a wooden sword — outclassing him technically while the subject is operating from rage — is the foundational lesson of the samurai project: *the animal loses to the disciplined man.* The subject's eventual killing of Shingen is performed with a claw to the heart, declared in formal terms — "I am a man" — the explicit self-renunciation of the animal mask. That this self-renunciation does not stick is the point; the moment is repeated, in different costumes, for the rest of his life.

**Trust / safety.** Hostile, deceased.

**Failure mode.** The Shingen template — *contest of discipline with a paternal-coded older man* — is one the subject seeks out (Bando Saburo positively; Ogun catastrophically; Cyclops, in a different key, contentiously).

**Leverage.** N/A directly; structurally important as the model against which subsequent paternal-rival figures are scored.

---

## B. INTIMATES & LOVERS

*Operating principle for this subsection: every romantic attachment in the file activates a single load-bearing prediction — **"she will die because of me"** (the Rose/Itsu/Mariko template, §5). Behavior across decades and writers is consistent with the subject managing this prediction either by avoidance (frustrated idealization, withdrawal at point of consummation) or by deliberate selection of partners whose own lethality makes the prediction false (Natasha, Yukio, intermittently Domino). The pattern is not preference; it is risk management.*

---

### B.1 — Rose O'Hara

**History.** Childhood servant girl at the Howlett estate; companion through the post-trauma flight to the Yukon mining camp (*Origin* #1–6, Jenkins/Quesada/Kelly, 2001–02). Killed accidentally when the subject extrudes claws during a fight with Dog (Thomas Logan's son) and impales her.

**Dynamics.** First love, first loss, first death-on-the-claws. The originating instance of the template. Behaviorally encoded as: *the woman closest to me dies of my body, doing exactly what my body was designed for.*

**Trust / safety.** Posthumous; the memory itself was implanted-over for most of the subject's life and recovered only with *


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Subject: LOGAN — Capability Mapping

The standard intelligence error with this subject is to itemize his powers as a kit — claws, healing, senses — and stop there. The file approach is different: each capacity is mapped for *mechanism, operational envelope, demonstrated ceiling, demonstrated floor, growth/decay trajectory, signature use, and what the capacity reveals about the man who lives inside it.* The thesis the section will substantiate: every one of his powers is also a symptom, and he uses them, fights with them, and survives within them in ways that disclose the underlying dissociative-spectrum trauma syndrome already established in §3–4.

---

## 1. Regenerative Healing Factor

**Mechanism.** Accelerated mitotic regeneration of damaged tissue, coupled to elevated immunoresilience (toxin clearance, pathogen resistance) and a profoundly retarded senescence curve. The factor operates without conscious direction; he cannot will it faster, slower, or off. It scales — measurably — to the magnitude of insult: a cigar burn closes in seconds, a 9mm wound in tens of seconds, blade and shrapnel wounds in minutes, organ destruction in hours, near-total tissue obliteration in days. The factor is metabolically expensive: large-scale regrowth produces measurable food-and-water demand spikes, observable lethargy windows, and (post-Apocalypse vivisection, *Wolverine* vol. 2 #145) extended convalescence.

**Operational envelope.** Demonstrated recoveries include: full musculature regrowth from skeleton (Genesis arc); regrowth of soft tissue from a charred adamantium frame; survival of point-blank ordnance, immersion in lava, atmospheric re-entry temperatures, and prolonged anoxia. Demonstrated *failures*: drowning in liquid adamantium asphyxiates the regeneration itself because the encasement prevents the cells from clearing the cardiopulmonary obstruction (*Death of Wolverine*, 2014); Muramasa-blade wounds and carbonadium impedance suppress the factor locally and persistently; biological neutralizers (Persephone-class agents, the Carbonadium Synthesizer fragments) bring him to a normal-human attrition curve within hours. Healing is not invulnerability; it is *deferral of mortality through repeated experience of dying*.

**Growth curve.** Across the canon the factor has been *narratively* uprated (1974 baseline: heals from a stabbing in panel-time hours; 1990s onward: routine resurrection from skeletal-only states) but the structural truth holds across recalibrations: it tracks the writer's need to escalate threat. Operationally, treat the factor as effectively limitless against conventional weapons, bounded by (a) factor-suppressors, (b) ongoing-encasement scenarios, (c) magic and soul-class injuries, (d) attacks that out-scale regeneration rate at the moment of insult (decapitation by adamantium edge would, on balance of evidence, kill him).

**Signature use.** Tactically: he walks into killing fire. The combat doctrine is *interpose, absorb, close, kill at conversation distance.* He uses his own body as the breaching tool — to enter rooms through walls of bullets, to grapple weapons by closing on the blade, to take the hostage's wound. He has, on multiple recorded occasions, allowed himself to be impaled to fix an enemy in place for a counterstrike (the "skewer-and-step-through" maneuver appears from Claremont's first run forward).

**Symptom-as-signature.** The factor has trained him, across thirteen decades, that *no injury is final*. In any non-mutant the behavioral profile he displays — habitual exposure of self to lethal force, refusal of armor, refusal of cover, ingestion of substances at toxicity-threshold quantities, willingness to be set on fire as a tactical option — would constitute parasuicidality, and would be charted as such. In him it reads as competence. The file should not let the physiology launder the behavior: the man *wants out frequently enough* that the wish has organized his fighting style. The low-grade lifelong death-wish identified in §5 is somatically expressed here as a willingness to repeatedly experience dying without expecting death.

---

## 2. Bone Claws / Adamantium-Bonded Claws

**Mechanism.** Three retractable osseous projections per forearm, anatomically integral to the ulnar/radial complex rather than implanted weaponry; the adamantium bonding sheathed the existing bone. Extrusion is voluntary, fast (sub-second), and traverses the dorsal hand fascia between the metacarpals — meaning every extrusion lacerates his own hand. The healing factor closes the wound immediately on retraction. Each extrusion is therefore *self-wounding by design*.

**Operational envelope.** Adamantium edge severs effectively any non-adamantium material at hand-tool scale: steel rebar, vehicle armor, masonry, bone. Penetration is limited by his own muscular drive and reach, not by edge integrity. Range: ~12 inches of blade beyond the fist. The claws cannot be disarmed, dropped, or taken from him while he lives, which is their decisive tactical property. Bone-claw periods (post-Magneto adamantium extraction, *X-Men* #25, through Apocalypse re-bonding) showed reduced cutting power, identical reach, identical psychological function; he fought no less aggressively without the metal.

**Demonstrated control.** He can extrude one, two, or three claws per hand independently; partial extrusion (an inch, for warning or fine work) is documented. Fine motor use — engraving, cigar trimming, lockpicking — appears throughout the Claremont/Hama runs. The claws are not only weapons; he uses them as can-opener, climbing piton, surgical instrument (self-extracted bullets, several instances), and silent signal.

**Signature use.** The *snikt* is a verbal punctuation mark as much as a tactical action. He extrudes claws conversationally to threaten, to refuse, to grieve, and — most diagnostically — alone, in private, as a self-soothing tic. The single-claw point-out (one claw at the throat, two retracted) is his signature interrogation tool: maximum precision, minimum lethality, maximum unspoken information. In berserker states the extrusion is reflexive and constant; the claws stay out for the duration of the episode and he often regains consciousness with them still extended.

**Symptom-as-signature.** This is the central somatic fact of the file. *His primary defensive act is self-injury.* Every time he protects himself or another, he opens four wounds in his own hands. The healing factor erases the visible evidence but does not erase the conditioning: pain is the prerequisite of agency. Read against the §3 Bushidō ideal and the §4 dissociation framework, the claws are not a weapon-system; they are a daily, repeating, neurologically-encoded enactment of *I bleed to do this.* A century of this is not behaviorally neutral. It is the embodied template for every other choice he makes — that protecting is wounding, that intimacy injures, that to extend himself is to be cut.

---

## 3. Hyperacute Sensorium

**Mechanism.** Olfaction at canine-or-better thresholds (parts-per-trillion class discriminations, individual scent-signature recognition retained across decades, ability to track at distance and across water under favorable conditions). Audition into ranges typically inaudible to human ears, with directional resolution adequate for echolocation in zero-visibility. Vision with low-light adaptation and acuity above human norms. Touch and proprioception elevated. The sensorium is *always on*; there is no off-switch, no eyelid-equivalent for nose or ear.

**Operational envelope.** He can identify: a specific person by scent through walls; a lie, by autonomic markers (perspiration, cortisol, micro-changes in respiration); arousal, fear, illness, pregnancy, recent intercourse, recent weapon-handling, alcohol or drug intake, the brand of cigarette someone smoked an hour ago, the gun oil on a holstered weapon, the make of explosive in a sealed case. Operationally treat him as a walking forensic instrument with retained scent-memory across the entire active period of his life.

**Limits.** Sensory overload is real and exploitable: strong masking agents (industrial solvents, mustard-class chemicals, Mystique's pheromonal mimicry on occasion), confined high-stimulus environments (firefights in enclosed spaces, fires, sewer pursuits), and synthetic scent-jammers degrade tracking. Information density can exceed processing — in crowds and in combat he runs hot, which interacts with §4 to lower the berserker threshold.

**Growth curve.** Stable across the canon at high baseline; episodic enhancements (when the healing factor is uprated, senses are uprated proportionally). Skill-side growth: a century of training has converted raw sensory data into expert interpretation. He does not merely smell — he reads.

**Signature use.** Tracking is the discipline he most respects in himself. He works a scent trail with formal patience uncharacteristic of his other modalities — head low, slow gait, repeated cross-cuts, the body language of a working hound. The investigative posture is one of the few states in which he is observably *calm.* He uses scent as memory cue: a person's smell triggers durable recall in him that visual recognition does not, which has both tactical and pathological consequences (Sabretooth's scent, the Weapon X facility's scent-signature, can trigger acute dissociative reactions).

**Symptom-as-signature.** The hypersenses are the anatomical substrate of his hypervigilance. §3 noted that in him hypervigilance is partly imposed by anatomy; this is where it lives. He cannot *not* know that the woman across the bar is afraid, that the man two tables over has fired a gun this morning, that the bartender's marriage is failing. Normal human social filtration — the merciful dimming that lets people coexist — is unavailable to him. The withdrawal pattern, the preference for wilderness, the bar-stool-in-the-corner posture, the readiness to leave town: all are *sensory ergonomics* as much as personality. He retreats because the room is loud in ways no one else can hear.

---

## 4. Berserker State (Dissociative Combat Mode)

**Mechanism.** Under threshold-breach conditions — harm to a protected person, signature-enemy scent cue, sustained sensory overload coupled to perceived entrapment — consciousness narrows or splits; behavior becomes automatized; verbal output reduces to growls and short imperatives; tactical sophistication *increases* in some dimensions (target acquisition, environmental use) and collapses in others (discrimination of friend from foe, restraint thresholds). Subsequent amnesia for the episode is partial-to-complete and characteristically patchy in the manner the Şar (2014, 2022) framework predicts for acute dissociative reactions.

**Operational envelope.** In berserker mode he has cleared rooms of trained operators, taken sustained injury that would incapacitate his baseline state, and fought through factor-suppression that would otherwise drop him. The state extends his functional combat duration and damage tolerance — at the cost of control. Recorded incidents of friendly-fire injury during berserker episodes exist across the canon; he has come back to find teammates wounded by him.

**Triggers.** (a) Specific olfactory signatures (Sabretooth, Weapon X personnel, Hand chemistry); (b) the configuration *child in danger* (overrides everything, per §5); (c) replication of original-trauma conditions (restraint + surgical implements + bright light, recurrent across abduction arcs); (d) cumulative sensory load past a threshold he cannot consciously meter.

**Voluntary access.** Partial. Across the Claremont and post-Claremont runs he learns — under Ogun, under the Yashida disciplines, in long meditation periods — to *enter* the state semi-voluntarily and to *exit* it earlier than uncontrolled episodes would. He never achieves reliable *suppression.* The training converts an acute dissociative reaction into something closer to a controllable altered state, but the underlying mechanism remains dissociation, not anger.

**Symptom-as-signature.** This is not a power. It is a symptom listed in the powers section because the canon treats it as one. The file should be explicit: the berserker state is an acute dissociative reaction within his CPTSD/dissociative syndrome (§4), repackaged narratively as a combat capacity. Its operational value is real; its etiological status is pathological. The two facts coexist. The Bushidō practice, the meditation, the kata, the formal etiquette periods in Japan, are *prosthetic affect regulation* applied to a dissociative threshold he cannot otherwise raise.

---

## 5. Retarded Aging

**Mechanism.** Cellular-senescence inhibition, secondary to the healing factor; apparent biological age stabilized at mid-40s for over a century of chronological time. No measurable cognitive decline; no measurable physical decline outside factor-suppression intervals.

**Operational envelope.** Functional immortality on human timescales, bounded by the mortality conditions itemized in §1.

**Symptom-as-signature.** The cost is psychological, not somatic. He has outlived essentially every non-mutant he has loved. Rose, Itsu, Silver Fox, Mariko, Carol's earlier era, every Yashida elder, every wartime comrade who was not also enhanced. The protective bonds with adolescent girls (§3) are partly a function of this fact: he reliably re-enters phases where a vulnerable young person needs a guardian who will outlast their enemies. The Old Man Logan presentation (§1) is in part what fifty years of grief looks like in a body that will not let grief kill it. Longevity in him is a *prolonged exposure protocol* to loss without the natural endpoint that ends exposure.

---

## 6. Skill Stack — Acquired Capacities Across 130+ Years

The mutant abilities are inseparable from a century-plus of skill accretion. The intelligence value of the file depends on charting these as carefully as the powers.

**Combat.** Expert across edged weapons (katana, tantō, knife — Bushidō-trained, Yashida lineage), unarmed striking and grappling (multiple traditions; observed jiu-jitsu, karate, military combatives, Western boxing), firearms (military-grade, sniper-capable but disprefers — see below), explosives, vehicle-borne combat. Equally lethal in close quarters and at distance, but *strongly* prefers close. The preference is psychological: at sword range he can read the opponent's micro-tells and scent; at rifle range he cannot, and engagement at distance does not satisfy the discharge requirement of §3.

**Languages.** Documented working fluency in English, Japanese, Russian, German, French, Chinese (Mandarin and at least one regional), Spanish, Lakota and at least one other Indigenous North American language; functional in additional tongues per situational appearance. The polyglot profile is consistent with a century of operational deployment across theaters.

**Tradecraft.** Surveillance, counter-surveillance, infiltration, exfiltration, document forgery, alias maintenance (the *Patch* identity in Madripoor is the canonical exemplar — sustained operational cover with separate dress, gait, eye-patch, and verbal register), interrogation, evasion. The Team X period and the postwar mercenary/CIA work are the training base.

**Wilderness.** Tracking (with and without the senses), trapping, hunting, foraging, cold-weather survival, navigation without instruments. The feral-living periods produced a substrate the senses then amplified.

**Vehicles.** Motorcycles (signature), light aircraft, helicopters (Blackbird-class as part of X-Men operational training), boats, horses (the Alberta upbringing and the early-century military service).

**Cultural / contemplative.** Bushidō (the load-bearing organizing system of his higher functioning); meditation practice; tea ceremony and formal Japanese etiquette to a level enabling integration with the Yashida clan; bar-craft and the working-class North American idiom that constitutes his default social camouflage.

**Pedagogy.** Substantial, under-credited. He has trained — to operational competence — Kitty Pryde, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, Surge, Hellion's cohort, X-23, and others. His teaching method is observable and consistent: high expectations, low praise, durable presence, scenario-based instruction, refusal to do the work for the student, and (the diagnostic feature) explicit instruction in *surviving him* — how to read his moods, when to disengage, what his triggers smell like.

**Symptom-as-signature.** The skill stack is enormous and the autobiographical record of acquiring it is fragmentary. He knows how to do things he does not remember learning. This is one of the most destabilizing features of his lived experience: competence without provenance. He has woken in a sparring stance from a style he cannot name; spoken languages he does not recall studying; executed tradecraft drills with no memory of training. The skills are evidence of a life he cannot access, which is why memory-restoration arcs (House of M, the post-Origins recoveries) are simultaneously relieving and devastating — they confirm that the competent stranger inside him is in fact himself.

---

## 7. Limits, Vulnerabilities, and Exploits

For the operational section of the file, the exploitable surface:

- **Factor suppression.** Carbonadium, Muramasa-edge wounds, Persephone-class biochemistry, Mister Sinister's targeted countermeasures, the Microverse atmospheric conditions in select arcs. Within hours of suppression he is a high-skill normal-human combatant — formidable but mortal.
- **Encasement.** Anything that fixes him in place faster than the factor can adapt: liquid adamantium, sustained stasis fields, deep burial. Drowning, asphyxiation, and ongoing crush injuries scale poorly against regeneration because the insult is continuous.
- **Magic and soul-class attacks.** The factor is a somatic system; magical, psychic, and soul-targeted insults route around it. Telepathic intrusion has consistently been one of his vulnerabilities, mitigated only by Xavier-installed mental shielding that periodically fails.
- **Memory and identity attack.** Per §4: an adversary who can credibly destabilize his autobiography lands a blow the factor cannot close. Hand, Hydra, Romulus, Apocalypse, the Weapon X program itself, have all demonstrated this. The same exploit, applied today, would work again.
- **Children-in-danger override.** Documented exploit. Recruits him to suboptimal tactics, into traps, against his own faction.
- **Sensory overload and masking.** Industrial-scale olfactory jamming, sustained high-decibel environments, pheromonal mimicry.
- **The configured-beloved scenario.** The Rose / Itsu / Mariko template (§5). A high-skill adversary who structures a confrontation so that the woman he loves must die by his hand or in his presence achieves a psychological wound the factor never repairs.
- **Peace.** Underrated. Unstructured time without a mission and without a young person to protect produces decompensation faster than combat. He is most vulnerable when nothing is wrong.

---

## 8. Integration

The capability map and the psychiatric map are the same map. His healing factor trains parasuicidality. His claws make self-wounding the prerequisite of agency. His senses make hypervigilance anatomical. His berserker state is an acute dissociative reaction operationalized as a combat capacity. His longevity is prolonged-exposure to grief. His skill stack is competence without recoverable autobiography. The pedagogical instinct is reparative parenting routed through expertise. The Bushidō discipline is prosthetic affect regulation worn as a culture.

A century and a third of this has produced a fighter of unusual quality and a person of unusual cost. The powers are not separable from the symptoms; the symptoms are not separable from the man. The file's working assumption — and the operational implication for any party planning to engage, recruit, oppose, or support him — is that you cannot use the capacities without activating the pathology, and you cannot treat the pathology without disarming the capacities. He has been navigating this trade-off, alone, since before most of his colleagues' grandparents were born. He has gotten very good at it. He has not gotten well.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*File section 6 of the workup. Cross-reference §1 (history), §3 (psychological), §5 (personality). What follows is the operational reverse-engineering: how the subject moves, decides, kills, hides, funds himself, and signals — derived from a hundred and thirty years of observable behavior across the canon (Wein 1974 → Hickman/Duggan/Percy present).*

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

**Time-to-decision: anomalously short, anomalously stable.** The subject does not deliberate the way comparably experienced operators deliberate. The sensorium (§2 of the workup — hyperacute olfaction, audition, proprioception) supplies a continuous unconscious threat-grade on every body in the room; decisions are felt before they are reasoned. He has described this in his own internal monologue across writers (Claremont, Hama, Aaron) as *knowing* who the threat is before the situation has resolved. Operationally this means he commits to an action one to two beats before any conventional operator would commit, and almost never reverses mid-commitment.

**The cost of that speed.** False positives are common and unrecoverable. Once the claws are out he has poor mid-action override; the same compressed decision cycle that wins him fights also produces the catastrophic misreads that recur in his record (Mariko-by-his-hand, the Hand-controlled assault on the X-Mansion in *Enemy of the State*, the *Old Man Logan* slaughter under Mysterio). His decision system has no built-in latency for the case where his senses are being deceived. He knows this about himself. It is the single greatest source of his self-loathing and the reason he prefers to operate alone when senses are suspect.

**Three-tier decision stack.**
- *Tier 1 — Sensorium-driven autonomic response.* Sub-second. Threat localization, lethality assessment, movement. Most of his combat operates here.
- *Tier 2 — Tactical reasoning.* Seconds-to-minutes. Terrain reading, exit selection, target priority (he prioritizes by smell of intent, not by rank — the most committed killer in a room dies first, regardless of nominal status).
- *Tier 3 — Strategic / moral reasoning.* Slow, often retrospective. Frequently runs *after* the operation in the form of brooding, prayer at small Shinto-style shrines, or alcohol. This is the tier where Bushidō lives. Tier 3 produces apologies, gravesite visits, hospital bills paid anonymously, and the protective decisions about which young people to extract from which lives.

**The fail-state.** When Tier 1 escalates past a threshold (smell of specific historical enemies, harm to a protected adolescent, captivity by surgical adversaries) the berserker dissociation cuts Tiers 2 and 3 out of the loop entirely. The episode runs to completion. He does not remember it cleanly afterward. This is not a tactic; it is a *failure mode that has been weaponized against him repeatedly* (Romulus, Hand, Apocalypse) precisely because it removes his strategic judgment from the field.

---

## 2. PRIMARY OPERATIONAL MODES

He runs in five distinguishable modes, switched between by context. They are stable across decades; observers (Xavier, Nick Fury, the Yashida household, Heather Hudson) have all noted the transitions.

**Mode A — Pointman/Tracker.** Lead element on insertion. Moves ahead of the team by anywhere from fifty meters to a kilometer. Reads ground, scent, sound. Reports back in clipped half-sentences. This is the role X-Men ops have used him in since *Giant-Size* #1 and it is the one he prefers because it minimizes the friction of working in formation.

**Mode B — Solo wetwork.** The X-Force role (Kyle/Yost, Remender). Pre-authorized lethality. Targets isolated. No witnesses if avoidable. Cleanup self-managed. He operates this mode reluctantly but competently — the reluctance is the *point*, because anyone who likes it (Sabretooth, Daken pre-redemption) is precisely whom he was made to be and refuses to remain.

**Mode C — Embedded mentor.** Schoolteacher, dojo instructor, "Headmaster" role (Aaron's *Wolverine and the X-Men*). Pedagogical and protective. He runs students through realistic threat drills and explicitly trains them to be more disciplined than he is. The infrastructure of this mode — class schedules, gradebooks, faculty meetings — is *prosthetic structure* for his own affect regulation as much as it is service to the school.

**Mode D — Undercover / "Patch."** The Madripoor identity (Claremont/Buscema, *Wolverine* vol. 2, 1988+). Operates from a known bar (the Princess Bar), maintains a transparent-pretense cover (the eyepatch fools no one who matters; the *point* of it is that it signals "do not formally recognize me"), trades in information, settles local accounts. This is the mode in which he is most relaxed because the rules are explicit and the population is self-selected.

**Mode E — Exile.** Cabin in Alberta or the Yukon, or wandering the continental northwest, or the high country in Japan. No comms. Game-trapped food. Manual labor when he needs cash. Cycles in and out of this mode every few years; the trigger is almost always a moral failure he cannot metabolize in company. The mode looks like quitting and is not quitting — it is decompression and a deliberate, monitored test of whether he can tolerate being alone with himself yet. He often cannot, and returns.

---

## 3. COMBAT TRADECRAFT

**Doctrine.** *Close the distance, control the geometry, end it before adrenaline metabolizes.* He prefers contact range. He is competent at distance work (rifle, bow, thrown blade) but does not lead with it; standoff weapons separate him from the sensory feedback his decision system requires.

**Movement.** Low center of gravity (he is canonically 5'3" in classic continuity, taller in modernized renderings; the build is stocky regardless). Uses his height as an advantage — he fights *underneath* the swing planes of taller opponents and reaches the femoral/popliteal/abdominal lines they cannot easily defend. Lateral movement preferred to retreat. He almost never gives ground in a straight line; he gives ground at an angle that sets up the counter.

**Use of claws.** First extrusion is usually a *display*, not a strike — a controlled warning at conversational range, often paired with a verbal preamble ("Bub, you don't want to do this"). If the warning is unheeded the second motion is committed and lethal. He uses the claws as picks (climbing, breaching), as can-openers (vehicle armor, restraint cuffs, locks), and as surgical instruments (he has performed field tracheotomies and bullet extractions on himself and others). He extrudes one claw rather than three when the application is precise rather than lethal — an under-noted operational detail that distinguishes him from his imitators.

**Weapons beyond claws.** Comfortable with most small arms, prefers not to carry them. Maintains genuine and not theatrical proficiency with the katana and the wakizashi (Yashida-house training); the Muramasa blade arc (Daniel Way) is significant because that blade *can* kill him, and he has used it sparingly, with awareness of its irreversibility, as a calibration tool against the worst of himself. He has historical familiarity with the Lewis gun, the Thompson, the M1 Garand, the AK pattern, the M4 — a century of small-arms drift. He does not fetishize hardware.

**The healing factor as tactic.** He *uses* injury. Will take a blade or a burst to close distance and finish an opponent who would otherwise escape. The calculation is invisible to most enemies and is part of why he is so difficult to engage — the normal cost-benefit of trading hits does not apply to him. The corollary is that he treats his own body as expendable infrastructure, which produces the parasuicidal flavor noted in §2 of the workup.

**Vehicle/terrain.** Comfortable in wilderness above all (a century of it). Competent urban operator but visibly less relaxed; the sensorium is overloaded in cities. Drives motorcycles (preference; the open posture suits his hearing/smell); flies fixed-wing prop (learned mid-20th-century, never quite trusted jets); operates small craft on water. Does not pilot the Blackbird as primary, will if forced.

**Interrogation.** A specialty, and one of the few areas where his reputation overstates rather than understates the reality. The threat is credible because the *demonstrated* willingness to maim is credible. He prefers to extract information by structured intimidation: cataloging the subject's anatomy aloud, naming their relatives, allowing the subject's own imagination to do most of the work. He inflicts less actual injury than most witnesses remember inflicting. He has rules he does not articulate but adheres to: no children, no civilians, no torture for entertainment, never go past what is required to get the answer.

---

## 4. INTELLIGENCE TRADECRAFT

**Collection.** Primarily HUMINT, conducted in bars and back rooms across a network of contacts a century deep. He remembers people his cognitive memory does not — recognizes them by scent across decades. This is an operational asset no other intelligence operator in his peer group possesses and he exploits it constantly without naming it.

**Networks.** 
- *Madripoor:* the Princess Bar, O'Donnell behind the counter (in classic continuity), the lowlife brokerage that flows through that single node. Tyger Tiger as a fence and ally.
- *Japan:* the residual Yashida network (degraded post-Mariko, partially restored through Amiko Kobayashi, the adopted daughter he placed with Yukio for safekeeping), Yukio herself as an irregular, contacts within the Tokyo PD and the rural Shinto temple network in Jasmine Falls.
- *North America:* SHIELD/Avengers institutional access through Rogers and through Fury (both the elder and the successor); the Canadian intelligence community through residual Department H/Alpha Flight ties (compromised, not severed); the X-Men's own intelligence apparatus; a long-standing relationship with selected Hellfire-adjacent figures (operationally useful, personally distrusted).
- *Eastern Europe / former Soviet sphere:* legacy ties from the Romanova/Danvers Madripoor mission (*Uncanny X-Men* #268) and from interwar/wartime work.
- *Latin America and the Caribbean:* thinner, mostly mission-specific.
- *Krakoan period:* Quiet Council seat and access to X-Force's intelligence product; this is the most institutionally embedded he has ever been and he is visibly uncomfortable with it even when using it well.

**Counter-intelligence on himself.** He assumes — correctly — that he is a recurring target for re-conditioning. He maintains *test phrases* and *test memories* with trusted intimates (Rogers, Kurt, occasionally Jean) used to detect when his behavior has been overridden. He has prepositioned letters with attorneys to be opened in the event of certain behavioral signatures. He has been known to surrender his weapons voluntarily to allies when he suspects a trigger has been planted. After *Enemy of the State* and after the Persephone protocols in *Return of Wolverine*, this counter-intelligence on himself becomes more formal and more paranoid.

**OPSEC habits.** Uses cash. Maintains physical paper records in caches (cabin in Canada, footlocker in the Princess Bar, a deposit box network across at least four cities). Suspicious of biometrics and of any digital identity system; the Krakoan resurrection records bother him in a way he does not fully articulate because they constitute the most complete dossier on him ever assembled and it is held by people who, however benevolent, have once already encoded him as a weapon.

---

## 5. INFRASTRUCTURE AND FINANCE

**Residences (operational, not exhaustive).**
- Multiple safehouse-grade cabins in Alberta and the Yukon — log construction, off-grid, weapons cached, no neighbors within sound of a rifle.
- Rooms above the Princess Bar in Madripoor's Lowtown.
- A small house in or near Jasmine Falls, Japan, maintained through the Yashida residuum.
- His suite at the Xavier school / Krakoan equivalent.
- Transient short-stays in working-class motels off interstate routes when in transit; preference for ground-floor rooms with rear exits and a view of the parking lot.

**Caches.** Weapons, cash in multiple currencies, false identity documents in various stages of staleness, medical supplies (largely for others — he requires few), spare clothing in the heavy-flannel/denim register he favors, at minimum one cold-weather kit per cache. Some caches predate WWII and are sporadically refreshed.

**Finance.** A century of intermittent earnings handled, on the evidence, with surprising adequacy. Sources: military pay (multiple armies), CIA/Team X compensation, Department H salary, X-Men stipend, Madripoor operations (legitimate and otherwise), Yashida-clan financial residue (contested and partial), occasional well-paid private contracts, intermittent income from teaching. Storage: physical cash in caches, holdings under aliases (the alias archaeology alone would fill a separate file — "Patch," "Logan," "Jim Logan," "Emilio Garra," "Mr. Canada" and at least a dozen others), some legitimately invested under counsel. He is not wealthy by the standards of his peers (Stark, Worthington) and does not aspire to be. He keeps enough to disappear with on a day's notice and enough to fund a small mission without asking permission.

**Logistical preferences.** Travels light. One bag, ideally a duffel. Wears clothing he can fight in (denim, flannel, leather, boots laced specifically — double-knotted, never tucked in a way that catches). Reluctant air-traveler when commercial, prefers driving or institutional aircraft. Acquires local clothing on arrival in unfamiliar regions to lower his profile; the cowboy hat, the gi, the suit-and-tie — he can wear any of them, none with full comfort.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE BEHAVIORAL TELLS

The granular detail a surveillance file would carry. These are the patterns by which a competent watcher confirms the subject in a crowd, predicts the next move, and notices when he has been replaced or compromised.

**Static body tells.**
- Stands with weight forward, slight squat, hands loose at thigh-line — a fighter's neutral, not a civilian's. Maintains this even at funerals and parent-teacher meetings.
- Habitually positions himself with his back to a wall and line-of-sight to the primary entrance. In restaurants he requests a specific table or trades for one; in lecture halls he stands rather than sits.
- Scans rooms in a consistent left-to-right sweep on entry, then re-checks the exit behind him before he commits to a seat. This is a sub-second behavior and reliable.
- When seated and ostensibly relaxed, one boot remains flat on the floor in a posture from which he can rise immediately. He almost never crosses his legs.

**Olfactory/auditory tells.**
- Pause-and-incline-of-head when registering a familiar scent at distance. Brief, almost imperceptible; watchable.
- Pupil dilation and nostril flare when scent-tagged to a hostile (Sabretooth's signature in particular produces an immediate posture change).
- Will track a conversation across a crowded room while ostensibly engaged in another. Tells himself by occasional inappropriate timing in his nearer conversation.

**Hand tells.**
- The dorsal hand scars from claw extrusion are present and never fully fade between extrusions; they are a watchable bio-tell.
- When affect rises, the dorsal hand muscles tense in the pre-extrusion pattern even when he has chosen not to extrude. A trained observer can watch his hand and know whether the next claw is going to come out.
- Knuckle-cracking and a brief flex of the forearm before a meeting he expects to be hostile — a self-soothing pre-flight check.

**Verbal/paralinguistic tells.**
- "Bub." Direct-address marker used with strangers, near-strangers, and antagonists; never with intimates. Frequency of "bub" in a conversation is inversely correlated with how dangerous he considers the listener — it drops out as threat assessment rises.
- "Darlin'." Reserved for women he has classified as non-threats or as protected. Misuse of "darlin'" — by him or by an impostor — is diagnostic.
- "Snikt" / "snakt" as actual vocalization of claw extrusion: a meta-textual joke in the comics, but operationally there *is* a distinct mechanical noise the extrusion produces (bone or adamantium through fascia) that he has long since learned to muffle when stealth is required. He can extrude silently. The audible extrusion is a deliberate display.
- Speech pattern: contracted, dropped consonants ("th'" for "the"), occasional Canadian residue ("aboot" softened, "eh" sparingly), faint Albertan rural baseline. Under stress the dialect deepens. Under dissociation it disappears — he becomes monosyllabic or wordless, which is itself diagnostic.

**Habitual rituals.**
- Cigar after combat. Ritualized and consistent across writers since the 1980s; the cigar serves as a paced-breathing exercise and a closure ceremony.
- A specific drink order in most bars (beer-and-shot configuration, regionalized). The bar itself is the ritual more than the drink — he metabolizes the alcohol fast and what he is consuming is *the place*.
- Visits to graves. He keeps a roster of dates and locations and shows up. Mariko, Jean (variably, given resurrection logistics), Itsu, Charles when applicable, Kurt as needed. He brings sake or whisky depending on the recipient and the culture.
- Maintenance of a small Shinto-style shrine in his residence wherever the residence is fixed enough to permit one. Watched only by intimates; he does not advertise it.
- Quiet hand-washing rituals after combat — meticulous, longer than functionally necessary, particularly attentive to the dorsal hand. Mariko's blood, Itsu's blood, Rose's blood — the ritual exists for them.

**Operational micro-tells (counterintelligence-grade).**
- Will not eat food prepared out of his sight without a discreet scent check.
- Reads menus with the menu held low and angled so it does not block sightlines.
- In any vehicle he does not drive, sits in the seat with the best egress (rear passenger-side in a sedan; aisle in any aircraft).
- Pays bar tabs in advance or after each round — he does not run a tab he cannot walk out on.
- Does not sign his actual signature on anything optional; carries multiple plausible signature variants for the alias network.
- When uninjured will favor a slight limp in unfamiliar territory — a long-standing habit from the early espionage years to suggest he is less mobile than he is.

---

## 7. RELATIONSHIP TO HANDLERS AND INSTITUTIONS

He has been *handled* — in the intelligence sense — more than any operator of his peer group: Department H, CIA, Weapon X program, Hand, Hydra, Romulus, Apocalypse, and arguably Xavier and the Quiet Council in their gentler institutional forms. Each instance has terminated badly. His baseline working assumption with any institution is that it intends to use him and will eventually attempt to override him.

He manages this by:
- *Reserving exit.* He keeps an exfiltration option from every operation, including operations he initiated.
- *Limiting briefings.* He prefers to be told the target and the constraints, not the strategic rationale, because rationale-level briefings are the channel through which manipulation enters.
- *Selective insubordination.* He breaks chain of command when his sensorium contradicts the brief. This is reliable enough that competent commanders (Cyclops in his better periods, Fury, Rogers) have learned to factor it in as a feature.
- *Personal loyalty as the override of institutional loyalty.* He will obey Xavier where he will not obey "the X-Men" as an institution; he will follow Rogers where he will not follow "the Avengers"; the loyalty is to the person, and when the person is replaced or compromised it does not transfer.

He is therefore a uniquely capable, uniquely unreliable asset by conventional intelligence standards, and a uniquely valuable one by the standard of the rare missions that require an operator who *cannot be turned by his organization* because his organization-loyalty is shallow and his person-loyalty is bedrock.

---

## 8. KILL/CAPTURE DOCTRINE — HIS OWN

He maintains, without articulating it as policy, a doctrine on the use of lethal force that has been remarkably stable across writers:

1. *Children: never.* Including the children of enemies. Including hostile enhanced children, where containment is sought first.
2. *Civilians: never deliberately, and the unintentional kill is a wound he carries forever.* The graves-visits roster includes a number of these.
3. *Surrendered combatants: not under his hand.* He will turn them over even at tactical cost.
4. *Enemies who have crossed specific lines* (slavers, certain categories of intelligence operators, those who experiment on the young): pre-authorized, by his own standing order to himself.
5. *Sabretooth: a special category.* The annual ritual. Operationally he has had Creed dead-to-rights repeatedly and not finished it; the inability is psychological (see §3, §5 of the workup) and constitutes his single most exploitable doctrinal gap.
6. *Himself: held in reserve as an option.* The Muramasa blade is the operational artifact of this clause. He has not used it on himself; he has positioned it where he could.

---

## 9. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL FAILURE MODES

A complete operational profile must catalog the ways the subject reliably fails, because adversaries do.

- *Sensory deception.* Olfactory illusion (Mystique-grade impersonation, Mysterio-grade environmental falsification) defeats his Tier 1 decision system and he is then operating on degraded inputs without knowing it. This is the *Old Man Logan* mechanism and it would work again.
- *Surgical/restraint scenarios.* Any scenario evoking the Weapon X surgical table — restraint, anesthesia, medical personnel — triggers a dissociative collapse disproportionate to the actual threat. Captors who recognize this can extract behavior from him by staging the configuration.
- *Protected-person hostage scenarios.* Reliable override of every other tactical consideration. Documented exploitation by the Hand, Mystique, Mojo, others.
- *Implanted-memory destabilization.* As above; faster and more total than physical injury.
- *Forced inactivity.* Confinement without combat — house arrest, prolonged hospitalization, an institutional sinecure — degrades him faster than any wound. He will manufacture conflict to escape it, which can be predicted and exploited.
- *The "samurai" ledger.* Adversaries who invoke Bushidō, Mariko, the Yashida name, or the broader honor frame can rec


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Section 6 of the dossier. The substrate of everything Section 5 named as "drives" — what the subject actually believes about the universe he is moving through, derived from a hundred and thirty years of behavioral evidence. Beliefs here are inferred from action, not from his own self-report, because the file has long since established that the subject is an unreliable narrator of himself.*

---

## 6.1 The Cosmology — How the World Is Built

The subject operates as a **functional materialist** with a layer of acquired Zen-Shinto vocabulary over the top. He has met gods (Amatsu-Mikaboshi, the Hindu pantheon during the *Magik* and Daimon Hellstrom crossovers), been to heaven and hell (the post-*Death of Wolverine* Hell arcs, the Mariko-in-the-Buddhist-afterlife sequences), and treats none of it as cosmologically decisive. His operative metaphysics is: *the universe is indifferent matter that occasionally organizes itself into predators, prey, and weather.* Supernatural beings are reclassified on contact into one of those three categories and engaged accordingly.

The Bushidō and Zen overlay — acquired in Jasmine Falls, sustained for a century — is not, on the behavioral evidence, a belief system. It is **a discipline he uses to govern a self he does not trust**. He kneels at Mariko's shrine, he sits zazen when he can, he keeps a daishō; he also drinks through the rituals when they fail to hold. The forms matter to him precisely because their content is optional — they are scaffolding, not faith.

He does, however, hold one quasi-metaphysical conviction with the weight of doctrine: **memory is not identity, and may be a lie**. A century of Weapon X, Team X, Romulus, Apocalypse, the Hand, the Professor, and Persephone has hardened into an epistemology: *what you remember is evidence, not truth; what you do is truth.* This is the closest thing in him to a first principle.

---

## 6.2 The Taxonomy of Persons

The subject sorts every human he meets, within seconds and largely by scent, into a small fixed taxonomy. The categories are stable across decades of writers:

- **Predators.** Those who hunt for pleasure or for hire and who will not stop. Sabretooth is the type-specimen. Predators are not to be reasoned with, not to be reformed, and — this is doctrinal for him — *not to be left alive when the situation permits otherwise*. His repeated arguments with Xavier and Cyclops about lethal force come down to this taxonomic disagreement: Xavier believes predators are patients; the subject believes predators are weather.
- **Handlers.** Anyone who wants to point him at a target. The default classification for institutions, governments, intelligence services, corporate actors, and most authority figures on first contact. Handlers are to be obeyed only conditionally and watched continuously. Xavier was a handler who earned reclassification; Nick Fury occupies a permanent handler-with-courtesies slot; Department H, the CIA, Hydra, the Hand, Romulus, and the Weapon Plus program are all the same category at root, distinguished only by the prettiness of their letterhead.
- **Innocents / the protected.** Children, adolescents, civilians under threat, women in the orbit of his enemies, anyone he reads as not having chosen this. The category triggers his most reliable and most exploitable behavior. He will degrade his tactical position to keep someone in this category alive. He knows it, the file knows it, and his enemies have known it since the 1970s.
- **Peers.** A small, named, mostly fixed set: Rogers, Ororo, Kurt, Jean (complicated), Scott (more complicated), Carol, Natasha, Ben Grimm, occasionally Charles, occasionally Strange. Peers are owed candor, backup without question, and the truth about his condition that he denies to everyone else.
- **The young in his keeping.** A subcategory of innocents promoted to apprenticeship. Kitty, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, Pixie, X-23, Quentin Quire by exception. The only category in which his attachment system works without distortion. They are owed teaching, and the teaching content is always the same: *survive me, survive the people like me, do not become me.*
- **Ghosts.** Rose, Itsu, Silver Fox, Mariko, Jean (intermittently). The dead he loved. They are not metaphors to him; on the behavioral evidence he addresses them, drinks with them, asks their counsel. The category is operational — decisions are tested against what the ghosts would think.

Note what is *not* in the taxonomy: a category for "ordinary strangers" with rich interiority. Strangers are pre-sorted into one of the above by smell and posture within seconds. This is not contempt; it is bandwidth management forced by the sensorium. He does not have the option of meeting people neutrally.

---

## 6.3 Conflict — What It Is and What It Is For

Conflict, to him, is **the natural state of affairs and the medium in which he is most legible to himself**. He does not believe in the possibility of permanent peace, not because he is nihilistic but because he has lived through eleven decades of evidence to the contrary, including two world wars he fought in personally. Peace, in his operational code, is *the interval in which one prepares the young for the next war.*

He distinguishes carefully — and this distinction is doctrinal — between **fighting**, **killing**, and **butchery**.

- *Fighting* is a conversation, sometimes friendly (Colossus in the Danger Room, sparring with Kurt), sometimes lethal, sometimes courtship-adjacent (Ororo, in early Claremont). It has rules even when unspoken.
- *Killing* is a tool. It is owed to predators, to enemies who will return if left, and — under the samurai overlay — to the mercy-stroke for the suffering (Mariko). It is not to be done lightly, never for an institution, and never publicly in front of the young if he can help it.
- *Butchery* is what Weapon X made him do, what the Hand made him do under *Enemy of the State*, what Mysterio tricked him into in the *Old Man Logan* timeline, and what he will not do under his own steam. Butchery is the line. When he has crossed it, even involuntarily, his response is decades of withdrawal.

The berserker state sits uncomfortably across all three categories and is the thing he most fears about himself — because in it the distinctions collapse.

---

## 6.4 Control — Who Gets to Run Him

The deepest political belief in the file is **anti-handler**. A century of being driven — by the Howlett household's expectations, by Hudson, by the CIA, by Romulus, by the Professor of Weapon X, by the Hand, by Hydra, by Apocalypse — has produced a near-allergic response to instrumentalization. He will *volunteer* to be used (this is the X-Men, this is the Avengers, this is every team) and will tolerate enormous amounts of it; what he will not tolerate is *being aimed without consent*. The line between the two is thin and entirely his to draw.

His relationship with authority, accordingly, is a layered code:

- **Default posture:** insubordinate, sarcastic, present anyway. He shows up to the briefing, sits at the back, makes the remark, then does the job — usually well, occasionally his own way.
- **Earned trust** unlocks compliance. Xavier earned it over years and lost it episodically (the Danger arc, the Onslaught arc, the Schism). Cyclops earned it and then lost it on Utopia and partly regained it. Steve Rogers has had it since the 1940s. Fury has a working version with caveats.
- **Institutions never get it.** Even Krakoa, where he serves on the Quiet Council, is held at arm's length — he treats the resurrection protocols as an *operational fact* to be exploited, not a metaphysical promise to be believed.
- **The veto.** He reserves an absolute personal veto on lethal orders that violate his code. He has walked off teams over this. He will walk off again.

The deeper structure: **he believes that any sufficiently large organization will eventually try to make a weapon of whatever's useful to it**, and that mutants, and he in particular, are the most useful thing in the room. His political conservatism on this point is total and is the one place his worldview has not updated in a century.

---

## 6.5 Trust — Its Architecture and Its Costs

Trust, in him, is **granular, person-specific, and irreversible in both directions**. Once given, it survives almost any provocation (Jean's Phoenix episodes, Charles's deceptions, Scott's authoritarianism, Carol's intermittent hostility); once withdrawn, it is not re-extended (Romulus, the Professor of Weapon X, anyone who has handled him knowingly).

The trust-granting protocol, reverse-engineered from behavior, has roughly four tests:

1. **The scent test.** He smells lies, fear, arousal, and intent. If a person's scent does not match their words, the gate does not open. This is not metaphor — it is anatomy doing the work of social cognition.
2. **The under-fire test.** Trust is provisional until he has fought alongside the person. He treats combat as the only honest interview. Storm passed this in the Morlock tunnels; Rogers passed it in 1944; Kitty passed it during the Brood arc; Jubilee passed it in the Reavers sequence; X-23 passed it the first time she hesitated to kill.
3. **The young-in-the-room test.** How a person behaves toward children when they think it does not count. He watches this constantly. Failures here are permanent disqualifications.
4. **The handler test.** Whether the person tries, even subtly, to point him. Charles failed this multiple times and was forgiven; most others, once detected, are not.

Self-trust is the harder problem. He does not trust **his own memory**, **his own berserker decisions**, or **his own intuitions when he has been recently around telepaths**. He compensates with external checks: he tells Kitty things to hold for him; he leaves himself notes; he uses the Yashida shrine and the cabin in the Rockies as fixed reference points; he relies on a small number of peers to tell him when he has changed and not noticed.

He trusts his **body** (it heals), his **senses** (they do not lie even when he does), and his **violence** (it works). He does not trust his **judgment** about himself, which is why he outsources so much of it.

---

## 6.6 Risk — The Calculus of an Unkillable Man

The subject's risk calculus is **structurally distorted by the healing factor** and he knows it. He will take wounds no sane operator would take to buy a tactical second; he will walk into fire, jump from aircraft, accept obvious traps. In any non-mutant this profile would be parasuicidal; in him it is a rationally-priced use of a unique resource. He has thought about this and accepted it.

But the distortions go deeper. Because nothing kills him, he has lost the normal human apprenticeship in *finitude as a planning constraint*. His time horizons are odd: he plans across decades for some things (the Yashida shrine, mentorship arcs, the slow campaign against Romulus) and across seconds for others, with little in between. He is poor at the middle distance — the six-month plan, the career, the marriage — which is part of why intimacy fails him.

The risks he **will not** take are diagnostic:

- He will not risk **the young in his keeping**, even at catastrophic cost to a mission. The Hand has exploited this. Mystique has. Mojo has.
- He will not risk **becoming the weapon again** if he can see it coming. The *Old Man Logan* vow is the extreme version: when the risk of involuntary butchery becomes unbearable, he zeroes the variable by refusing to fight at all.
- He will not risk **a peer's life on his judgment when he is compromised**. He pulls himself off operations after telepathic contact, after head injuries that may have shaken something loose, after recent berserker episodes. This is one of the few places he is consistently disciplined.
- He will not risk **the ghosts**. He will not betray Mariko's memory by behaving in ways that would shame her. This is a planning constraint that has stopped him from taking jobs, from accepting alliances, and from sleeping with at least three of the women who have made the offer.

The risks he *over*-takes — physical, geographic, romantic-in-the-short-term, financial (he is indifferent to money) — are all in categories where the only person paying the cost is him. The asymmetry is principled.

---

## 6.7 Violence — Its Ethics

The subject has a developed ethics of violence that is more rigorous than most of his colleagues credit. The components:

- **Proportionality is real but the floor is high.** He does not believe in graduated force in the way Rogers does; once committed, he commits with the assumption that the opponent will reciprocate at maximum. This is a survival heuristic earned in the trenches, not a moral position.
- **Witnesses matter.** He prefers not to be seen by the young at his worst. The Kitty Pryde arcs are explicit about this — he sends her away before things become what they become. The teaching is *that this exists*, not *that this is the work*.
- **Mercy is owed to the suffering.** Mariko's poisoning, the Hellfire children in some readings, the wounded enemies he has finished quickly rather than left in pain. The mercy-stroke is not a violation of his code; it is part of it.
- **No torture.** He has been tortured at industrial scale and will not perform it. He will hurt people for information, fast and bluntly, but the protracted, instrumentalized infliction-for-its-own-sake of his Weapon X experience is a line. Sabretooth crosses it routinely; the subject's revulsion at this is, in the file, one of the cleanest tells of where they actually differ.
- **No collateral if avoidable.** He prefers blades to firearms partly for this reason — they require him to be close enough to see what he is hitting.
- **The berserker is not exculpatory.** Even though the dissociative state genuinely fragments agency, he does not use it as excuse. He owns the bodies. This is, on the evidence, the most morally serious thing about him.

---

## 6.8 His Own Place in the Order

The subject's self-positioning is the **interpositional**: he stands between predators and the protected, and that is his vocation. He came to this position late — he was a predator for most of a century before he chose to stand between — and he holds it with the convert's intensity. He does not believe he has earned redemption; he believes redemption is not a category that applies to a creature like him. What applies is *work*. The work is to be of use to the young and to the peers, to kill the things that need killing, and to die — finally, when it sticks — having reduced the net amount of weaponized agency in the world by at least the amount he himself represented.

He does not believe he is a hero. He believes the people around him are, sometimes, and that his job is to make their being heroes survivable. The X-Men, the Avengers, the team-of-the-decade are scaffolding for them, not for him. He is the **expendable variable in any equation involving them** — and the expendability is the point, not a tragedy.

He believes he is, in the long count, **on the wrong side of the ledger** — that more harm has flowed through his hands than good, that the Weapon X kills and the Hand kills and the berserker kills and the wars all add up to a number that the mentorships and the rescues and the X-Men years cannot quite offset. He does not say this. He acts it. The drinking is partly this. The recklessness is partly this. The refusal of long-term happiness with the women who have offered it is largely this.
