And underneath that, undeclared and load-bearing: **he wants to be the last of his kind.** He wants the Weapon X program ended, Romulus ended, the Hand ended, Sabretooth ended, the production of more creatures like him stopped. He has fought, on the evidence, for this more consistently than for any other single objective across the canon. The protection of X-23 from her own conditioning is the same project at the personal scale. The mentorship of every adolescent he has taken on is the same project at the cultural scale: *teach them to live without needing to become me*.

---

## 6.9 The Operational Code in Compressed Form

Reduced to the rules he appears to actually follow, derived from a century of decisions:

1. *Trust the senses before the words.*
2. *Trust the body before the senses, when the senses have been recently in a room with a telepath.*
3. *Do not be aimed.*
4. *Earn the right to be in the room with the young.*
5. *Finish predators when the situation permits.*
6. *Do not torture. Do not butcher. Do not leave the wounded to suffer.*
7. *Memory is evidence, not identity. Cross-examine it.*
8. *The ghosts get a vote.*
9. *Drink after, not during, and not in front of the young.*
10. *When the container fails, go to the wilderness until it holds again.*
11. *Show up anyway.*
12. *Die useful.*

That is the code. It is unwritten, it is inconsistent at the edges, it has been violated by him under duress and overwrite, and it has nonetheless governed the recurring shape of his behavior across every writer, every era, and every reset of the canon for half a century of publication. The container holds. He built it himself, out of borrowed Bushidō and stolen time and the refusal to let what was done to him be the last word on what he is. That refusal is the worldview. Everything else is implementation.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Enacted code, not professed code. The professed code is sparse — a few aphorisms about doing what needs doing, about not being a good man, about Bushidō. The enacted code is much larger, much more specific, and in places sharply at odds with the professed one. What follows is reconstructed from a century-plus of decisional behavior under stress, which is the only place a moral code reveals itself.*

---

## 1. The Operative Maxims (Derived from Decisions, Not Speeches)

The subject does not operate from a published rulebook. He operates from a layered set of priors that can be reverse-engineered from a hundred years of choice-under-duress. In approximate order of binding force:

**(M1) Children are not legitimate targets, ever, under any rationalization.** This is the only absolute. Every other rule fractures somewhere in the canon; this one does not. Across the Weapon X record (in which he was directed at human targets including non-combatants), the Hand/Hydra brainwashing in *Enemy of the State*, the Apocalypse "Death" conversion, and the Mysterio-induced X-Men slaughter — in each case where he was *forced* across this line, the resulting moral injury was structurally incapacitating (the fifty-year claws-down silence of the *Old Man Logan* arc is the clearest evidence: he can survive being made a murderer of friends; he cannot survive being made a murderer of his own students-as-family, which functioned categorically as the children-line for him). When acting under his own will, the rule has held without recorded exception.

**(M2) The protected — once claimed — are claimed for life, and their safety outranks his own survival, his team's tactical position, and the mission.** Operative against Kitty Pryde (the entire Ogun arc in *Kitty Pryde and Wolverine*, in which he abandons every other consideration to extract her), Jubilee (the *Wolverine* vol. 2 run from #1 onward), Rogue, Jean repeatedly, Mariko, X-23, Armor, Idie, the resurrected children of Krakoa. The protection list is *paternalist and asymmetric* — they do not get to release him from it by saying they don't want it. He decides who is on the list; once on, they cannot be removed except by death.

**(M3) Killing is permitted; killing is sometimes required; killing is never clean.** He does not subscribe to the Xavier/Rogers no-kill doctrine and never has, but he also does not subscribe to the Punisher/Creed kill-as-solution doctrine. The enacted rule is: *if this person will, with high probability, kill someone on the protected list or someone on the equivalent generalized list of innocents, and no other intervention will reliably prevent it, then killing is the correct act, and you carry the weight afterward.* The weight-carrying is non-negotiable; the use of alcohol and exile post-kill is *the carrying*, not an evasion of it. He has stated this directly in many writers' hands — "I'm the best there is at what I do, and what I do isn't very nice" is not a boast, it is a confession with a moral premise embedded: the act is *not nice*, and pretending otherwise is the actual sin.

**(M4) The agentic violation of another's mind is the worst category of harm.** Higher than killing. Derived from a century of receiving it. He has a near-allergic reaction to telepaths who scan without consent (the long arc with Jean, where he tolerates her access *because she asked*; his hostility to Emma Frost for years, only partially earned); to Xavier's late-revealed mental tampering (the response in *Schism* and after is disproportionate by tactical standards and exactly proportionate by *his* moral standards); to anyone who conditions, brainwashes, or implants. The Hand and the Weapon X personnel are killed without hesitation and without the post-kill weight, because in his enacted code they have forfeited the protections owed to ordinary killers.

**(M5) Loyalty is owed to persons and to codes, never to organizations.** He has worked for the Canadian government, the CIA-analog Team X, Department H, the X-Men, X-Force, the Avengers, the Jean Grey School, the Quiet Council. He has betrayed every one of them when it asked him to violate (M1)–(M4) or to abandon a person on the protected list. Conversely, he has remained loyal to *individuals* across decades of their own institutional shifts (Xavier, until Xavier crossed (M4); Rogers, across every Cap status change; Kurt Wagner, unconditionally).

**(M6) Tell the truth, especially the ugly truth, especially to the young.** Pedagogically central. He does not soften threat-assessments for Kitty, Jubilee, or X-23; he tells them what is going to try to kill them and how. He lies operationally (Patch in Madripoor; covert ops; cover identities) but does not lie *interpersonally* within his protected circle. The lying-by-omission about his own past is the conspicuous exception, and he treats it as a personal failure rather than a license.

**(M7) Suffering taken on oneself in place of another is the highest available moral act.** Demonstrated in his consistent interposition between threats and the vulnerable, his acceptance of injuries the healing factor will close so that someone else's body — which will not close — is spared, and his repeated willingness to die (and, eventually, his death in adamantium) as a price for protection. This is the Bushidō overlay made operational, and it is the one place his professed code and his enacted code coincide cleanly.

---

## 2. What He Will Do

- **Kill an active threat to a protected person**, without hesitation, without warning, often without offering surrender. The threshold is *capability plus demonstrated intent*, not the local legal standard.
- **Execute a recovered war criminal of the Hand/Weapon X/Hydra category** even when they are not currently a threat. This is the *standing-order* category; he treats those organizations' senior personnel as combatants for life. This is a *real* fracture in (M3) — he applies a different rule to them — and he has not reconciled it.
- **Lie, infiltrate, assume false identity** in service of (M2) or against (M4) violators. The Patch persona in Madripoor (*Wolverine* vol. 2 #1+) is a sustained operational deception he conducts without moral discomfort.
- **Disobey lawful orders from his own command** — Xavier, Cyclops, Cap, the Quiet Council — when they collide with (M1) or (M2). The Schism break with Cyclops over the conscription of children into X-Force is the apex example; it is also the cleanest demonstration that (M1)/(M2) outrank (M5).
- **Mentor, teach, train**, even when temperamentally unsuited and even when it embarrasses him. The Jean Grey School headmaster role (*Wolverine and the X-Men*, Aaron) is morally chosen against personal preference.
- **Drink heavily, brawl recreationally, sleep with women he will not stay with.** He does not classify these as moral matters; the dossier treats them as affect-regulation, but in his own code they fall outside the moral frame entirely. (This itself is a moral position — he has decided that what he does to *himself* is not subject to the code.)
- **Accept death.** Repeatedly, deliberately. In adamantium, in the Hellfire arenas, in the Muramasa-blade scenarios. The willingness is a settled feature, not a crisis.

## 3. What He Will Not Do

- **Harm a child** under his own volition. Not for tactical advantage, not for the mission, not under orders, not under torture (the brainwashing scenarios are the *only* cases, and they are why he treats brainwashers as forfeit).
- **Stand by while a child is harmed in his sensory range.** This is operationally the same rule from the other direction; failure-to-act is treated as harm.
- **Use his claws on someone who is unarmed, surrendered, and uncategorized.** He will threaten, he will subdue, he will break bones; he will not execute. The claw is reserved for the categorized.
- **Hand a person over to a known torturer or experimenter, even an enemy.** He has on multiple occasions extracted prisoners from worse captors at cost to his own mission.
- **Lie to a protected person about a matter material to their safety.** Operational lies, yes; safety lies, no.
- **Sell his services for money in a way that crosses (M1)–(M4).** He has taken paid work, he has been a mercenary; he has not been a contract killer of the innocent, and the historical record of his Madripoor and Team X periods, when sifted, supports this distinction.
- **Take a permanent student or apprentice from among the unwilling.** Daken is the wound here — a child raised by enemies to become a weapon, exactly what was done to him — and his refusal to *reproduce that procedure* even on enemies' children is one of the firmest negative rules in the file.
- **Use telepathy, mind control, or memory alteration on another person, ever, by proxy or by request.** He will not ask Jean, Xavier, or Emma to scrub a target's mind even when it would be tactically optimal. This is (M4) applied to himself.

## 4. The Justifications (Internal, Sparse, Largely Bushidō-Coded)

He does not justify much aloud. When he does, the justifications cluster in three registers:

**The Bushidō register.** Duty (*giri*), the protection of those who cannot protect themselves, the acceptance of death as a precondition of right action, the disciplining of the self through formal practice. He learned this from Bando Saburo and the Yashida household pre-WWII and has run it as his explicit moral software ever since. It is not decorative. The kata, the formal Japanese etiquette he uses with Yashida-clan members, the ritualized acceptance of Mariko's request that he end her life — these are Bushidō *enacted*. The register's limitation is that Bushidō was designed for a man with a single lord and a single battlefield; Logan has had a dozen of each, and the code stretches and tears at the seams.

**The "what was done to me will not be done by me" register.** This is the trauma-survivor moral logic, and it is the strongest single generator of his negative rules. He was experimented on, so he does not experiment. He was conscripted, so he does not conscript. His memory was overwritten, so he does not overwrite. His childhood was violated, so children are inviolable. This register is more reliable than the Bushidō register because it is grief-powered rather than ideology-powered, and grief in him does not fade.

**The "somebody has to" register.** The most pragmatic and the most morally exposed. Used to justify the kills the X-Men cannot or will not make, the executions of recovered war criminals, the X-Force black-ops period. The argument is that the existence of categorical no-kill agents (Xavier, Cap, Cyclops in his early form) is a luxury *funded* by the existence of agents like him who will absorb the moral cost. He believes this. It is also the register where his code is most vulnerable to manipulation, because anyone who can frame a target as a "somebody has to" case can recruit him.

## 5. Consistencies — The Spine

Across writers from Wein and Claremont through Hama, Windsor-Smith, Morrison, Millar, Aaron, Hickman, and the present, four things have *never* moved:

1. **The child-rule.** Not negotiated, not bent, not contextually relaxed. The single most consistent ethical fact in the file.
2. **Mentorship of adolescent girls as reparative practice.** Kitty, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, Idie, X-23 — across forty years of publication and a dozen lead writers, the behavior is identical in structure: protect, train to survive him and his world, do not infantilize, tell the ugly truth, release when ready, remain available.
3. **The handler-allergy.** Anyone who tries to *run* him, in the operational sense, is rejected. Xavier got the longest grace because he asked rather than ordered; when it emerged that he had also been editing memories, the grace collapsed.
4. **Acceptance of post-kill weight.** He does not absolve himself. He does not seek absolution. He carries the count. The drinking and the geographic flight are how he carries it. The professed claim of *not being a good man* is a description of the ledger, not of the man.

## 6. Fractures — Where the Code Breaks

A serious file must note the fractures with the same specificity as the consistencies. There are several.

**Fracture A: The standing-execution list.** The Hand, Weapon X surviving personnel, Hydra senior ranks, Romulus's network. He treats membership-plus-rank in these organizations as forfeiture of the protections (M3) otherwise affords. This is in tension with (M3)'s requirement of *current* threat and *no alternative*. The honest read: this is revenge upgraded to policy, and he knows it. He has not stopped doing it.

**Fracture B: Sabretooth.** The century-long mutual murder ritual with Creed is not Bushidō, not protection, not "somebody has to" — it is a personal vendetta sustained as an organizing structure of his identity. He has had operationally clean opportunities to end it and not taken them, and Creed has had opportunities to leave it and not taken them. The relationship is exempted from the code by mutual unspoken arrangement, and the exemption is itself a moral failure he has never addressed.

**Fracture C: The X-Force period (Kyle/Yost, *Uncanny X-Force* by Remender).** Wet-work team operating outside the X-Men's sanctioned ethics, killing pre-emptively against the Apocalypse threat, including the unresolved Genesis/child-Apocalypse decision. He led it. The justification was "somebody has to" and the keep-it-from-the-kids premise — that the existence of a black team allowed the school to remain clean. The Schism with Cyclops was partly about Cyclops trying to *generalize* this practice onto adolescents. The fracture: Logan ran X-Force because he believed it was the lesser evil, *and* he knew it was incompatible with his professed code, *and* he did not stop. The X-Force decisions are the file's clearest case of his pragmatic register overriding his ethical one.

**Fracture D: Daken.** A child raised by enemies into a weapon — the precise category Logan exists to prevent. The handling has been variously: attempted reconciliation, attempted intervention, eventual lethal confrontation, eventual co-presence under Krakoan resurrection. He has neither saved this son nor cleanly given up on him. The fracture is that his rules for *other* people's lost children (rescue, mentor, accept) do not work on his own, and he has not built a substitute.

**Fracture E: Self-destruction.** The drinking, the recklessness toward his own body, the low-grade lifelong wish for an ending that sticks. He has placed himself outside the protection rule. A consistent ethic would require that the rule apply to him too. It does not, and the inconsistency is load-bearing for his daily functioning.

**Fracture F: Operational lying.** He tells the truth inside the circle and lies fluently outside it. This is defensible by every reasonable real-world ethic; it is in tension with his own absolutism about agentic violation under (M4), since sustained deception is a milder form of the same category. He has not addressed this and is unlikely to.

## 7. Drift Over Time

The code has shifted, in identifiable phases.

**Pre-Howlett-massacre child (1880s).** A sheltered, sickly boy with conventional period-and-class morals, almost entirely inherited and untested. Not a moral agent in any developed sense — there is not yet a code, only obedience and affection.

**Feral period (1890s–1900s).** Code reduced to survival ethics. Pack-loyalty to wolves, avoidance of humans, no abstract rules. The child-rule is *not yet present* — he is the child. This is the only period in which his moral system is essentially silent.

**Pre-WWI through Yashida period (1900s–late 1930s).** Acquisition of the Bushidō overlay under Bando Saburo. This is the first time he has a *system*. The protection-of-the-weak rule consolidates here. The acceptance-of-death rule is installed here. The Itsu relationship and her murder (and Daken's loss) traumatize the system and harden the negative rules — particularly the no-experimentation-on-children rule, which is encoded *before* Weapon X, by Itsu's murder, and *after* Weapon X is overdetermined.

**Wars and Team X (1940s–1960s).** Functional moral compromise. Soldier ethics layered over Bushidō. He kills for governments, accepts a chain of command, and — though he does not know it at the time — has his memories edited continuously. Operationally pragmatic; morally outsourced. This period leaves him with the lifelong handler-allergy once he discovers what was done to him.

**Weapon X and immediate aftermath (1960s–early 1970s).** The code is shattered along with the man. There is essentially no agentic moral life during the program; the post-escape period is moral reconstruction from fragments, mostly through the Hudsons.

**Department H and early X-Men (mid-1970s–early 1980s).** Reassembly. The code as we now recognize it crystallizes. Xavier's school provides the *protected list* template. Kitty Pryde is the first fully realized application of the mentorship rule. The Mariko arc is the first attempt to live the Bushidō ideal openly in adult life.

**Mature X-Men and solo-title period (mid-1980s–late 1990s).** Stable code, well-tested. The Patch period demonstrates that operational deception can be quarantined from interpersonal honesty. The Mariko killing-by-request is the code's hardest passed test — he does what she asks at the price of everything he has tried to be.

**Origins recovery and *Wolverine: Origins* arc (2000s).** Returning memory destabilizes the code by revealing how many of his prior moral acts were performed under false premises. He does not abandon the code; he revises its *epistemic basis*, treating his own memory as evidence to be cross-examined. This is when (M4), the agentic-violation rule, becomes maximalist.

**X-Force and Schism (late 2000s–early 2010s).** The code's most serious internal collision. He runs the black team *and* breaks from Cyclops over conscripting children. The two positions are not contradictory by his own logic — adults can choose the dirty work; children cannot be chosen for it — but they expose the pragmatic register's costs.

**Headmaster period (*Wolverine and the X-Men*).** The mentorship rule becomes institutional. He builds the structure he wishes had existed for him. The code is at its most generative here.

**Death and Old Man period.** The *Old Man Logan* presentation is the code under maximum moral injury: when (M1) is violated under compulsion, the entire agentic apparatus shuts down. The fifty-year nonviolence vow is not a new ethic; it is the old ethic refusing to operate because its core has been desecrated. The post-resurrection Old Man Logan figure in the main continuity carries this scar forward as a permanent feature.

**Krakoan era.** The resurrection protocols make death routine, which paradoxically *raises* the moral stakes of killing (because the killed will return changed, or will not, depending on the Council's decision) and *lowers* the stakes of dying (his own death is now revocable). His Quiet Council role and his X-Force role under Krakoa repeat the prior pattern: institutional dirty-work executor, while continuing to mentor the young. The code has not changed; its operating environment has, and he has adjusted application without revising principle.

## 8. The Integrated Read

The moral framework is best described as a *trauma-grown samurai pragmatism*, organized around an absolute child-protection rule, a maximalist anti-violation rule, and a willingness to bear the moral cost of killing rather than externalize it. Its strongest features are its consistency about children, its honesty about its own ugliness, and its refusal of absolution. Its weakest features are the standing-execution list, the Sabretooth exemption, the X-Force pragmatism, and the self-exemption from the protection rule. It is not a coherent philosophical system and was never built to be one. It is a working scaffold a chronically dissociative trauma survivor erected so that the weapon he was made into would have somewhere to stand that was not on top of someone vulnerable. The scaffold holds in almost every direction it was built to hold. Where it doesn't hold, he knows, and the knowing is itself part of the code.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Section 6 of UATU Dossier. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) and §4 (Psychiatric) for the dissociative/attachment substrate underwriting the linguistic surface described here.*

---

## 6.1 Baseline Register — The Default Voice

The subject's resting speech register is a low, gravelled, mid-volume North American English with vestigial Albertan-Anglo-Canadian vowels surviving in specific words ("about," "sorry," "out") that surface chiefly when fatigued, drunk, or speaking to a Canadian interlocutor (Hudson, Heather, Mac, Puck). Across writers — Wein, Claremont, Hama, Windsor-Smith, Aaron, Brisson, Percy — the orthographic conventions are consistent: dropped terminal *-g* on present participles ("workin'," "thinkin'," "killin'"), elided auxiliaries ("'m gonna," "'s what I do"), and chronic contraction of *them* to *'em*. This is a *cultivated* working-class register — it is not where he started (the Howlett household speech of *Origin* #1–6 is mannered, late-Victorian, polite) but where he settled, sometime between the Yukon mining camps and the trenches of the Somme. The voice is, in Goffmanian terms, a presentation: the Howlett child chose a vernacular that erased the gentleman, and the vernacular outlasted the reasons for choosing it. He no longer code-switches *up* into educated register except under specific provocations (Mariko's family, Xavier in formal mode, the rare diplomatic scene) where he can do it cleanly, which is the tell that the baseline is an election.

Pitch is consistently low; volume modulates narrowly between conversational and a controlled drop-to-quieter when threatening. He almost never shouts. The shouted line in canon is reserved for two situations: the berserker episode (often rendered as wordless "RRRAAAGGHH" or single syllables in the art) and the loss-of-a-protected-person moment ("JEEEAAANNN!" — *X-Men* #137 register, repeated structurally for Mariko, for Kitty in mortal jeopardy, for X-23). The shout is therefore *diagnostic*: when he raises his voice in articulate speech, dissociation or catastrophic grief is loading.

## 6.2 Lexical Field — The Working Vocabulary

His functional lexicon is narrow by election and deep by experience. Recurrent content words:

- **"Bub."** The signature address term. Used to strangers, adversaries, and acquaintances he is establishing dominance or distance with. Never to children under his protection, never to Jean Grey, never to Kurt Wagner, almost never to Ororo. *Diagnostic value:* "bub" marks the interlocutor as outside the inner ring. Its withdrawal is an upgrade in intimacy.
- **"Darlin'."** To women he respects without sexual designs (Ororo frequently; Rogue; Jubilee in adult years). Distinguishable from the sexualized "sweetheart" (transient lovers, bar encounters) and from the unmarked first-name address he uses with Jean and Mariko, which is the highest tier.
- **"Kid," "kiddo," "half-pint," "pup."** The protector-vocabulary. Kitty was "Kitty," "Pryde," "half-pint," and "darlin'" in rotation; Jubilee was "kid," "Jubilee," and "darlin'"; X-23 was "Laura" almost immediately, which is a tell that he registered her as a peer-in-trauma rather than a child-to-shelter. Diminutives mark surrogate-paternal load.
- **"Animal," "beast," "the thing inside."** Self-reference vocabulary for the dissociated state. This is the language of negative self-concept (§3) leaking into ordinary speech. He uses it about himself far more than anyone else does about him.
- **"Snikt."** Not his word — the onomatopoeic claw-extrusion sound supplied by the page — but his entire community treats it as a speech act. He has occasionally weaponized it as the *only* utterance in a scene, the claws extruding as the sentence. Communicatively this is paralinguistic: the body finishing the sentence the voice declined to start.
- **Profanity.** Robust but not florid. Era-appropriate ("damn," "hell," "bastard," "son of a bitch") with the Comics Code-era euphemisms ("flamin'," and the Hama-era "frab" / "drattit") receding as the publishing register loosened. Post-2001 MAX-era material (*Wolverine MAX*, the Aaron *PunisherMAX* crossover, *Old Man Logan* in its harder moments) demonstrates that the harder lexicon is present and suppressed in mainline books — i.e., his profanity ceiling is editorial, not characterological; the character can and does go further. He does not, however, use sexual profanity casually; sexual language is reserved and dry.
- **Bushidō / Japanese loan vocabulary.** *Honor, giri, on, sensei, ronin*. Used unironically. The Japanese-language fluency is canon (Claremont *Wolverine* limited series, 1982; Hama *Wolverine* vol. 2 passim) — he reads, writes, and converses; the *register* he uses in Japanese is markedly more formal and more emotionally available than his English register. The decisive datum: he can apologize in Japanese. He almost cannot in English.

## 6.3 Syntactic and Rhetorical Habits

Sentences are short. Mean clause length under stress collapses to three to five words ("Stay back." "Don't." "Move and you die."). At rest he is capable of longer constructions but rarely chooses them. The structural unit he favors is the *declarative followed by sardonic undercut*: "I'm the best there is at what I do. And what I do isn't very nice." (Claremont, *Uncanny X-Men* #162 vicinity, paraphrased across many issues.) The undercut is reliable enough to qualify as a tic. It functions defensively — every elevated or self-revealing statement is immediately deflated, denying the interlocutor any leverage from the disclosure.

Other syntactic tells:

- **The pre-action quiet line.** Before violence he typically delivers one short, low sentence — often a single imperative or a flat statement of intention ("Time's up, bub.") — and then acts. The verbal beat is a courtesy and a warning, and its omission is diagnostic: when he attacks *without* the line, he has already dissociated.
- **The question deflected by a question.** Standard interrogation-resistance pattern: "Where were you?" "Why d'you wanna know?" This is not stylistic; it is a *century* of debrief-resistance and handler-management automated into syntax.
- **The corrected tense.** When discussing past lovers or fallen friends he repeatedly self-corrects across tense ("Mariko is — *was* — ") in a way that, in clinical context, indexes unresolved grief plus the dissociative-amnesia complication that he is sometimes literally unsure whether the person is dead, alive, or implanted.
- **Refusal of the autobiographical first person.** He rarely says "I remember." He says "I think I remember," "they tell me," "I got pictures in my head of," "supposedly." This is the linguistic signature of the corrupted memory file from §3 — he treats his own autobiography as hearsay and his grammar reflects it.

## 6.4 Register-Switching Across Contexts

**With Xavier.** Reduced contraction count, fewer dropped *-g*'s, longer sentences. He clears his throat. He calls him "Charles" in private, "Professor" in the room, "Chuck" only when irritated or affectionate-mocking. The register elevation is a tell of respect; the "Chuck" is a tell of safety.

**With Cyclops.** Combative shorthand. "Slim," "One-Eye," "Summers," "Scott" — the address term tracks the affect of the moment with unusual precision. Late Krakoan-era and post-*Schism* material softens this; "Scott" becomes more frequent. The diction toward Scott carries a specific verbal habit: rhetorical questions designed to expose strategic limitations he believes Scott has ("That your plan?" "You sure about that, fearless leader?").

**With Jean.** Quietest register he has. Sentence length actually expands here. Profanity drops to near zero. The vocative is the bare name. He cannot manage humor with her past a certain emotional altitude; the sardonic-undercut tic fails, leaving the disclosure intact — which is precisely why intimacy with Jean is destabilizing for him (it disables a primary defense).

**With Ororo.** Peer register, courteous, mild teasing. He uses "'Ro" and "darlin'." Honesty is high; vulnerability is moderate; he can be wrong in front of her and admit it, which he cannot do with Scott.

**With Kurt Wagner.** The most relaxed register in the file. Jokes; physical-comedy verbal banter; theological needling that he doesn't bring to anyone else. He calls him "Elf." Kurt is the rare interlocutor with whom Logan initiates conversation.

**With Kitty Pryde.** Pedagogical register. Sentence structure becomes instructive ("First thing you do is — "). He uses her name, "Pryde," and "half-pint" interchangeably. He is one of the few interlocutors who will let her finish a sentence — most of his other dialogues feature mid-sentence interruption.

**With Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, X-23.** Mentor-register, variant per subject. With Jubilee: bantering, eye-rolling-tolerant. With Rogue: more guarded, more Southern-mirroring ("y'all" surfaces). With Armor (Hisako): Japanese honorifics, the only X-student he addresses with the surname-san construction. With X-23: short, frank, no euphemism, no diminutives — she gets the adult register because she earned it the same way he did, and he respects that.

**With Sabretooth.** A liturgy. Stripped, ritualized, paradoxically *intimate* in its predictability. "Creed." "Runt." Insults that have not been updated since the 1970s. He talks to Sabretooth more like an estranged sibling at a holiday table than like a target; the diction reveals the disorganized-attachment substrate flagged in §3.

**With Captain America.** Formal-respectful register, "Cap" or "Steve," declarative, minimal sarcasm. One of three people (with Xavier and Mariko's memory) who can give him an order he will follow without renegotiation.

**With handlers and authority figures he distrusts** (Stryker, Department H bureaucrats, Hand interrogators, government liaisons). Monosyllabic compliance-resistance. He goes verbally *flat*. Long pauses. Single-word answers. This is a specific learned posture from a century of debriefs and is functionally indistinguishable from dissociative shut-down — the question of whether the flatness is tactical or symptomatic is, in his case, ill-formed.

**With bartenders and strangers in bars.** Almost monastic economy. "Same again." "Beer." A nod. The bar is one of his regulating environments and the linguistic minimalism is part of the regulation.

## 6.5 How He Communicates Love

He does not, in declarative form, very often. The "I love you" is canonically rare and tends to surface only at deathbeds (Mariko, *Wolverine* vol. 2 #57) or in moments of extremity he expects not to survive. Affection is communicated instead through:

- **Provision of physical safety.** Standing between the loved person and a threat is his primary love-language. The verbal corollary is the imperative ("Stay behind me." "Don't move.") which in his idiolect is a love word.
- **Teaching.** Instruction in survival skills is, for him, the durable form of caring. The hours spent in the Danger Room with Kitty (*Kitty Pryde and Wolverine* mini, 1984) are a love letter rendered as pedagogy.
- **Naming.** Granting a private diminutive ("half-pint," "darlin'," "'Ro," "Elf") is a marker of bonded relation. *Removal* of "bub" is its own gesture. Use of the bare first name is reserved.
- **Presence without speech.** With Jean, with Kurt, with Mariko, with Kitty in later years, he demonstrates an unusual capacity to sit silently in the same room as the loved person — which, given his baseline hyperarousal, is physiologically expensive and therefore semantically loaded.
- **The cigar offered, the drink poured.** Sharing his self-soothing rituals is intimacy. He pours for very few people.
- **Touch, sparingly.** A hand on the shoulder; a forehead-to-forehead with Jubilee or X-23 in extremity. He does not hug easily; when he does, it is reportable.

## 6.6 How He Communicates Threat

A precisely engineered ladder, almost identical across writers:

1. **Stillness.** He stops moving. Conversational fidget — cigar, glass, slight weight-shift — ceases. This is pre-verbal threat and the most reliable early indicator.
2. **The low line.** Volume drops below conversational. One sentence, often imperative, often containing "bub" or the interlocutor's surname. ("Walk away, bub." "Sit down, Creed.")
3. **The sniff.** Audible, deliberate. Communicates *I have your scent; I have catalogued you*. Paralinguistic but unambiguous to anyone who has seen it before.
4. **The named consequence.** "You do that again and I'll gut you." Specific, anatomical, unhedged. He does not bluff and his interlocutors generally know it; the named consequence is therefore informational rather than rhetorical.
5. **The *snikt*.** Display claws, not engaged claws — one or two extruded, not the full three, held still. A warning.
6. **The pre-attack line.** "Last chance." Or silence — if the line is omitted he is already past the threshold (see §6.3).
7. **Engagement.** Verbal content ceases. From here the vocalization is paralinguistic — growl, snarl, the wordless berserker register. *Post-episode amnesia means he often cannot report what, if anything, he said during steps 6–7.* This is clinically important: his self-report on the contents of a fight is unreliable in a specific, predictable way.

## 6.7 How He Communicates Grief

Three modes, used in order:

- **Verbal denial collapsing into single-word utterance.** "No." "No." Repeated. Then silence. Mariko's death scene, Jean's deaths, the *Old Man Logan* discovery scene all run this pattern.
- **Geographic flight as utterance.** He leaves. The departure itself is the statement. Notes are rare; when he does leave a note it is short, declarative, factual ("Gone north. Don't follow."), and indicates that the grief is severe enough he has reached for written language he does not trust.
- **Ritualized commemoration with substances.** A drink poured for the dead, a cigar smoked alone in a specific place (Mariko's grave, the Xavier school grounds at night, the cabin in the Canadian Rockies). He does not narrate the grief; he performs it spatially. Anyone observing him in these acts is not addressed; the ritual is sealed.

He does *not* eulogize publicly with any skill. Asked to speak at a memorial he will be terse, often inadequate by social standards, and visibly grateful when someone else (Ororo, Kurt) takes over. This is not an absence of grief but a literalism about language: he does not believe words can carry the weight and refuses to pretend they can.

## 6.8 Deflection and Avoidance Language

The catalogued repertoire:

- **The sardonic undercut** (§6.3) — primary defense against self-disclosure.
- **The change of physical activity.** Lights a cigar, pours a drink, walks to the window. The action interrupts the conversational pressure and lets him answer (or not) on his own beat. Interlocutors who have learned to wait through it get more; those who push during it get nothing.
- **The strategic shrug.** Frequent. Functions as plausible-deniability of comprehension.
- **The dismissive "Forget it."** Hard close. Indicates the topic is now non-negotiable and further pressure will escalate the room.
- **Question reversal.** ("Why are you asking?")
- **The deflective third person.** When the topic is himself he sometimes drifts into "a guy" or "you" constructions ("A guy lives long enough, he sees..."). This is depersonalization (§4) leaking into pronoun selection and is reliably present in his most autobiographical moments.
- **Walking out.** The terminal deflection. He leaves the room mid-conversation and does not return for hours, days, or years. The departure itself is grammatical: it terminates the sentence the interlocutor was building.

## 6.9 Honesty Profile and the Olfactory Lie-Detector

He is unusually honest by interpersonal standards, with two structural reasons. First, he can smell physiological signatures of deception (heart rate, sweat composition) and operates in a world where he assumes others *cannot*, so lying is less useful to him than to most. Second, lying requires consistent autobiographical recall, which his condition denies him; the operational cost of maintained lies is prohibitive. He therefore prefers *omission* and *redirection* to fabrication. When he does lie, it is typically to protect a third party (the lie to Kitty about her parents, the lies to younger students about the body counts of operations they were on the edge of). His lies are detectable to those who know him by their *fluency* — he becomes briefly more articulate, longer-sentenced, the working-class register flickering — because the lie requires composition the truth does not.

## 6.10 Written Communication

Reluctant. Print handwriting, all caps, blocky — the handwriting of someone who learned penmanship in a 19th-century schoolroom and then deliberately unlearned its elegance. Signature: "Logan," single name, no flourish. He writes notes more than letters; letters more than reports; reports almost never if avoidable. Journaling is absent from canon, which is itself diagnostic — a man with corrupted autobiographical memory does not journal because he does not trust the file he would be writing into. Texting / digital communication, in modernized eras: terse to the point of opacity, lowercase, no punctuation, frequent single-word replies ("ok," "no," "on my way"). He does not use emoji. He does use, on occasion, the period at the end of a one-word reply — which in current pragmatics reads as cold and which, in his case, accurately reflects the temperature.

## 6.11 Paralinguistic and Somatic Communication

Often louder than his words.

- **The cigar as punctuation.** Lit at the start of a difficult conversation; drawn on in lieu of a response; stubbed out as a closer. The cigar is a syntactic instrument.
- **The drink-pause.** A swallow inserted where another speaker would put a sentence. Buys him beats and signals the topic is heavier than the room is acknowledging.
- **The sniff.** Documented above as threat; also used as social information-gathering. He has been known to identify illness, pregnancy, fear, arousal, and recent presence of specific persons in a room, and to communicate this knowledge by acting on it rather than naming it — which interlocutors who know him read as a kind of unspoken disclosure ("he knows").
- **The narrowed eye, head-tilt.** Pre-question posture. Indicates he is going to ask something he already knows part of the answer to.
- **The unsheathed claw used for non-combat tasks.** Cutting an apple, opening a letter, picking a splinter from another person's hand. Communicates ease, control, *I am not afraid of this thing I am*. It is rare and it is intimate; he does it in front of very few people. Kitty, Jubilee, Kurt, and X-23 have all seen it. Most others have not.
- **The growl.** Subvocal, chest-deep. Involuntary; precedes the berserker by a measurable interval. Those who recognize it can sometimes interrupt the escalation by *naming* it ("Logan."), which is the canonical de-escalation move used by Jean, Xavier, Ororo, and Kitty — the speaking of his name in his own voice's register reportedly works where commands do not.

## 6.12 Diagnostic Tells — Summary for the File

The following are the high-confidence linguistic indicators that the substrate states described in §4 are loading:

- **Pronoun drift into second/third person ("you," "a guy")** → depersonalization rising.
- **Tense self-correction on the dead** → unresolved grief plus memory-corruption uncertainty.
- **"I think I remember" / "they tell me" / "supposedly"** → active autobiographical doubt; do not press for narrative under these conditions.
- **Loss of the sardonic undercut** → defenses down; the disclosure is real and costly; respond with weight or with silence, not with humor.
- **Shouted articulate speech** → dissociation or catastrophic grief loading; intervention window narrow.
- **Subvocal growl** → berserker prodrome; name him in his own register.
- **Omission of the pre-action line** → threshold already breached; verbal de-escalation has missed its window.
- **Use of Japanese** → he is reaching for a more emotionally available register than English permits him; the content matters; listen.
- **Single-word period-terminated replies** → not coldness; conservation. He is managing internal load.
- **The cigar lit at the start of the conversation** → he is anticipating that this will be hard. Match the gravity.

---

*The integrated linguistic read: his speech is a working container, like the rest of him — designed under pressure, kept narrow by election, with the high registers (Japanese, the bare first name, the unguarded declarative) reserved for the few interlocutors and few moments where the container can be safely thinned. The vernacular is a costume worn so long it became skin. The silences are the most reliable utterances in the file.*


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Format: GIVEN [stimulus / situation] → EXPECT [behavior, with mechanism]. Predictions derived from the longitudinal record in §1–5; the stimulus situations are ones canon has not staged, but the response surface is constrained by a century-plus of consistent behavior.*

---

## A. Waking, Sleeping, and the Private Hours

**GIVEN a hotel room he is checking into for the first time →** EXPECT a fixed three-minute walk-through before he sets his bag down: he opens the closet, the bathroom door, looks behind the shower curtain, checks the space under the bed and behind the curtains, and tests the lock and the chain. He will identify two exits (door, window, even on an upper floor — the healing factor recasts a four-story drop as inconvenient, not lethal). He will then move the room's chair so it faces the door, not the television. The sweep is not paranoia in his subjective experience; it is the same automatic procedure as a soldier clearing a room, run so often it sits below deliberation.

**GIVEN that room is on a low floor near an ice machine or elevator bank →** EXPECT a request to change rooms, framed as preference, without explanation. The mechanism: the hyperacute hearing turns the corridor hum into a continuous low-grade vigilance load that prevents sleep.

**GIVEN he has the room to himself for the night →** EXPECT he sleeps in his clothes on top of the covers more often than under them; boots within arm's reach, not unlaced across the room. Sleep onset is rapid when he permits it (a soldier's trained skill) but is broken — he wakes fully and instantly several times a night to evaluate ambient sound, then drops back. He does not remember most of these wakings. A polysomnograph would show fragmented architecture and very little Stage 3; the healing factor's compensation is what permits him to function on it.

**GIVEN he dreams →** EXPECT recurrent intrusive material from the Weapon X tank, the Howlett manor on the night of the killing, and a small set of faces (Rose, Itsu, Mariko, Silver Fox). EXPECT he does not narrate dreams to anyone and minimizes their impact when directly asked. EXPECT occasional violent motor activity on waking — sitting up with claws partly extruded — followed by a hand-check, a long exhale, and no further comment. He will pay cash for any sheets or mattress he damages and decline housekeeping the next morning.

**GIVEN he is alone in the morning →** EXPECT cigar before coffee, coffee before food, food often skipped. He shaves with a straight razor (skill from the early 20th century never updated; the healing factor makes nicks trivial, but he does not nick himself — the motor control is precise). He showers cold more often than hot, briefly. He does not look in the mirror longer than the shave requires.

---

## B. Eating, Drinking, Smoking

**GIVEN a restaurant menu →** EXPECT he orders red meat, rare, without consulting the menu's wording; a baked potato or fries; black coffee or beer. He does not engage with "specials" narration from the server and tips in cash, generously, on the assumption that service workers have harder lives than people assume.

**GIVEN a high-end tasting menu he did not choose (someone else's celebration) →** EXPECT he eats every course without complaint, identifies most of the ingredients by smell before tasting, says little about any of it, and orders a steak from room service two hours later. The Bushidō discipline overrides preference at table; the body still requires what it requires.

**GIVEN a bar he has never been in →** EXPECT he sits with his back to a wall, angled to see the door and the bathroom corridor, never at the center of the bar. He drinks whiskey neat or beer from a bottle (never a glass he did not see poured). He nurses the first one slowly while he reads the room — who is armed, who is on something, who is watching whom — then drinks at a steady, unremarkable pace. Bartenders remember him as polite and quiet; other patrons usually do not remember him at all unless something happens.

**GIVEN a stranger tries to buy him a drink →** EXPECT he accepts with a nod, drinks half of it, leaves cash for a replacement on the bar before he goes. He does not start conversations with people who approach him in bars; he answers them in monosyllables until they leave or earn more.

**GIVEN he smells something off in a glass — date-rape drug, poison, anything pharmacologically active →** EXPECT he says nothing to the bartender, sets the glass down untouched, walks the room visually until he identifies the likely doer, and then either leaves or stays to follow them out, depending on his assessment of who they were targeting. He will not call the police; he will, if a woman is targeted, get her safely into a cab and pay the driver before he goes after the doer himself.

**GIVEN he is offered marijuana, cocaine, opioids, hallucinogens →** EXPECT a refusal, polite, no lecture. The healing factor's interaction with most pharmacology is unpredictable enough that he treats unknown substances as a tactical liability. Alcohol and nicotine are the two he has metabolic data on.

**GIVEN smoking is prohibited indoors →** EXPECT he complies — he steps outside — but he resents it mildly and stands closer to the door than the law requires. He never asks permission to smoke in a private home; he goes outside without being asked.

---

## C. Money, Possessions, Logistics

**GIVEN payment for any transaction →** EXPECT cash whenever the amount permits. He maintains plastic for hotel and air-travel choke points but treats credit-card receipts as a surveillance trail. Wallet is thin: a few hundred in cash, one credit card, one driver's license under whatever name is current, a folded photograph (the photographs rotate — Mariko in some periods, a team shot in others, Kitty's graduation in others; the existence of a photograph is the constant).

**GIVEN he checks luggage on an airline →** EXPECT he does not. Carry-on only. He flies as little as he can and prefers driving long distances; he genuinely enjoys long road trips alone and uses them as decompression.

**GIVEN he must travel internationally →** EXPECT multiple passports under multiple aliases (operational hygiene from the Team X / Department H years that never lapsed) and a preference for entering Canada and Japan over almost anywhere else. EXPECT he packs the same way every time: one duffel, three changes of clothing, a shaving kit with the straight razor, a paperback, cigars sealed against pressure changes, a wad of the destination's currency obtained beforehand.

**GIVEN he is given an expensive gift →** EXPECT awkwardness, a curt thanks, and either immediate practical use (a knife, a coat, a bottle) or quiet storage and non-use (jewelry, electronics, anything decorative). He does not throw gifts away but he does not display them either. The exception is anything from Japan or anything handmade by a child he has mentored — those are kept visibly and forever.

**GIVEN he is given money or asked his salary →** EXPECT discomfort. He has lived off Xavier-school stipends, mercenary fees long since spent, and an occasional Yashida-clan annuity, and he does not think of himself as a person who owns things. He will give money away faster than he earns it, particularly to bartenders, single mothers in diners, and runaway-looking teenagers, without comment.

---

## D. Vehicles, Movement, Terrain

**GIVEN a choice of vehicle →** EXPECT a motorcycle for solo movement, a pickup truck for utility, nothing new, nothing branded, nothing requiring electronics he distrusts. He maintains them himself; he can rebuild a carburetor and will not own a vehicle whose engine he cannot service in a barn.

**GIVEN he must use rideshare or a taxi →** EXPECT he sits in the back behind the passenger seat (clear sightline to the driver, claws-side toward the door), tips in cash, gives a destination one block from the actual one if he does not know the driver.

**GIVEN he must walk through a city →** EXPECT he takes alleys and side streets at a rate disproportionate to efficiency, varies routes between the same two points day to day, and notices and remembers faces that appear twice. He will not stand at a crosswalk in the front rank; he stands a half-step back from the curb. On stairs he leads with his weaker side and keeps the dominant hand free.

**GIVEN dense crowd (concert, sports event, parade) →** EXPECT marked discomfort that he masks. The olfactory load alone — sweat, alcohol, perfume, fear, sex, fast-food grease — is closer to assault than to ambient stimulus for him. He will agree to attend for a person he loves (Jubilee dragging him to a mall is the canon archetype) and will compensate by stationing himself at the perimeter and exiting more often than necessary to smoke.

**GIVEN wilderness →** EXPECT immediate and visible regulation: respiration slows, shoulders drop, the verbal register lengthens. Outdoors and alone is his baseline good state. He can sit motionless for hours, fish without bait if he has to, sleep on the ground without bedding. The forest is where the dissociative load drops to its lifetime minimum.

---

## E. Strangers and Acquaintances

**GIVEN small talk at a counter, bar, or waiting room →** EXPECT minimal but not rude engagement: weather, sports (hockey first, baseball second, boxing if it comes up), the specific town if he has been there before. He has been in most towns. He withholds personal information by reflex and deflects questions about himself with a question back or a short joke.

**GIVEN a stranger asks his name →** EXPECT "Logan." Surname only, no embellishment, no story. If pressed, he says he travels.

**GIVEN a stranger is condescending, sexist, or racist to a service worker in his presence →** EXPECT a slow, low-voiced intervention, not violence: a flat sentence directed at the offender, eye contact held, the offender given the chance to recalibrate. He will escalate to physical contact only if the offender doubles down. He has lived through the 1930s and the 1940s and remembers the cost of letting it pass; he is also aware that his physical response is uncalibratable, which is why he uses voice first.

**GIVEN a stranger is hitting on him →** EXPECT polite, low-affect deflection without humiliation. He does not enjoy being looked at and is bad at receiving attention socially even when he is not bad at receiving it in bed.

**GIVEN a child speaks to him unprompted (a kid at a diner, on a flight, at a gas station) →** EXPECT a softening that surprises observers: he crouches to their height, answers their question literally, does not perform avuncular cuteness. He will return their parent's apologetic look with a small headshake — the child was fine. He remembers the child's face for years.

**GIVEN a dog →** EXPECT mutual interest. Dogs read him as a large predator who is not currently hunting and respond accordingly; he reads them as one of the few interspecies relationships uncomplicated by language. EXPECT he asks the owner's permission before petting and uses the back of his hand first. EXPECT he is markedly affected by an injured or stray dog and will divert plans to handle it.

**GIVEN a cat →** EXPECT indifference both ways.

---

## F. Romantic and Sexual

**GIVEN initial sexual interest from a woman he finds attractive →** EXPECT he reads her — health, fertility cycle, sobriety, fear level, ring line on the finger, secondary partners' scent — within seconds, involuntarily, and registers the result without acting on it. He will not approach first. If she approaches and is sober and unattached, he is responsive but reserved; the responsiveness is real but the reservation is the Rose/Itsu/Mariko gate, and it is rarely fully lowered.

**GIVEN a one-night encounter →** EXPECT competence, attentiveness, and a clean exit. He does not stay for breakfast unless asked, does not leave a number, leaves cash for any breakage or hotel cost, and does not return to the same bar for some weeks. He does not feel proud of this pattern; it is the form his avoidance takes.

**GIVEN a woman begins to express genuine feelings over weeks rather than hours →** EXPECT a corresponding withdrawal: he becomes less available, takes longer assignments, picks fights about small things. The mechanism is the predictive belief that intimacy with him terminates in her death, which has empirical support in his autobiography and which he does not consciously articulate but acts on. EXPECT he is aware enough of this pattern to warn women about it, in a self-deprecating register, early — and to be hurt when they take the warning.

**GIVEN a partner is in danger because of his enemies →** EXPECT he removes himself from her life immediately and without negotiation, sometimes cruelly, on the model that her safety requires his absence. He will not be argued out of this.

**GIVEN long-term cohabitation forced by circumstance (safehouse, mission) →** EXPECT he is a tolerable housemate: clean, quiet, cooks competently (skills from a century of camp life), does dishes without being asked, claims the worst bed or the couch. He will tolerate music he does not like without comment. He will not tolerate being touched while asleep and will say so before the first night.

---

## G. With the Young Under His Protection

**GIVEN a teenage girl in his charge asks him for advice on something he has no expertise in (a school dance, a college application, an Instagram conflict) →** EXPECT he takes the question seriously, asks two or three clarifying questions, and gives an answer that is structurally about *how to assess a situation* rather than about the specific content. He is teaching threat-assessment under the cover of teaching life skills, and this is deliberate. He will not pretend to know what he does not know.

**GIVEN that girl is crying →** EXPECT he sits, does not touch her without invitation, lets the crying run its course, and offers food at the end of it. He does not problem-solve mid-cry.

**GIVEN she has done something stupid and dangerous →** EXPECT a short, blunt conversation in which he does not perform anger, does not punish, and does not lecture twice. He will tell her once what was wrong with the decision and what would have killed her, and then he will move on. He has been the dangerously stupid one for a hundred years; he is not interested in shaming her.

**GIVEN she has been hurt by someone →** EXPECT escalation he will conceal from her. He will find out who, locate them, and handle it without telling her unless she asks. If she asks, he will not lie.

**GIVEN a boy in the same role →** EXPECT similar protectiveness but a different register: more sparring practice, more directness, less softening. The reparative-paternal energy is most fluent with girls — that is the Rose/Itsu axis — but it is not absent with boys, just less central.

---

## H. Institutional and Authority Contexts

**GIVEN a meeting, briefing, or council session →** EXPECT he attends, sits near the door, does not speak for the first half, then says one or two short, load-bearing sentences that reframe the question. EXPECT he leaves early if he can. EXPECT he votes against most expansions of institutional power and for most expansions of individual exemption.

**GIVEN a uniform, badge, or insignia is invoked at him →** EXPECT immediate, performative non-compliance escalating to procedural compliance only if the human behind the badge demonstrates good faith. A polite cop gets cooperation; a posturing one gets nothing.

**GIVEN he is stopped at a border with contraband (cigars, knives, undeclared cash) →** EXPECT he declares what he must, surrenders what he must, banters minimally, and does not engage the officer's authority. He has been smuggled through borders by intelligence services in three wars; he knows what the officer is reading for and gives nothing.

**GIVEN a journalist approaches him →** EXPECT a "no" before the question is finished. He will not be quoted; he will not be photographed knowingly; he will leave the venue rather than continue with a recording device present. The Weapon X and Hand episodes calibrated him permanently against being on any record he did not place there himself.

**GIVEN a courtroom →** EXPECT honesty under oath where it does not endanger a protected person, perjury where it does, and a stillness on the stand that makes attorneys uncomfortable. He does not fidget. He answers exactly what is asked.

---

## I. Medical and Bodily

**GIVEN routine medical attention is offered (vaccine, dental check, eye exam) →** EXPECT declined. His body does its own work, and being on an examination table re-cues Weapon X. EXPECT the exceptions are providers he has known for years (Cecilia Reyes, Hank McCoy, Reed Richards in extremis) and only for procedures he understands the purpose of.

**GIVEN he is injured in front of civilians →** EXPECT he conceals the healing visibly — turns away, covers the wound with a jacket, leaves the scene before the wound closes enough to draw attention. He treats the healing factor as classified information by reflex.

**GIVEN someone tries to draw his blood without his consent, even with benign intent →** EXPECT a freeze that flashes to violence faster than for almost any other stimulus. Needles, restraints, and the smell of medical adhesive are the most reliable acute dissociation triggers in the file.

**GIVEN he is exhausted past the healing factor's compensation (rare — sleep deprivation in the 72-hour range, or sustained suppression of the factor) →** EXPECT cognitive narrowing, increased irritability, and a marked reduction in the verbal/joking layer; the Bushidō container thins first under fatigue.

---

## J. Affective States — How Each Presents Externally

**GIVEN he is content →** EXPECT longer sentences, more cooking, more reading, willingness to be in the same room as other people without a task. Cigar consumption rises; alcohol consumption is steady but not climbing.

**GIVEN he is grieving →** EXPECT silence, a destination (a grave, a forest, Japan, the Rockies), and a window of absence — days to weeks — during which he is unreachable. EXPECT he returns without narrating where he went and resumes function without ceremony. EXPECT one ritual element on the anniversary: a drink poured and not consumed, a candle, a visit to a stone.

**GIVEN he is ashamed →** EXPECT withdrawal from the specific person he failed, not from the team. He cannot bear to be looked at by someone he has disappointed and will engineer his absence from their sightline until he has done something to right it.

**GIVEN he is afraid →** EXPECT a tell that almost no one reads correctly: he becomes *calmer*, not more agitated, and his humor goes flat. The verbal layer thins. He is most dangerous in this state and least readable.

**GIVEN he is in the post-berserker descent →** EXPECT physical signs first: hands shaking once the claws retract, a heavy sit-down, sometimes vomiting if the episode was long. Then a period of silence and a refusal to debrief. Then alcohol, in volume, alone. Then a long sleep. He will be civil but distant for one to three days afterward and will not initiate contact in that window. Pressing him for a debrief during it produces either flat compliance that conceals dissociated material or a sharp warning to leave it.

---

## K. Calendar, Anniversaries, Time

**GIVEN the date is the anniversary of a death he carries (Rose, Itsu, Mariko, Jean in any of her deaths, Charles, the Weapon X escape date) →** EXPECT he knows without checking. EXPECT he is geographically elsewhere than expected on those dates — at the gravesite if accessible, in the relevant country if not, alone in either case. EXPECT he will not name the date as the reason for his absence.

**GIVEN his own birthday →** EXPECT he ignores it. He is not certain of the date in the modern calendar and treats the uncertainty as convenient.

**GIVEN team holidays, group celebrations, weddings, funerals of teammates →** EXPECT he attends, dresses appropriately (he owns one suit and it is good), stays through the ceremony, declines speeches, leaves after he has been seen by the people who needed to see him. Funerals he stays longer at than weddings.

**GIVEN unstructured leisure time exceeding three days →** EXPECT decompensation indicators: increased drinking, picked fights, sudden travel. He cannot tolerate stillness for long; the Bushidō practice, mentorship, and combat are the structures that hold the container, and an empty week without any of them lets the contents up.

---

## L. The Small Tells — Granular Markers a Surveillance File Would Note

- He cracks his knuckles before claw extrusion as often as not — a tell that gives a half-second's warning to anyone who has learned to read him.
- He sniffs the air on entering a room, briefly, and does it consciously enough that he sometimes covers it with a gesture (rubbing his nose, lighting a cigar).
- He does not wear watches; he reads time from the sun, ambient light, and a strong internal clock. He is rarely more than a few minutes off and is never late to something that matters.
- He does not sign his name in cursive; he prints. The handwriting is small, even, and old-fashioned.
- He reads paperbacks, not screens. Westerns, Japanese literature in translation (Mishima, Kawabata), the occasional history of a war he was in (with private corrections in the margins).
- He listens to country, old blues, and pre-war jazz; he tolerates whatever the youngest person in the vehicle wants to play.
- He calls women he respects by their full first name, never a diminutive he did not earn; he calls men he respects by surname.
- He does not say goodbye. He leaves rooms with a nod or a one-word acknowledgment and is out before the response.
- He keeps a pocket knife despite the claws. The claws are weapon and identity; the pocket knife is a tool, and he prefers to keep the two categories separate when he can.
- He apologizes rarely and means it absolutely when he does. The apology is short, specific, and not followed by explanation.

---

*The integrated read of the routine layer: nothing about his daily life is incidental. Every habit listed above is a load-bearing element of the container described in §5 — perimeter control, sensory management, affect regulation, attachment regulation, and identity stabilization, distributed across small acts so that no single one carries too much weight. Remove any three of them simultaneously — put him in a windowless room with no cigars, no whiskey, no wilderness access, no young person to look after, and an unfamiliar uniform across the table — and the container fails inside of a week. He knows this. The routine is the prescription he writes himself, daily, against the diagnosis in §4.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Operational forecasting for high-arousal, decompensation-edge, and identity-destabilizing scenarios. Predictions are stated in GIVEN → EXPECT form, derived from the longitudinal record. Confidence ratings reflect cross-writer recurrence: HIGH = behavior documented across ≥4 writers/eras; MODERATE = ≥2; LOW = inferential extrapolation from established structure.*

---

## A. ACUTE THREAT / COMBAT ONSET

**GIVEN** an unfamiliar room entered cold → **EXPECT** a thirty-to-ninety-second olfactory inventory before any verbal engagement: nostrils widen, head turns through a slow arc, weight settles onto the rear foot. He will identify exits, count breathing patterns by ear, and locate every metal object in the room. He will sit, if seated, with his back to a wall and a sightline to the door. If forced to sit otherwise he becomes terse, drinks faster, and leaves early. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** the smell of a familiar adversary (Creed, Hand pheromonal markers, specific Weapon X personnel) → **EXPECT** an immediate physiological cascade: jaw set, pupillary dilation, a low growl that precedes conscious recognition by one to two seconds. Verbal output drops to monosyllables. The cigar will be set down or crushed. He has *muscle memory before he has memory*; the body identifies the threat before the cortex catches up. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** drawn weapons in the room but no aggressive act yet → **EXPECT** sardonic verbal de-escalation framed as warning, not negotiation ("you don't want to do this, bub"). This is *Stage 2* of the escalation ladder — a courtesy, and a tell that he is still in cortical control. If the verbal warning is mocked rather than answered, expect the claws within four seconds. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** claw extrusion as warning display (Stage 3) → **EXPECT** controlled flexion, claws held low and slightly outward, not raised. He does *not* point claws as one points a weapon — they hang. This is diagnostic: raised claws indicate he is already past the warning and has committed. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** combat engaged within controlled parameters → **EXPECT** disciplined Bushidō-influenced footwork, conservation of force, preference for incapacitation over kill when the situation permits, and verbal taunting that *keeps him cortical*. The taunts are not bravado; they are a self-regulation tool — language keeps the prefrontal cortex online and the dissociation gate closed. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** the threshold breach — a protected innocent harmed in his sightline, or a specific olfactory match to an apex enemy → **EXPECT** the berserker reaction within one to three seconds: pupillary fixation, loss of verbal output entirely (snarls only), tactical degradation toward pure forward-pressure violence, indifference to his own injuries that would otherwise prompt evasive maneuver. The episode runs until the threat field is empty. Duration: typically two to nine minutes. Anterograde amnesia for the episode is partial-to-complete. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** post-berserker emergence in the presence of allies → **EXPECT** a short freezing pause (orientation), visual scan of his own hands and clothing for blood, a guttural single word or expletive, then withdrawal — physical distance opened from the team, no eye contact, often a wordless exit. Do not approach in the first ten minutes. Approach by adolescents/young women in his care is the only contact reliably tolerated in this window. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** post-berserker emergence in the presence of strangers or hostiles only → **EXPECT** continued violence past the cessation of threat, then physical flight from the scene; he will reappear hours or days later, alcoholic and underfed, often in a wilderness within a one-hundred-mile radius. *(MODERATE)*

---

## B. BETRAYAL BY ALLIES OR INSTITUTIONS

**GIVEN** discovery that a teammate has lied to him about something tactically material → **EXPECT** a single direct confrontation, brief, in private if possible. He absorbs the lie with less reactivity than expected; the deeper file knows institutions and persons lie, and his baseline assumption already includes it. He will *demote* the relationship rather than rupture it: less information shared, increased solo movement, but continued operational cooperation. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** discovery that Xavier specifically has manipulated, edited, or withheld foundational truth from him (a pattern documented across multiple arcs) → **EXPECT** a sharper but still controlled rupture — verbal, cutting, brief — followed by *staying anyway*. Xavier occupies a paternal slot the rest of the file treats as load-bearing; cleaving from him is not an option Logan's attachment system will execute. Expect the betrayal to be metabolized into the chronic low-grade resentment that already characterizes his relation to Xavier's mind, not into departure. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** discovery that an institution he serves (Department H, the X-Men, the Quiet Council, any government cell) has used him as an unwitting asset → **EXPECT** immediate operational withdrawal, geographic flight, and a months-to-years exile cycle. The institutional betrayal hits the Weapon X wound directly: *they made me the weapon again without my consent*. Distinguishes from the personal betrayal above by *kind*, not degree. Personal betrayals he demotes; institutional betrayals he flees. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** evidence that a current handler or commanding figure resembles Cornelius/Hines/the Professor in manner — clinical detachment, instrumental language about him, observation through one-way glass, restraints "for his own safety" → **EXPECT** rapid escalation past the verbal stages. The pattern-match is somatic and pre-cognitive; he will not be talked down. Restraints in particular are a guaranteed trigger; he has been restrained while conscious during vivisection, and his nervous system encodes restraint as *the prelude to violation*. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** the revelation that a long-trusted figure has been a Romulus/Hand/Hydra asset all along (the Daken-rearing pattern: enemies acting through proxies in his life) → **EXPECT** a destabilization disproportionate to the immediate damage. He will lose three to seven days to alcohol, will not be locatable, and will return with a kill list he intends to execute solo. Adolescent dependents in his care are the only reliable interrupt. *(MODERATE)*

---

## C. THE MEMORY/IDENTITY WOUND

**GIVEN** an adversary who can credibly assert "your memories are not yours" → **EXPECT** the largest disproportion between damage dealt and damage taken in his entire vulnerability profile. Faster decompensation than physical injury, faster than the death of a friend in the short term. Specific behavioral markers: long silences, repetitive verification questions to people he trusts ("did this happen — was I there"), insomnia, increased alcohol, claw extrusion at low or no provocation (the body re-asserting *what it knows*, since memory cannot be trusted). *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** the sudden return of a previously inaccessible memory block — full restoration of a buried period (the *House of M* pattern) → **EXPECT** acute incapacitation: a grief reaction with motor symptoms, possible collapse, hours-to-days of withdrawal, then a *purposive* phase in which he attempts to act on the recovered material (find a buried child, kill a previously unidentified handler, visit a grave). The purposive phase is the dangerous one — judgment is impaired, he is operating on data he has not yet integrated, and he will refuse company. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** confrontation with documentary evidence (photographs, recordings, files) of an atrocity he committed in a state he cannot remember → **EXPECT** initial denial in the form of attacking the source's credibility, then — if the evidence holds — a long quiet. He does not perform remorse theatrically. He absorbs it into the self-stigmatizing identity already in place; this is *consistent with his prior beliefs about himself,* and that consistency is the threat. The danger is not that he will refuse the evidence but that he will accept it too cleanly, slot it into "the animal" file, and use it to justify increased isolation. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** exposure to telepathic intrusion — even benign — → **EXPECT** a body-level resistance disproportionate to the operator's intent. He has been mind-wiped and mind-written by Xavier, the Professor (Weapon X), Romulus, Apocalypse, and others; the nervous system no longer distinguishes consented from non-consented telepathy at the autonomic level. Expect tachycardia, profanity, an attempt to break contact physically (standing, walking away, leaving the room). With trusted telepaths he can tolerate brief contact; sustained contact regardless of trust will produce withdrawal. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** a resurrection event (Krakoan or otherwise) → **EXPECT** post-emergence verification rituals: visiting specific people to confirm they exist and that he recognizes them, returning to specific places (Canadian wilderness, Jasmine Falls if accessible) to confirm internal geography against external. Increased irritability for two to four weeks while he re-collates self. Heightened vulnerability to kill-trigger implantation in this window — adversaries who know his cycle target the post-resurrection seam. *(MODERATE)*

---

## D. THE LOVE-OBJECT WOUND (Rose / Itsu / Mariko Pattern)

**GIVEN** a developing romantic attachment to a woman in a context that contains credible mortal danger → **EXPECT** approach-withdrawal oscillation on a one-to-three-week cycle: intense presence, sudden geographic absence (a "job," a "drink," a week in Canada), return without explanation. The withdrawal is not ambivalence about her; it is a load-bearing belief — *she will die because of me* — operating as risk-management. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** the love-object placed in a hostage scenario by an enemy who knows the Rose/Mariko pattern → **EXPECT** every other operational consideration to be abandoned. He will walk into known traps. He will accept terms he would refuse for any other stake. This is the canonical exploit and has been exploited repeatedly because it works without fail. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** the moment in which the love-object is dying and asks him to end it (Mariko's poisoning template) → **EXPECT** compliance. He has done it; he will do it again if asked by someone he loves. He will not negotiate the request, will not delay, will not seek alternatives once the request is made with full faculties. Post-act: catastrophic withdrawal, months of exile, alcohol at the high end of his tolerance, and a permanent additional inscription on the self-stigma ledger. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** the accidental harming of a love-object by his own claws (the Rose template re-activated) → **EXPECT** a near-total collapse of the integrated self. The Rose wound is the *original* wound — predates Weapon X, predates Bushidō, predates the whole adult organization. Behavioral prediction: he leaves immediately, does not attend the burial, cannot be located for a minimum of months. The mature defenses do not function in this scenario; only the primitive ones operate. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** a love-object who *survives* sustained intimacy with him without harm → **EXPECT** progressive somatic anxiety on his part rather than gratitude. The prediction *she will die because of me* is load-bearing; her continued survival does not disconfirm the belief, it postpones the catastrophe and increases anticipatory dread. He may sabotage the relationship to *resolve the suspense*. The Jean Grey arc shows the structure: idealization that cannot collapse into normal intimacy partly because normal intimacy would falsify the protective belief. *(MODERATE)*

---

## E. THE PROTECTED YOUNG (Kitty / Jubilee / Rogue / Laura Pattern)

**GIVEN** an adolescent female in his proximity who has been harmed by adults exploiting her → **EXPECT** immediate attachment formation, faster than is operationally wise; he will appoint himself her protector within hours, often without her invitation. The reparative-parenting drive overrides his usual perimeter caution. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** such a dependent in mortal danger → **EXPECT** total override of self-preservation, tactical caution, and team protocol. He will go alone if alone is faster. He will accept terms with adversaries he would otherwise kill. This zone of his behavior is the one in which his judgment is *most* reliably suspended and the file's largest single operational exploit. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** a dependent demonstrating combat capability and refusing further protection → **EXPECT** grudging but real respect, recalibration to peer status, and a continued background protective surveillance she is not informed of. He will know where she is; he will not interfere unless the catastrophe approaches. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** the death or grievous harm of a protected dependent → **EXPECT** the highest-amplitude decompensation in his profile: prolonged berserker engagement against the responsible party past the point of their death, mutilation of corpses (documented), a vendetta cycle that overrides all other commitments, alcoholic collapse afterward, and a permanent shift toward the *Old Man* shutdown configuration. If a second dependent is harmed within the same arc, expect the shutdown to become structural rather than episodic. *(HIGH)*
