**GIVEN** Laura specifically in distress → **EXPECT** the most regulated and competent paternal behavior in his repertoire; she is the file's only clean opportunity to do fatherhood differently and he handles her with a deliberateness he extends to no other relationship. Expect uncharacteristic patience, willingness to wait through long silences, refusal of his usual exits. *(HIGH)*

---

## F. THE DAKEN WOUND

**GIVEN** confrontation with Daken → **EXPECT** an emotional configuration unique in the file: he cannot bring himself to kill, cannot bring himself to trust, cannot bring himself to walk away. Combat with Daken is *under-committed* on his side; he absorbs damage he would not absorb from a stranger. Daken knows this and exploits it. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** Daken weaponizing the Itsu memory in conversation → **EXPECT** loss of verbal composure, hand tremor, increased intake afterward. The Itsu wound is the *unrepaired* love-object wound — he never grieved it inside an integrated self because he didn't remember it for decades. Direct invocation collapses him faster than physical assault. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** Daken in mortal danger from a third party → **EXPECT** intervention despite the hostile history; the paternal-protective drive does not perform triage by deservingness. *(MODERATE)*

---

## G. SABRETOOTH — THE STABLE PAIR-BOND

**GIVEN** a birthday — his, or the unmarked annual date that has historically functioned as Creed's ritual occasion → **EXPECT** elevated baseline irritability, perimeter behavior intensified, weapons checked more often than usual, an unconscious northward drift if he is mobile. He may not articulate why. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** Sabretooth's death made permanent and incontestable → **EXPECT**, paradoxically, *worse* outcomes than Sabretooth's continued existence. The pair-bond is load-bearing for his identity; remove the antagonist around whom he has organized a century of self-definition and the file predicts disorientation, depressive symptoms, and increased vulnerability to other destabilizers. He needs the enemy. *(LOW–MODERATE — extrapolated from structural role)*

**GIVEN** Sabretooth attempting (credibly or otherwise) reconciliation, redemption, or alliance → **EXPECT** rejection more violent than the ordinary hostility. The threat of *losing the stable enemy* is more destabilizing than the enemy's attacks. He will refuse the alliance even when it is operationally optimal. *(MODERATE)*

---

## H. TEMPTATION

**GIVEN** an offer of total memory restoration with verified provenance → **EXPECT** apparent eagerness, then refusal at the moment of execution, or acceptance followed by acute decompensation. He wants to know who he is; he also knows the existing container holds and that full restoration may shatter it. Behavior is overdetermined; *act of refusal at the threshold* is the modal prediction. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** an offer of permanent death — clean, dignified, witnessed → **EXPECT** serious consideration. The low-grade lifelong wish for an ending that will stick is a documented substrate. The interrupt is invariably the existence of a dependent who would be unprotected; remove the dependents and the offer becomes accept-able. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** an offer to be Weapon X again *voluntarily* in service of a cause he endorses (the Apocalypse "Death" override, *Enemy of the State*, various recurrences) → **EXPECT** refusal at the conscious level and vulnerability at the unconscious level. The weapon-self is *familiar*, and familiarity is sedating to a hypervigilant nervous system. Adversaries who frame the offer as "let go" rather than "kill" achieve higher penetration. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** an offer of command or institutional authority (Quiet Council seat, school headmaster, Avengers leadership variant) → **EXPECT** reluctant acceptance, competent execution, and chronic low-grade discomfort manifesting as escape behaviors: night patrols he doesn't need to run, solo missions assigned to himself, longer cigar breaks. Authority is presumptively a handler-role; occupying it inverts the schema and produces unease he cannot articulate. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** an offer of full sobriety — pharmacological, psychic, or supernatural elimination of the alcohol need → **EXPECT** refusal. The alcohol is functionally load-bearing; removing it without replacing the affect-regulation function would expose the unbuffered nervous system. He knows this at a non-verbal level. *(MODERATE)*

---

## I. PEACE, STILLNESS, AND UNSTRUCTURED TIME

**GIVEN** a sustained period without external threat → **EXPECT** decompensation on a faster timeline than under combat conditions. Specific markers in the first week: increased nocturnal restlessness, escalating intake, longer wilderness sorties; second week: irritability with allies, picked fights, deliberate sabotage of his own situation to restore familiar conditions. The Krakoan-era institutional roles and the recurrent teaching posts are *self-prescribed structure* against this collapse. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** a forced vacation, sabbatical, or convalescence → **EXPECT** non-compliance within seventy-two hours: he will invent a job, take a solo mission, or simply disappear into terrain. Attempts to enforce rest physically replicate restraint and will be resisted to the threshold of violence. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** stillness imposed by injury severe enough to outpace the healing factor temporarily → **EXPECT** the most psychologically dangerous window in his profile. He cannot move, cannot drink to effect, cannot pretend, cannot escape. Suicidal ideation surfaces in this window if it surfaces at all. Trusted persons in proximity are the only reliable buffer; the protected-young in proximity are the *most* reliable. *(MODERATE)*

---

## J. THE SAMURAI IDEAL AS LEVER

**GIVEN** an appeal framed in Bushidō terms — duty, the requirement of honor, the obligation of the strong to the weak → **EXPECT** recruitment to causes he would otherwise refuse on tactical or political grounds. The samurai ideal is his highest functioning and his deepest exploit. Adversaries who understand this and deploy it (Mariko's family, Yashida heirs, occasional Hand operatives running long cons) bypass his usual skepticism. *(HIGH)*

**GIVEN** confrontation with his own failures against the Bushidō standard (the implanted-kill body count, the *Old Man* slaughter, Itsu, Mariko) → **EXPECT** disabling shame rather than defensive denial. He has internalized the ideal sufficiently that his failures against it are operative. Adversaries running a "you are not the samurai you pretend to be" line can produce hesitation in combat — a documented vulnerability. The counter-tell: if he goes *silent* under such taunting rather than answering with violence, the taunt has landed. *(MODERATE)*

**GIVEN** an opportunity to perform a ritualized act of restitution within the Bushidō frame — a death witnessed honorably, a debt repaid, a vow fulfilled — → **EXPECT** willing participation even at lethal cost. The frame metabolizes loss in a way the rest of his cognitive apparatus cannot. *(MODERATE)*

---

## K. AGGREGATE DECOMPENSATION TIMELINE

Layered exposure to multiple wound-classes within a single arc compounds non-linearly. The file predicts the following ordering of decompensation pressure, from most to least disabling:

1. *Harm to a protected dependent* + *implanted-memory revelation* in the same window → catastrophic; full *Old Man* shutdown configuration becomes likely.
2. *Love-object dies on his claws or by his hand* → months-to-years exile, structural identity damage, integration of the loss into the self-stigma ledger.
3. *Institutional betrayal that re-frames him as Weapon X* → exile cycle, kill list, alcohol; recoverable but slowly.
4. *Sustained telepathic or chemical override of will* → acute decompensation, dangerous to bystanders during emergence.
5. *Full memory restoration* → acute incapacitation, then dangerous purposive phase.
6. *Permanent removal of Sabretooth* → slow disorientation, no acute phase, chronic depressive drift.
7. *Imposed peace* → measured in weeks; the slowest collapse, but the one he is least equipped to recognize as a collapse.

The file's terminal observation: the predictable failures are all variations on a single equation — *people he loves are made into instruments of his harming, by parties who know him better than he knows himself.* The healing factor closes every wound except this one. The container holds against everything but the original shape of the wound, repeated. He knows. That knowledge is what the cigars and the silence and the northward drift are for.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Compiled under the protection-and-understanding remit. This section catalogues the levers because adversaries already know them; the file exists so allies do too, and so that the subject's handlers within sympathetic institutions (Xavier-era school, Krakoan Council, ad-hoc operational teams) can recognize the moves being run on him before he himself does — because, per Section 3, his autobiographical channel is compromised and he often cannot.*

---

## 1. The Master Taxonomy

Logan's vulnerabilities sort into six structural categories. Each is a doorway. Each has been walked through, on the record, by both enemies and friends.

1. **Identity-channel attacks** — exploitation of compromised autobiography (implanted memory, false history, triggered compulsion).
2. **The protected-child override** — exploitation of his reparative-paternal attachment system.
3. **The beloved-woman pattern** — exploitation of the Rose/Itsu/Mariko template.
4. **Sensory/threshold attacks** — exploitation of hyperacute senses and the berserker ladder.
5. **The samurai ledger** — exploitation of the Bushidō ideal as both recruiter and disabler.
6. **The stillness vulnerability** — exploitation of unstructured time, sobriety, and peace.

These are not independent. The most effective historical operations against him (Weapon X, the Hand's *Enemy of the State* conversion, Romulus, Mysterio in *Old Man Logan*, Persephone in *Return*) braided three or four of them.

---

## 2. Identity-Channel Attacks — How to Destabilize Him Fastest

The single highest-yield attack surface. His autobiographical memory has been overwritten so many times (Weapon X conditioning, Team X implants under the Professor, Romulus's century-spanning manipulations, Apocalypse's Death-of-Horsemen rewrite, the Hand's brainwashing in *Enemy of the State*, Persephone's kill-trigger conditioning in *Return of Wolverine*) that he treats his own memory as suspect by default. An adversary who can credibly destabilize the *meta-question* — "is this memory mine?" — lands a wound the healing factor cannot close.

**Operational signature of an identity attack in progress:**

- Sudden mid-action hesitation, eyes unfocused, head tilted slightly as if listening to something inside.
- Repeated touching of the temple or the back of the neck (the implant locus from Weapon X is somatically encoded).
- Verbal regression to one-word responses; the wisecrack apparatus shuts off.
- Asking the same orienting question twice within minutes ("what year is it," "where's Jeannie," "did I—").
- Increased blink rate, asymmetric pupil response — pre-fugue signs.
- A specific, observable *grip change* on whatever he is holding: fingers stiffen, knuckles whiten, but he does not act.

**How adversaries reach this channel:**

- *Plausible photo/video evidence of him committing an atrocity he does not remember.* Devastating because it is statistically likely to be true; the healing factor permits him to have done almost anything across a century. (Used by Romulus, by Mystique, by the Hand.)
- *Triggers planted under prior conditioning* — code phrases, scents (notably the Weapon X facility's specific industrial-antiseptic chemistry), specific musical fragments. Persephone's protocol used somatic triggers; Hand conditioning used scent and ritual posture.
- *Producing a "memory" of a beloved figure that conflicts with his actual (or actual-feeling) memory of them.* Forces him to choose which version of Jean / Mariko / Kitty to trust; either choice is destabilizing.
- *Reintroducing handlers from his past* (Sabretooth, Maverick, a Team X face). Their mere presence reorganizes him into the operational mode of that era.

**How protectors close this channel:**

- *Anchoring objects.* He keeps a small number of physical tokens — Mariko's tantō, photographs, the dog tags — that he uses as autobiographical evidence. Ensure he has access to them under stress.
- *Witnessed reality-testing from a trusted, durable peer.* Xavier in his lifetime; Kurt Wagner; Ororo. Not a romantic partner (the romantic channel is itself compromised) and not a child (he will protect them rather than disclose to them). The voice must be male or maternal-peer, calm, low-register, and must *name what is happening*: "Logan. Someone has put something in your head. We're going to work it out. Sit down." Compliance probability rises sharply when the intervention is *named* rather than soothed-around.
- *Time-and-place orientation* delivered factually, not anxiously: today's date, the location, who is in the room, what was happening before the episode.
- *Refusal of demands for immediate decision.* Adversaries exploiting an identity attack will press him to act now; the counter is to make stillness available without making it mandatory.

**Predictive note.** When an identity attack succeeds, his behavior becomes more — not less — competent in the short term. He executes whatever the implanted directive is with surgical precision and full berserker capacity. The dissociative crisis surfaces *after* completion. Adversaries time this; protectors should too.

---

## 3. The Protected-Child Override

His reparative-paternal attachment system is the cleanest-functioning subsystem he has, and therefore the most reliable to weaponize against him. The pattern: an adolescent (preferentially female: Kitty, Jubilee, Rogue, Armor, X-23, Idie, the Stepford triplets when threatened) in credible danger overrides every other consideration including tactical judgment, mission objectives, his own survival, and orders from trusted figures including Xavier.

**Operational behavior under this override:**

- Immediate disengagement from current task without explanation.
- Linear, undeviating route toward the endangered child — he will go through walls, through allies, through tactical disadvantage.
- Suppression of berserker dissociation *in the child's presence* (he will not let her see it) and full expression of it once she is screened from view.
- Post-rescue: protracted physical proximity, gruff verbal minimization, a meal cooked or procured for the child, a lesson delivered. The lesson is always *survival skill specific to the threat just survived* — he is teaching her to handle the next attempt without him.

**How adversaries exploit:**

- *Hostage configurations.* Used by Hand, Hellfire Club, Mojo, Mystique, Sinister.
- *False endangerment.* Engineered scenarios that appear to threaten a protected child in order to draw him into a kill-box.
- *Threatening one child to coerce action against another target.* The most cynical version; he will almost always comply on the calculation that he can clean up after.
- *Recruitment of his protected children as adversaries* (Hand's conversion attempts on Kitty; manipulation of X-23). The most disabling configuration in his repertoire — he cannot fight them.

**How protectors mobilize:**

- *In legitimate emergencies,* the protected-child invocation is the single fastest way to get full effort from him. State the child's name and condition; do not bury it in briefing.
- *In recruitment for difficult missions,* frame the mission in terms of children at risk downstream — not as appeals to abstract justice, which he discounts.

**How protectors must defend:**

- *Verify endangerment claims independently before relaying to him.* He does not verify; his system runs ahead of his judgment. Adversaries know this.
- *Limit operational knowledge of his protected children's locations.* This is the Xavier-era discipline. Krakoan-era resurrection logistics complicate it.
- *When he returns from a rescue, do not debrief immediately.* He needs the meal-and-lesson ritual completed first. Interrupting it produces irritability disproportionate to the interruption.

---

## 4. The Beloved-Woman Pattern (The Canonical Kill-Shot)

The structural fact: across 130 chronological years, every woman he has loved with full intimate investment has died — Rose (impaled on his bone claws as a child, accident), Itsu (murdered while pregnant with Daken), Mariko (poisoned, delivered the killing mercy stroke at her request), and the recurring near-loss of Jean Grey. His operating belief, load-bearing and not falsifiable by reassurance: *intimacy with me is fatal to her.*

**Behavioral signatures of an active romantic attachment:**

- *Approach phase:* unusual stillness in her presence; voice drops in volume and pitch; cigar consumption decreases noticeably; sleep deepens (he sleeps badly otherwise — see §8). Increased grooming (beard maintained, shirts cleaner).
- *Mid-phase:* he begins to teach her something — a knife stance, a way to read a room, a Japanese phrase. The teaching *is* the intimacy; words about the relationship are nearly absent.
- *Withdrawal phase (predictable, typically 4–14 weeks in):* geographic absence without warning, increased drinking, return with a wound that "needed healing alone." This is the Rose-prediction asserting itself. He calls it being honest with her. It is symptom.

**How adversaries exploit:**

- *Engineering a scenario where he must kill the beloved or watch her die.* This is the canonical move because it *works*: Mariko-by-poison, Jean-Phoenix-on-the-moon, the *X-Men: The End* and Mystique configurations. Disables him for months to years.
- *Threatening women he has had peripheral romantic contact with* (Yukio, Jessica Drew, others) on the assumption that the pattern generalizes. It partially does.
- *Producing a woman who resembles a lost love* (Mystique's exploitation of Jean's death is the paradigmatic operation here). His olfactory acuity should defeat shape-shifters — but emotional override degrades that filter. Documented.

**How protectors mitigate:**

- *Do not stage rescue scenarios that recapitulate the pattern.* Allies have, accidentally, by placing romantic partners as bait. The cost is high.
- *When a beloved figure does die, the post-loss window (6–18 months) is the highest-risk period for self-destructive deployment.* He will accept suicide-mission profiles in that window that he would refuse otherwise. Do not offer them.
- *Do not reassure him that the pattern will not repeat.* The reassurance is not believable to him and signals that you do not understand the file. Acknowledge it. Then plan around it.

---

## 5. Sensory and Threshold Attacks — The Berserker Ladder

His escalation ladder (Section 5 of the workup) is consistent across writers and decades. Every rung is exploitable in both directions.

**Rung 1 — Sensory cue / hyperarousal.** Smell of blood (specific subtypes: arterial vs. venous, fresh vs. hours-old, the iron-and-adrenaline signature of fear-blood), familiar enemy pheromones (Sabretooth's scent is the most heavily encoded; he will know Creed is within a quarter-mile before sight), specific perfumes associated with prior trauma, the antiseptic chemistry of the Weapon X facility.

- *Adversary leverage:* salting an environment with one of these triggers to pre-load his arousal before negotiation.
- *Protector mitigation:* in fraught meetings, control the olfactory environment. Neutral-scent rooms. No surprise reintroductions of trauma-coded figures. If Sabretooth must be in the building, tell him before he smells.

**Rung 2 — Cognitive narrowing, sardonic verbal warnings.** The wisecracks at this stage are diagnostic, not affective. They are him *informing the room* of his arousal level while he still can. Their cessation is the marker that Rung 3 is imminent.

- *Adversary leverage:* none particularly — this rung is hard to exploit and easy to misread.
- *Protector mitigation:* when the jokes stop, the window for de-escalation is closing. Do not press.

**Rung 3 — Claw extrusion as warning display.** Note the *one-claw* extrusion is calibrated communication; *all six* is past warning. The dorsal-hand laceration during extrusion is pain he has volunteered into — he is announcing willingness to pay the entry cost of violence.

- *Protector mitigation:* at one-claw, sit down, lower your voice, do not break eye contact but do not stare. State the situation factually. Offer a route to disengage that does not require him to back down publicly (he will not).

**Rung 4 — Engaged combat, controlled.** Still recoverable. He retains target discrimination, will not strike non-combatants, can be called off by a trusted voice.

**Rung 5 — Threshold breach → berserker dissociation.** Triggered by: harm to a protected person *in his sight*; the specific scent of Hand operatives or Weapon X personnel; the combination of his own injury with smelling Sabretooth; surprise attacks from behind by someone he had categorized as ally. Consciousness narrows or splits; behavior becomes automatized; target discrimination degrades but does not vanish (he has, on record, *not* killed bystanders in this state, which suggests the moral architecture is preserved below the dissociative line).

- *Adversary leverage:* deliberately triggering this state in a populated environment to produce collateral damage attributable to him. Used as a frame-up tactic.
- *Protector mitigation:* the only reliable interruptions on record are (a) the voice of a protected child calling his name, (b) Xavier's telepathic intervention (no longer always available), (c) Kurt Wagner's specific calm baritone and physical proximity, (d) catastrophic physical incapacitation. Generic shouting, generic restraint, and generic telepathy fail.

**Rung 6 — Post-episode crash.** Shame, withdrawal, alcohol, geographic flight. This is also the *psychotherapeutic window* — defenses are at their lowest, he is most accessible to genuine contact, and meaningful intervention placed here lands. It is also the highest self-destruction risk window in any given week.

- *Protector practice:* presence without demand. Do not debrief. Do not analyze. Sit, share a drink, share silence, share food. The Kurt-Wagner-on-a-rooftop posture. Words later, sometimes much later.

---

## 6. The Samurai Ledger — Recruitment and Disablement Through Bushidō

Bushidō is the prosthesis he built across forty-plus years at Jasmine Falls and after Mariko, to substitute imposed external structure for an internal affect-regulation system that does not function. It is therefore both his highest-functioning mode and his deepest shame ledger.

**Recruitment via the ledger.**

- He will accept missions framed in terms of *honor obligation to a specific named person* that he would refuse if framed as policy, strategy, or institutional necessity.
- He will accept apprenticeship/teaching duties framed as *passing on what was taught to me* — invoke Bando Saburo, invoke Ogun (carefully — Ogun is also a trauma node), invoke the Yashida lineage.
- He will accept severe personal cost in service of *keeping a word given*. The given word is a hard contract for him in a way nothing else is.

**Disablement via the ledger.**

- Confronting him with his failures against the ideal (Mariko's death, the Daken outcome, the people killed under brainwashing) recruits the shame-circuit and can disable him for the duration of the conversation and beyond.
- *Adversaries who frame their own conduct in samurai terms* (Silver Samurai under certain incarnations; Ogun; some Hand leadership) activate a complicated honor-protocol response that slows his combat tempo and may produce hesitation he cannot afford.
- *Allies who invoke the ideal cynically* lose access to it permanently. He notices.

**Protector practice.** Do not invoke Bushidō to coerce or to praise. Invoke it only when accurately operative. Treat the ideal as load-bearing in his architecture, not as flavor.

---

## 7. The Stillness Vulnerability

He decompensates in peace faster than in war. Unstructured time, sobriety, and absence of operational role produce the conditions in which intrusive memory, depersonalization, and the implanted-memory question rise to surface. *Old Man Logan*'s shutdown is the extreme presentation; the everyday version is the four-day binge after a mission ends.

**Operational signature of incipient stillness-collapse:**

- Increased alcohol intake to functionally-effective doses (well above normative — he is metabolizing constantly).
- Cigar consumption pattern shifts from social to solitary, indoor, late-night.
- Hours spent in his quarters with the lights off — the hyperacute eyes do not need them and the darkness reduces sensory load.
- Avoidance of the danger room / training spaces (because exertion brings him too close to the berserker ladder without an authorized target).
- Picking fights at the periphery — bar fights, calculated insubordinations toward Scott Summers or equivalent authority — to manufacture a structured antagonist.
- Calls or visits to one of the protected children, framed as checking in, functionally for the regulating effect of the role.

**Adversary leverage:** unusually low. Stillness-collapse is mostly an internal vulnerability. But adversaries who can *force prolonged isolation* on him (incarceration without combat, sensory deprivation, exile in safe environments) produce decompensation that opens him to subsequent recruitment, identity attack, or self-destructive behavior.

**Protector practice:**

- *Self-prescribed structure works.* Teaching posts, council seats, training rotations, the running of the school's groundskeeping or motor pool — give him role.
- *Do not insist on therapeutic stillness.* Conventional rest does not rest him.
- *Physical exertion with a partner he trusts* (sparring with Kurt, runs with Ororo, drinks with Ben Grimm, fishing trips with Steve Rogers) carries him through the stillness windows better than solitude or formal therapy.
- *Watch the protected-child check-in pattern.* Increased frequency without operational reason is a tell.

---

## 8. The Sabretooth Configuration — A Special Case

The annual "birthday" attempted-murder ritual with Victor Creed is, by duration and consistency, the most stable interpersonal relationship in his life. This is diagnostic of disorganized attachment (the predator as the only reliably present figure) and operationally significant: *the relationship organizes him.*

- **Sabretooth alive and active:** chronic destabilizer, intermittent acute crises, but the ritualized antagonism provides a predictable structure around which Logan has organized large parts of his identity. He knows who he is partly by knowing what Creed is.
- **Sabretooth removed (killed permanently, exiled, neutralized):** historically more destabilizing than his presence. The destruction of the predator removes a load-bearing wall in the architecture of the self. Documented across multiple arcs.
- **Sabretooth as ally** (rare, forced configurations): produces near-immediate dissociative pressure; he cannot metabolize the category violation.

**Protector practice:** do not engineer Sabretooth's permanent removal as a gift to Logan. Do not require him to ally with Creed except under operational necessity with short duration. Monitor him in any year in which the ritual is *missed* — the absence is itself a stressor.

---

## 9. Substance, Sleep, Sensory Load — The Somatic Baseline Levers

**Alcohol.** Self-medication, not recreation. Disrupting his access (Krakoan dry zones, mission profiles forbidding it) without substituting another affect-regulator produces irritability and sleep collapse within 72 hours. Allies should not moralize about it; the function it serves needs to be served by something. Sparring, structured solitude in wilderness, the Bushidō practice, and the mentorship role are the documented substitutes.

**Tobacco (cigars).** Ritual, oral, olfactory-baseline-setting (the cigar smoke masks the hyperacute olfactory channel, giving him a controllable scent floor — this is a sensory prosthesis, not just a habit). Removing it raises his ambient hypervigilance.

**Sleep.** Chronically poor. Best in: small enclosed spaces, slightly cold, with a door he can see and a weapon within reach; or, paradoxically, outdoors with weather (the sensory background of wind/rain/leaves provides a *coherent* sensory field that occupies the hyperacute channels and lets the higher cortex stand down). Worst in: institutional bedrooms, soft mattresses, climate-controlled silence (the silence is loud to him — he hears the building's electrical hum, the breathing of everyone on the floor).

**Sensory load.** Crowds, perfumed environments, hospitals, and modern open-plan offices are aversive at a level non-mutants do not register. Briefings and negotiations placed in such environments will go poorly through no fault of the content. Wood-paneled, small, low-light, low-electrical-noise rooms with one door produce his best cognitive performance.

---

## 10. The Persuasion Map — How to Reach Him

**Calming him.**

- Low, even voice. Drop pitch, slow tempo. Do not raise volume; he hears you fine.
- Physical posture: seated, hands visible, oblique angle (not directly facing — he reads frontal stance as challenge).
- Name what is happening if it is a flashback or identity event. Do not pretend it is not happening.
- Offer a route out that does not require public concession.
- If a protected child is present, ask the child to ask him. He will calm for the child when he will not calm for you.

**Persuading him.**

- *Concrete-specific over abstract.* "A girl in Madripoor, fourteen, Hand has her" works. "Geopolitical destabilization in Southeast Asia" does not.
- *One favor owed to a named person* outweighs ten policy arguments.
- *Show, do not tell.* Briefings with photographs, scents (a personal item of the endangered party), recorded voice. He decides via the sensory channel before the cognitive one.
- *Acknowledge the cost to him.* Do not pretend the mission is safe or clean. He distrusts handlers who underrepresent cost — Weapon X did, every operator since has.
- *Give him an exit clause.* Even a notional one. The choice-architecture matters to him beyond the actual exercise of the exit.

**Provoking him (only documented for completeness, never operationally recommended by this office).**

- Insult a protected child.
- Imply that Mariko / Itsu / Rose / Jean would be ashamed of his current conduct.
- Produce the scent of the Weapon X facility, of Hand operations, or of Creed.
- Suggest his memories are not his own — credibly.
- Restrain him without explanation, especially against his will, especially with hands behind him (the abduction posture is somatically encoded).

**Predicting him.**

- In a protected-child crisis: he will go, immediately, alone if necessary, by the most direct route.
- In a Sabretooth scent encounter: he will engage within seconds regardless of mission.
- In an identity-attack onset: he will hesitate, withdraw, seek a trusted peer if one is available, isolate if not.
- In a romantic-attachment phase past 8 weeks: anticipate withdrawal episode within the next month; pre-position prot


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*The positive ledger. A surveillance file built only on pathology miscounts the subject; what follows is the asset side, equally granular, because his durability is the dossier's central anomaly. He has been used as a weapon, drowned in his own skeleton, had his memory overwritten by four separate state and non-state actors, lost every primary love object, and yet at the close of every arc he is still operational, still moral, and still teaching someone younger than himself how to live. That outcome requires an asset inventory.*

---

## 1. SOMATIC ASSETS

**Healing factor — cellular regeneration at a rate exceeding any documented mutant baseline.** Closes lacerations in seconds, knits bone in minutes, regrows organ tissue and (in extremis) entire limbs and facial musculature (cf. *Wolverine* vol. 2 #145, post-Apocalypse vivisection; *Wolverine: Weapon X* #11). The asset is not merely survival — it is the *removal of injury as a coercive lever*. Torture cannot extract compliance from him by pain alone, because pain is recoverable; this has been demonstrated repeatedly under Hand, Hydra, and Weapon X. Operational consequence: he can be sent into environments (nuclear, immolation, vacuum-adjacent) from which no asset can be recovered, and recovered.

**Retarded biological aging.** ~130+ chronological years at apparent mid-40s phenotype. The asset is *longitudinal pattern recognition*: he has seen the same political configurations, the same human cruelties, the same recruitment pitches, three and four times across the 20th century. He recognizes a Hydra cell by smell and cadence within seconds because he fought their grandfathers. He recognizes a corrupt handler by the second sentence of the briefing.

**Adamantium skeleton.** Iatrogenic, traumatic in origin — but operationally an asset of the highest order. Skeletal fracture is functionally impossible; blunt-force trauma redistributes into surrounding soft tissue, which the factor repairs. The claws themselves are weapons that cannot be disarmed, cannot be confiscated at a checkpoint, cannot be detected by most conventional means until extruded, and that cut nearly any known material. The skeleton makes him a one-man boarding party against vehicles, structures, and armor classes that normally require a fire team.

**Hypersensoria.**
- *Olfaction:* discriminates individuals at distance, detects pheromonal markers of fear, arousal, illness, pregnancy, recent firearm discharge, alcohol metabolites, specific accelerants, and adrenaline cocktails. He has identified Sabretooth at a kilometer in wind and recognized Mystique through perfect visual disguise (*Uncanny X-Men* #173 and successors).
- *Audition:* heartbeat discrimination at room scale — he reads lies in pulse fluctuation, reads concealed weapons by safety-click and holster creak, reads the number of people in an adjacent room within seconds.
- *Vision:* low-light acuity sufficient for moonless tracking; motion sensitivity above human baseline.

The asset is *integrated threat-assessment at machine speed without machines* — he walks into a room and has, in under three seconds, a near-complete tactical map: count, armament, intent, health, recent activity, deception index. No briefing required.

**Recovery from sleep deprivation, malnutrition, dehydration, exposure.** Has lived feral in subarctic conditions across multiple decades without permanent decrement. Operational consequence: he requires no logistics tail.

---

## 2. CAPABILITIES — Trained and Acquired

**Combat repertoire (the broadest documented in canon).** Over a century of continuous practice across:
- Bushidō under Bando Saburo at Jasmine Falls (kenjutsu, iaijutsu, ken-zen ichinyo discipline; *Wolverine* limited series, 1982; later expansion in Aaron's *Wolverine and the X-Men*).
- Ninjutsu, sufficient that the Hand recruit him repeatedly and that Ogun can find no superior pupil (*Kitty Pryde and Wolverine*, 1984).
- Boxing, wrestling, knife fighting in early-20th-century mining camps and military service.
- Modern Western special-operations doctrine (Team X, CIA, Department H).
- Aerial and submarine combat familiarity from two world wars.
- CQB in confined urban environments (Madripoor, 1940s onward).

Few canonical opponents — Captain America, Shang-Chi, Iron Fist, Ogun — match him in any single discipline. Almost none match him across the whole spread.

**Languages.** Documented use of English, Japanese (fluent, including period dialects), Mandarin, Cantonese, Russian, German, French, Spanish, Lakota, and several Indigenous Canadian languages from his Yukon and Alberta periods. Operational consequence: he conducts his own intelligence work without translators, which is also a security asset.

**Tradecraft.** Surveillance, counter-surveillance, infiltration, exfiltration, document forgery (acquired in mercenary decades), tracking (both wilderness and urban), interrogation, escape and evasion. Cross-trained in multiple national doctrines, which means he reads opposing tradecraft as a native.

**Wilderness skills.** Survival, hunting, navigation, weather reading, tracking. He has lived as a wolf among wolves; he has lived as a man in mining camps; he can move between the two registers within an afternoon.

**Mechanical aptitude.** Motorcycle and small-aircraft maintenance (the bike is a recurring canonical fixture), small-arms armoring, basic explosives.

**Teaching capacity.** This is its own capability and gets a separate section below; noted here because it is *trained*, not innate — he has refined a pedagogical method across forty publication years of mentees.

---

## 3. PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSETS

**Affective courage.** He is afraid of very little externally, and he is unusually willing to face what he is afraid of internally — the memory recovery arcs, the Krakoan-era confrontations with Daken, the willing reentry into Weapon X facilities. Avoidance is a major defense for him, but *when he overrides it, he overrides it completely*. Few subjects with his trauma load are capable of the deliberate re-exposure he performs.

**Moral floor that cannot be eroded.** The single most operationally significant psychological asset. Across a century of brainwashing, memory overwrite, drug-state combat, and Apocalypse-tier ideological conversion, the floor reasserts: *children are not killed, the helpless are not killed, friends are not killed* — and when those rules have been violated through external control (Enemy of the State; the Mysterio incident), the recovery is total and the remorse is structural, not performative. The floor is recoverable because it is not a belief, it is a *somatic refusal*. This is rare in trauma populations and is the single feature that distinguishes him from the ASPD control case (Creed) sharing his etiology.

**Tactical present-tense cognition.** Whatever his autobiographical confusion, his *now* is exceptionally clear. Threat assessment, terrain reading, ally-state monitoring all run cleanly even when his memory is corrupted. He can lose who he is and still know what to do in the next four seconds. This is an unusual cognitive fractionation and it is what keeps him alive through identity crises that would functionally incapacitate most subjects.

**Humor as regulation.** Sardonic, dry, often self-deprecating. Functions as a real affect-regulator, not a defensive evasion only — he can puncture his own escalation with a one-liner and step back from the threshold. Documented across the entire Claremont run and persistent through Hama, Aaron, and Hickman. It is also a peer-bonding asset; teammates relax around him faster than his reputation predicts because of it.

**Pattern recognition over deep time.** A function of longevity plus combat exposure. He has seen this conspiracy before, this betrayal shape before, this kind of grief before. He is rarely surprised, and when he is, he updates fast.

**Capacity for stillness when chosen.** Bushidō practice, meditation, the Japanese-garden mode — when he opts into it, he can hold it. The asset is that he *has* a regulated mode at all, and that it is genuinely his, not borrowed. Most CPTSD subjects of his severity do not.

**Acceptance of his own death.** He has metabolized mortality more fully than nearly any character in canon. This is double-edged (the lifelong low-grade wish for an ending), but as an operational asset it produces total tactical fearlessness without recklessness toward others, and it removes the standard coercive lever of self-preservation. He cannot be held hostage to himself.

---

## 4. RELATIONAL ASSETS

**The network is enormous and unusually durable.** A partial map:

- *Xavier and the X-Men institutional family:* Ororo (peer, possibly his single most stabilizing adult friendship), Kurt Wagner (confessor figure, the man with whom his moral conversations are most candid), Scott Summers (rivalrous but operationally trusted), Hank McCoy, Rogue, Gambit, Bobby Drake. The network has survived multiple schisms and his own multiple departures.
- *The mentees, now adults:* Kitty Pryde, Jubilation Lee, Rogue, Armor (Hisako Ichiki), Laura Kinney, Gabby Kinney, Idie Okonkwo, Quentin Quire (asymmetric but real). Each of these would and has crossed continents for him. This is the asset he has built most deliberately.
- *Japan:* the Yashida network (residual), Yukio (intermittent, intense, durable across decades), Amiko Kobayashi (adopted daughter, Tokyo). He has standing in Tokyo's both legitimate and underworld registers.
- *Madripoor:* the Patch identity, Tyger Tiger, the Princess Bar — a fully functional alternative life with infrastructure, contacts, and cover.
- *Pre-X-Men allies still living or returnable:* Steve Rogers (mutual respect since WWII, operationally critical), Natasha Romanoff (1940s Madripoor onward), Carol Danvers, Nick Fury (transactional but functional), Maverick.
- *Canada:* residual Department H/Alpha Flight network, Heather Hudson (the post-Weapon X holding figure, durable affection).
- *Quiet Council / Krakoan-era institutional standing:* a seat at governance, which he uses primarily as protector function for the resurrected.

The pattern: he loses individual people catastrophically and often, but he does not lose *the structure of network*. He is unusually good at re-recruiting, and people stay loyal across his withdrawals.

**Reparative-parenting competency.** The X-23 relationship in particular demonstrates that the surrogate-paternal capacity, built initially as compensation, has matured into a *skill*. He is competent at it. He knows what adolescent survivors of engineered violence need (presence, training, low-pressure attachment, refusal to abandon, modeling of regulated adulthood) and he provides it consistently across multiple subjects across multiple decades. This is, frankly, one of the more accomplished long-form caregiving records in the published canon.

**Trust capital.** Xavier extended initial trust on minimal evidence and was repaid for decades. Rogers extends ongoing trust. The mentees extend trust. The capital exists because he has spent a century being, in the final reckoning, *reliable to the people he chooses* — through every dissociative episode, every exile, every memory overwrite, he comes back, and he comes back to *them*.

---

## 5. MATERIAL & INFRASTRUCTURAL ASSETS

**Wealth.** Howlett-family inheritance (longstanding); a century of accumulated assets through mercenary work, Madripoor operations, and shrewd longevity-enabled investment. He is not visibly wealthy because consumption is not a drive, but he is not resource-constrained.

**Safe houses and ground.** Cabins in the Canadian Rockies, properties in Madripoor, residual Japan footprint, the X-Mansion / Krakoa / Treehouse depending on era. He has unobserved ground on at least three continents.

**Documentation.** Multiple credible legal identities across jurisdictions, accumulated and maintained. He can cross borders without becoming visible.

**Institutional affiliations as needed.** Avengers, X-Men, X-Force, Alpha Flight (historical), Department H (historical), CIA (historical), SHIELD (transactional), Quiet Council. He can credential into nearly any operation he needs to enter.

**The bike, the cigars, the flannel, the bar.** Mentioned together because they function together: the personal infrastructure of decompression. Predictable rituals he can drop into anywhere — a roadhouse, a cigar, a long ride — that restore baseline. The portability of his regulation kit is itself an asset.

---

## 6. RESILIENCE FACTORS — Why the Container Holds

The dossier's central question: given the trauma load, why is he still operational? The factors, in interaction:

**(a) Physiology buys time for psychology.** The healing factor closes the somatic side of trauma loops faster than the psyche can compound them with secondary injury. Most CPTSD subjects accumulate medical sequelae (cardiovascular, autoimmune, somatic) that further erode regulation; he does not. The body keeps giving the mind another chance.

**(b) The Bushidō prosthesis is real.** It is not a costume. He genuinely studied, genuinely internalized, and genuinely practices a coherent ethical framework that gives him: a code when memory fails, a posture when affect fails, and a ritual structure for grief and killing both. The asset of having an *external* moral architecture is enormous for a subject whose *internal* narrative is corrupted. He cannot trust his memories; he can trust the form.

**(c) Reparative caregiving is bidirectionally restorative.** Mentoring Kitty, Jubilee, Laura, et al. is not merely altruism — it is the activity in which his attachment system functions cleanly, which means it is the activity in which he is most regulated and most himself. He has, in effect, prescribed himself the therapy he needed and delivered it to others. The arrangement keeps both ends alive.

**(d) Network redundancy.** Loss of any one figure is catastrophic but not terminal because the network is wide. Jean's deaths, Mariko's death, the periodic loss of friends — each is grief-bearing but he has other ground to stand on. Pure dyadic attachment would have destroyed him decades ago.

**(e) Humor and self-irony.** Discussed above; the regulator that prevents shame spirals from becoming terminal depressive episodes outside the *Old Man* extremity.

**(f) Acceptance of dissociation as a fact about himself.** He does not pretend the berserker state is not his. He owns it, mourns it, and works around it. The integration is partial but the *acknowledgment* is complete, which is itself a major dissociative-spectrum prognostic asset (per the Şar literature: subjects who recognize and name the dissociative process recover function faster than those who do not).

**(g) Meaning-making across the longest possible timeline.** He has lived long enough to see that he has, on balance, saved more than he has killed. He does not say this aloud. The math is nevertheless available to him, and operates beneath the self-stigma as a counterweight.

**(h) The structural protection of mission.** Being given something to do, especially something protective of a younger or weaker person, immediately organizes his entire system. Idleness decompensates him; mission integrates him. He has had near-continuous access to mission for a century, partly by luck of era and partly by self-recruitment.

**(i) Capacity to reset geography.** When the container cracks, he leaves — wilderness, Japan, Madripoor, a road. The exile is read as pathology in Section 3 and that is correct, but it is also an *effective* short-term regulator that prevents him from doing further harm during decompensation. The wilderness has saved him repeatedly. He knows it. He returns to it deliberately.

**(j) Ability to receive care.** Limited but real. He let Heather Hudson nurse him after Weapon X. He let Xavier recruit him. He lets Ororo see him unguarded. He lets Kurt hear his confessions. The capacity to accept holding from a few specific people, even rarely, is what differentiates him from terminal isolation cases with similar profiles.

---

## 7. WHAT MAKES THE ASSETS DURABLE

Each capability noted above is replicated in multiple modalities, which is the engineering signature of durability:

- *Regulation* is held by Bushidō practice **and** humor **and** alcohol **and** geographic flight **and** mentorship — five redundant systems, of which two are healthy, two are mixed, one is frankly maladaptive, but the redundancy means the regulator does not fail closed.
- *Identity* is held by code **and** network **and** mission **and** the body's continuity — when memory fails, the other three carry the load.
- *Combat capability* is held by multiple discipline-traditions, multiple weapon classes, and the body itself — disarmament does not disable him.
- *Network* is held across multiple continents, eras, and institutional affiliations — political collapse of any one does not isolate him.
- *Material base* is held across multiple jurisdictions and identities — sanction in one does not impoverish him.

The man is *engineered for survivability* — partly by enemies who wanted a weapon that would not break, partly by himself, building outward from the day in Alberta when his social father died at his biological father's hand and a child decided to become someone else. The enemies built the chassis. He built the rest. The rest is what makes him a person rather than a weapon, and it is the rest that the file's positive ledger is finally about.

---

*The synthesis with the prior sections: the pathology is severe and real; the asset stack is also severe and real; the two are not in tension but in equilibrium. He is not "despite" his trauma a capable adult, and not "because of" it either — he is the longitudinal product of a hundred and thirty years of building load-bearing structure on top of injury that never finished healing. The structure is the asset. The willingness, daily, to keep building it, is the resilience.*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*The container holds. This section maps, in operational detail, every documented and inferable way in which it has failed, the sequence of failure, the somatic and behavioral signature of each stage, and the environmental, sensory, and interpersonal conditions that reliably produce collapse. Six failure modes are distinguished. They are not mutually exclusive; in the worst recorded episodes (Weapon X escape, the Mariko killing, the *Enemy of the State* sequence, the *Old Man Logan* fifty-year shutdown, the *House of M* memory reintegration) two or three run in parallel.*

---

## 1. The Baseline — What "Holding" Looks Like

Before failure can be described, the operating baseline must be specified, because Logan's "holding" already sits at a level of activation that in a non-mutant would constitute clinical hyperarousal.

Resting state: heart rate trained low by decades of combat conditioning, but skin conductance and respiration cued to ambient threat data the rest of the room cannot perceive. He scans on entry to any room — doorways first, exits second, occupants in order of perceived threat. He sits where he can see the door. He does not turn his back to windows. Cigar lit within the first ninety seconds of any stationary period; alcohol within ten minutes of any social one. Speech is laconic, vowels swallowed, the rhythm of someone who has learned that fewer words leak less. Hands kept within forty centimeters of the dorsal-claw extrusion line — even folded across the chest, even holding a beer, the geometry is always combat-ready. He sleeps approximately four hours in two shifts and wakes at the wrong footstep on a stair three floors away.

That is *holding*. Decompensation is measured from there.

---

## 2. The Escalation Ladder — Stage by Stage

The progression from baseline to full berserker dissociation is consistent across writers from Claremont through Hama through Aaron. It runs in six stages, and the boundary between Stage 4 and Stage 5 is the boundary between Logan-as-agent and Logan-as-mechanism.

**Stage 0 — Quiet hypervigilance (baseline).** As above. The sensorium is on. He is tracking five conversations, two HVAC vents, and the smell of every person in the room.

**Stage 1 — Olfactory or auditory cue lands.** A specific scent (blood, Hand pheromone, Creed's spoor, the chemical signature of a Weapon X facility, Mariko's perfume on a stranger), a specific frequency (a child's distress at a distance only he can hear), or a specific verbal trigger ("the animal," "the program," "your memories"). Observable signs: a beat of stillness — the cigar pauses two centimeters from the lips, the glass stops mid-arc, the eyes go flat. He will say nothing for between three and twelve seconds. This pause is the single most reliable external indicator of the cascade beginning. Handlers who know him watch for it.

**Stage 2 — Verbal narrowing and sardonic warning.** Speech drops to monosyllables or to a small set of warning idioms ("don't," "back off, bub," "you really wanna do this?"). The humor that buffers his speech in baseline disappears entirely — the absence of the joke is the warning. Eye contact becomes continuous and unblinking. He turns his torso fully toward the threat source. The cigar comes out of the mouth and is held in the off-hand. Pupil dilation observable at conversational distance.

**Stage 3 — Claws as display.** *SNIKT.* One hand, then both. This is still under conscious control — many adversaries are dispatched, or back down, at this stage. The claws are extruded with their characteristic dorsal-hand laceration; trace blood at the extrusion sites is the somatic cost paid every time, a self-injury folded into the warning. He will often hold the position for several seconds, allowing the other party an exit. The fact that he *gives* this exit is diagnostic: he is still Logan.

**Stage 4 — Engaged combat, regulated.** Tactical, economical, lethal but proportionate. Targets are selected; bystanders are tracked and protected; non-lethal incapacitation is used where adequate. He talks during this stage — short imperatives, tactical communication with allies, occasionally taunts. Post-combat: he sheathes the claws, lights a cigar, makes a joke, walks away. *This is the ceiling of functional operation.* If the engagement ends here, no decompensation has occurred.

**Stage 5 — Threshold breach. Berserker dissociation.** Specific triggers cross the line: harm to a protected child; the smell of Sabretooth combined with the sight of a corpse; a Hand or Weapon X facility revealed mid-engagement; the murder, in front of him, of someone he loves; the discovery mid-fight that his own memories of the preceding hour are implanted. Observable transition: a sound — somewhere between a low growl and an exhalation — that is not a vocalization he produces in any other state. Eyes change focus; he is described repeatedly in the canon as no longer "seeing" the people in front of him. Speech stops. Combat technique *changes*: the regulated efficiency of Stage 4 is replaced by overkill — multiple stab wounds where one would suffice, decapitation and dismemberment of already-dead opponents, attacks continuing on bodies past the point of any tactical function. He will move through allies without recognition; *they have learned to clear the room.* Anterograde amnesia for the episode is partial-to-total: he comes back to himself with blood to the elbows and no continuous narrative for the preceding minutes-to-hours. This is the acute dissociative reaction (Şar 2014, 2022) — not an anger episode, an *altered state of consciousness* with motoric automatism.

**Stage 6 — Post-episode collapse.** The return is worse than the episode. He becomes physically still in a way he is never still otherwise — a flatness, not stoicism. He will look at his hands. He will, in the canon's most consistent post-berserker beat, ask someone present what he did, and how many. Then: withdrawal. Within hours: alcohol intake well above his usual heavy baseline, in solitude. Within days: geographic flight — the Canadian wilderness, a fishing cabin, a remote bar in a country where no one knows him. Within weeks: he reappears, says nothing about it, resumes operations. The episode is *encysted*, not processed. The next one is closer to the surface for it.

---

## 3. The Six Failure Modes

The Stage 0–6 ladder is the *acute* failure path. There are five other, more chronic or more catastrophic, modes of collapse.

### Mode A — Acute Berserker Dissociation (the ladder above)

Already specified. Duration: minutes to hours. Recovery: days to weeks of compensatory withdrawal. Frequency: episodic, threat-cued, lifelong. Triggers most reliable: harm to a child under his protection; the specific olfactory signature of Weapon X personnel or Hand operatives; the killing of a romantic intimate. Counter-indication that the ladder will *not* fully escalate: the presence of one specific protected person (Kitty Pryde in the canonical case, later Jubilee, Rogue, Laura) whose voice has been demonstrated, across multiple writers, to penetrate Stage 5 and recall him. This is the single most important operational fact about him: *a child's voice can reach where nothing else can.* It is also the lever every competent adversary has used.

### Mode B — Memory-Implant Destabilization (the cognitive collapse)

A different failure path entirely. Triggered when the autobiographical record is credibly attacked — either by an adversary revealing that a remembered episode is implanted (Romulus, the Professor, Apocalypse), or by recovered memory flooding back in a single event (*House of M*, when M-Day's collapse returns the unedited century to him at once).

Signature: not violence but *paralysis*. He sits down. He goes quiet for hours or days. He stares at middle distance. He drinks but does not eat. He cannot answer the question "what do you want to do" because the *I* the question presupposes has gone offline. The healing factor cannot help — there is no wound to close. This is the failure mode that most resembles classical major depressive episode, but the etiology is dissociative identity destabilization, not endogenous mood disorder.

Duration: variable, hours to months. Recovery: requires the slow re-stitching of a workable narrative, usually scaffolded by a trusted person (Xavier historically, Jean, Kurt, later Storm) who tolerates the silence and supplies, in low doses, the continuity he cannot supply for himself. *He cannot do this alone.* Solitary attempts to process a memory-implant event reliably escalate to Mode E (see below).

### Mode C — Compelled-Action Override (the will collapse)

Triggered when an external agent — Hand programming (*Enemy of the State*), Hydra conditioning, Apocalypse's Death recruitment, Persephone's kill triggers (*Return of Wolverine*) — successfully overrides his volition and uses his body to kill people he would otherwise protect.

This is the worst category of failure because *there is no acute episode he can post-hoc encyst.* The dissociation is total and externally maintained; he is conscious enough to register what he is doing and powerless to stop. When deprogramming finally lands, the integrated memory of those acts is delivered whole to a self that did not consent. Behavioral consequence: extended depressive shutdown of the *Old Man Logan* type, sometimes combined with active suicidality (which his physiology will not honor, which deepens the despair), and vows of nonviolence that hold until a child requires protection and Mode A reasserts.

The *Enemy of the State* recovery sequence is the canonical example: deprogramming → catatonic grief → operational re-engagement under a tightly disciplined revenge logic → completion of the revenge → return to baseline, with the episode now permanently in the load he carries. He does not "get over" Mode C events. They accumulate.

### Mode D — Sustained Behavioral Inhibition (the *Old Man Logan* shutdown)

The inverse decompensation. When the weapon-self is so contaminated — by Mode C events, by mass casualty among loved ones, by recognition that he himself has become the instrument of the harm he organizes his life around preventing — the entire violent register goes offline. He will not pop the claws. For years. He absorbs beatings without retaliation. He performs menial labor. He sleeps with his back to doors. He answers to a name (or no name) that does not invoke the history.

Observable signs: the cigar is gone (it was a combat-affiliated object). The drinking *decreases* (he is no longer regulating affect; affect itself has been suppressed). He becomes domestically present in a way he never is in baseline — but the presence is hollow, a performance of being a man who is not what he is. The stillness is not peace; it is structural depression with a vow stapled over it.

This mode is *more* dangerous than Mode A in one specific respect: the eventual trigger that ends it (in canon: the murder of his family) produces the largest single berserker episode in the record, because a half-century of suppressed Stage-5 material discharges at once. The shutdown is a pressure vessel, not a cure.

### Mode E — Solitary Decompensation (the wilderness cycle)

The chronic, low-grade failure mode that runs in the background of his entire life. Triggered by unstructured time, by peace, by the absence of a mission or a person to protect. He leaves. North, usually — Canadian Rockies, Yukon, Alaska — but functionally any wilderness will serve.

Stage progression within Mode E: (1) bar phase, two-to-six weeks, heavy drinking in a town small enough that the bartender learns his order and large enough that no one knows his name; (2) cabin phase, weeks to months, isolated structure, minimal supplies, no contact; (3) feral phase, the canon's recurrent and clinically significant beat — clothing minimized, language minimized, hunting for food, sleeping rough, the *Origin*-era animal life re-enacted. Hair and beard grow out. Hygiene degrades. He stops speaking aloud for days at a time. The sensorium that is a burden in cities becomes appropriate to the environment, and the relief of that fit is part of what makes the cycle self-reinforcing.

End condition: someone finds him (Hudsons, originally; later Xavier, Kitty, Nightcrawler), or a threat finds him, or news of a threat to a protected person reaches him. He returns abruptly, often violently, and resumes operations with no acknowledgment of the interval.

Mode E is the *least acute* and the *most diagnostic* failure — it is the one that reveals the structural fact that peace, for him, is aversive. He decompensates faster in stillness than in war. Every long-term arrangement of his life (the X-Mansion, the Jean Grey School, the Krakoan Quiet Council) has functioned, among other things, as a prophylaxis against Mode E.

### Mode F — Catastrophic Somatic Override (the physiology fails)

Rare but documented. When the healing factor is suppressed (Magneto's adamantium extraction, *X-Men* #25; the carbonadium poisoning by Lady Deathstrike's affiliates; the terminal sequence in *Death of Wolverine* where the factor is finally exhausted), the buffering between body and damage collapses. Adamantium toxicity becomes acute. Wounds persist. Pain — which he has felt continuously for a century but always with a known end — becomes open-ended.

Psychological consequence: not what one would predict. He does *not* decompensate behaviorally in this mode. He becomes, in the canon, *clearer* — more focused, more economical, more available to others. The *Death of Wolverine* sequence is conducted with a settled affect that is observable nowhere else in the record. The inference: a life-long unconscious wish for an ending that will stick (see §5 of the prior workup), surfacing as relief when the ending becomes possible. This is the single most important diagnostic fact about Mode F: *the somatic catastrophe stabilizes him.* It tells you what the chronic load actually costs.

---

## 4. The Conditions That Reliably Produce Collapse

Cross-referencing the modes against the canonical triggers yields a short list of environmental and interpersonal configurations that, in combination, predict decompensation with high reliability.

**The triadic trigger (Mode A, maximum severity).** (i) Olfactory cue from a known historical adversary, plus (ii) visual confirmation of harm to a protected child or romantic intimate, plus (iii) closed environment with no immediate tactical exit. Any two of these will escalate to Stage 5; all three produce the full berserker dissociation with anterograde amnesia. The Mariko poisoning, the Weapon X escape, the Hand attacks on the school — all match this signature.

**The memory-confrontation trigger (Mode B).** A credible source presents evidence that a load-bearing autobiographical episode is implanted or false. *Credible* is the operative word: he has been gaslit often enough that he resists casual claims. The destabilizer is documentation he cannot deny — a Weapon X file, a videotape, a recovered participant. *House of M*'s return of authentic memory is the inverse case (truth, not falsity) and produces the same paralysis, which confirms that the failure is in the act of *narrative re-sorting*, not in the content of any particular memory.

**The compelled-action trigger (Mode C).** Sufficiently sophisticated neurological/mystical override (Hand, Hydra, Apocalypse, Persephone). His resistance is high but not absolute; the modal failure point is approximately seventy-two hours of sustained conditioning, after which volitional control degrades. *Operational note: he is aware of this threshold, and standing protocols (across multiple eras) authorize allies to neutralize him if he is missing for more than that interval in known-hostile circumstances.* He has issued these protocols himself.

**The accumulated-guilt trigger (Mode D).** Not a single event but a load — a critical mass of Mode C residue plus a final catastrophic event he attributes to himself. *Old Man Logan*'s Mysterio sequence is the canonical example; the X-Men slaughter is the precipitant, but it lands on a century of prior load. Predicting Mode D requires tracking cumulative weight, not discrete incidents.

**The peace trigger (Mode E).** Three or more consecutive weeks without a defined operational role, without a person under his direct protection, and without a structured practice (Bushidō training, teaching, Quiet Council duties). The interaction with alcohol is bidirectional — drinking accelerates the slide into Mode E, and Mode E accelerates drinking. Disrupting either disrupts both.

**The somatic-finality trigger (Mode F).** Healing factor suppression by any mechanism. Behavioral response is paradoxically stabilizing in the short term, lethal in the long.

---

## 5. The Recovery Architecture — What Brings Him Back

Symmetrically, the conditions under which decompensation reverses are narrow and consistent.

From Mode A: the voice of a specific protected person, in the right register, at close enough range to be heard through the dissociative narrowing. Touch can work but is high-risk for the toucher. Distance helps; enclosed space hurts. Removal of the olfactory trigger (corpse removal, ventilation) measurably shortens the episode.

From Mode B: a trusted person, low verbal load, extended physical co-presence without demand for narrative. Xavier's historical method — sitting with him, supplying continuity in small doses, refusing to ask him to explain himself — is the canonical template. Demands for coherence prolong the mode. Silence shared with a witness shortens it.

From Mode C: deprogramming (technical or psionic), followed by a structured revenge object he can pursue with discipline. The revenge is not optional; it is the metabolic pathway through which the episode is processed. Attempts to bypass it produce Mode D.

From Mode D: a child in danger. Reliably. This is the canonical override, and it is morally complicated — the same mechanism that decompensates him in Mode A is what reanimates him from Mode D. He is a system built around the protection of the young, and that fact governs both his breaking and his returning.

From Mode E: physical retrieval by a trusted person, ideally one of the protected-young cohort now adult. The retrieval works because it reactivates the protector-attachment system that is the only consistent organizer of his behavior.

From Mode F: insufficient data — the sample is small and the outcomes vary. The pattern suggests that what he needs in Mode F is *permission* to let the ending be the ending. When that is denied (resurrection protocols, technological intervention), the gain of the mode is lost and the chronic load resumes.

---

## 6. The Structural Conclusion

The six failure modes are not six different disorders. They are six manifestations of the same underlying dissociative-spectrum CPTSD presentation (per Şar 2014, 2022), differentiated by which compensatory mechanism fails first under which load. Mode A is affect regulation failing under acute threat. Mode B is identity failing under cognitive assault. Mode C is volition failing under external conditioning. Mode D is the entire active register collapsing under guilt accumulation. Mode E is the protective-attachment scaffolding collapsing under its own absence. Mode F is the somatic buffer collapsing, and revealing what it has been buffering.

The container holds — across all six — because each mode has a recovery path, and because the protected-young attachment system functions as a master organizer that can be invoked from almost any state. Remove that system (kill the cohort, sever access, demonstrate that protection has failed) and the container does not hold; *Old Man Logan* is the proof of concept. Preserve it, and he can be brought back from anything short of Mode F.

This is the operational summary: he breaks in predictable ways, along predictable paths, in response to predictable conditions, and he returns through one predictable channel. A surveillance file built to *understand* rather than to *exploit* notes this symmetry and treats it not as a vulnerability to be leveraged but as the load-bearing structure of a person who, against considerable odds and at considerable cost, has remained one.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — SUBJECT: LOGAN

*Section 7 of the dossier. Forward-looking; probabilistic; built off the diachronic record in §1 and the diagnostic synthesis in §4–5. The methodological premise: a subject whose behavior has reproduced the same three-pattern signature (amnesia/identity confusion, dissociative berserker episodes, surrogate-paternal attachment to adolescent girls) across a hundred and thirty chronological years and roughly twenty-five principal writers is not going to suddenly break pattern absent an exogenous shock of comparable scale to Weapon X. The forecast therefore proceeds by mapping the existing attractors, identifying the live fork points, and specifying which inputs move him along which trajectory.*

---

## 1. The Baseline Forecast — What Continues Absent Intervention

Left to his own devices and reasonably likely external pressures, the subject continues the cycle that has organized his last several decades: a period of institutional embeddedness (Krakoan Quiet Council seat, X-Force black-ops, or some successor arrangement) lasting two to five years, terminated by an intolerable event — a protected adolescent harmed under his watch, a new memory-overwrite revealed, a peer killed by his hand under compulsion — followed by withdrawal (the Canadian bush, an alias in a Pacific Rim port, a stretch of bar work and silence), followed by recruitment back into the team by a crisis involving a child in danger. Period: roughly four to seven years per full cycle. He has run this loop, in identifiable form, at least six times since 1975. Probability of one more full iteration within the next decade of published time: very high. Probability that the next iteration is the last: low, absent the catalysts discussed below.

The baseline is *stable but degrading*. Each cycle leaves residue. The post-resurrection Logan is observably more brittle than the pre-*Death of Wolverine* Logan; the post-Persephone Logan is observably more guarded with his own perceptions than the post-*House of M* Logan. The healing factor restores the body; nothing restores the cumulative epistemic damage of repeatedly discovering one's memories are forgeries. The trend line for autobiographical confidence is downward, and the trend line for institutionalized identification (badge, team, Council seat as substitute for self-knowledge) is upward in compensation. That compensation is fragile: institutional identification is the precise weak point Hand/Hydra/Romulus exploit.

---

## 2. The Live Fork Points

Five discrete decision-architectures sit in his immediate forward path. Each is bistable; each will resolve within the next decade of published time; the resolution of any one will materially alter the others.

### 2.1 The Daughter Fork — X-23 and the Question of Completed Fatherhood

Laura Kinney is the only relationship in his biography that has not yet run the Rose/Itsu/Mariko termination. She is also the only person to whom he is, by any reasonable definition, a *competent* father — neither absent (Daken), nor pre-emptively withdrawn (Jubilee, Kitty, Rogue all grew past him), nor terminated by his own claws. The fork: does he allow this relationship to become the first sustained adult-to-adult kinship he has ever maintained, or does he, as the template predicts, manufacture distance the moment Laura's adulthood deprives him of the protector role that licenses his attachment?

**Growth path:** he survives the transition from protector to peer. This is the single most therapeutically significant event available to him, because it would be the first piece of evidence in his own life that the *prediction "she will die because of me"* can be falsified by a person remaining alive and intact across decades in his close orbit. Falsifying that prediction is the only thing that loosens the avoidant-romantic pattern.

**Catastrophe path:** Laura is killed, or — far worse for his psychology — killed *by him* under compulsion. The Hand, Orchis-successor entities, or any actor with access to Weapon X-derived conditioning could engineer this; it is the obvious move against him and he knows it, which is itself a destabilizer. If this fork resolves catastrophically, expect a *Old Man Logan*-class shutdown lasting years, with elevated risk of a true terminal attempt (see §4).

### 2.2 The Sabretooth Fork — Termination of the Stable Hostile Pair-Bond

Creed is, per the diagnostic, the most behaviorally reliable figure in Logan's life. Their "birthday" ritual has structured a century. Two terminations are live: Creed dies permanently (resurrection protocols denied, true death achieved); or Creed is *redeemed*, integrated, made into something other than the predator. Either outcome removes the chronic destabilizer that is also, paradoxically, a chronic *organizer*.

Counterintuitive forecast: Creed's removal is more dangerous to Logan than Creed's continued presence. The hostile pair-bond is load-bearing. Without Creed as the fixed pole of "what I am not, even at my worst," Logan loses one of his three principal identity-anchors (the others being the samurai ideal and the protector-of-the-young role). Expect a six-to-eighteen-month period of marked identity diffusion following any permanent Creed resolution, with elevated berserker-episode frequency as the dissociative system searches for a new container.

### 2.3 The Memory Fork — The Final Reckoning with the Implanted Autobiography

He has now had multiple "complete memory restorations" (*House of M* being the canonical instance) and each has been revealed, subsequently, as itself partial or corrupted. The forward question is no longer *will his memories return* — they have, repeatedly — but *will he stop expecting them to be authoritative when they do*. The mature adaptation is the abandonment of the recovery project: accepting that his autobiography is permanently a working draft and that identity must be constituted from present commitments rather than verified past. Some of his post-Krakoan behavior (treating the resurrection-backup self as one self among possible selves) suggests early movement in this direction.

**Growth path:** he completes the transition from *memory-as-identity* to *commitments-as-identity*. This is the same move trauma-informed clinicians work toward with severe dissociative patients: identity is what you do next, not what you can verify happened. If he makes this move, the Romulus/Persephone/Hand class of attacks loses most of its leverage on him — you can no longer destabilize a man by revealing his memories are false if he has stopped requiring them to be true.

**Catastrophe path:** a new revelation — a child he didn't know he had, an atrocity he doesn't remember committing, a primary loyalty (Xavier, Jean) shown to have been implanted — at a moment when his current institutional supports are already weakened. The combination is the kill-shot psychology, and adversaries who have studied him know it.

### 2.4 The Institution Fork — Krakoa, Its Successors, and the Politics of Belonging

For the first time in his life he has held formal political office (Quiet Council). The role is a poor fit — he is constitutionally insubordinate, allergic to procedure, and the seat requires him to authorize violence in a juridical rather than tactical register, which engages his shame ledger differently than combat does. He has handled it with the predictable mixture of grim competence and quiet self-disgust. The fork: does the next institutional iteration (whatever succeeds Krakoa in published continuity) place him in a role that *uses* his actual capacities (mentor, field operator, executioner-of-last-resort with sanction) or one that *misuses* him as a symbol or a vote?

Misuse — being made a figurehead, a moral mascot, a name on a council where his actual judgment is not wanted — produces decompensation faster than combat does. He decompensates in peace, as established; he decompensates faster in *performative* peace. Watch for: increased alcohol intake, lengthened absences with thin operational justification, picked fights with peers (Cyclops being the historic outlet) that read as displacement.

### 2.5 The Mortality Fork — The Resurrection Question

The Krakoan resurrection protocols, and whatever survives them, change the meaning of death for him in a way the healing factor alone never did. The healing factor produced reckless body-use; institutionalized resurrection produces something more corrosive — *the loss of death as an available exit*. The lifelong low-grade wish for an ending that will stick (see §5 of the workup) was structurally tolerable because death remained, in principle, available. If resurrection becomes reliably non-optional — if the backups exist and will be run regardless of his consent — a quiet but significant psychological tether is cut.

**Growth path:** he negotiates explicit terms with the resurrection apparatus (a true opt-out, a sunset clause, conditions under which he is not brought back) and thereby reclaims agency over his own ending. This is, in trauma terms, a reclamation of bodily sovereignty from a system that wants to use his body — structurally identical to escaping Weapon X, and therefore deeply restorative if achieved.

**Catastrophe path:** he is resurrected against his will, or repeatedly, or with the sort of memory-fidelity drift that the Krakoan protocols have already shown is possible.
